# 太平御览道部

*The Imperial Reader of the Taiping Era*
**Title:** *Taiping Shilang* (Comprehensive Survey of the Taiping Era)
**Section:** Daoist Canon
Compiled by Li Fang et al. under imperial commission during the Song Dynasty
Twenty-one fascicles

**Source of Base Text:**
The original work comprises one thousand fascicles. Fascicles 659 through 679 constitute the Daoist Canon, totaling twenty-one fascicles. The *Zhengtong Daoist Canon* (Orthodox Unity, First Section) originally transcribed three fascicles (674–676). The present edition is collated from the full text of the Daoist Canon in the Song-dynasty photographic reproduction.

**Collated Edition:** *Zhengtong Daoist Canon*

**Daoist Canon I**   The Dao/Way

The *Laozi* states:
The Dao/Way that can be spoken is not the eternal Dao/Way—its wondrous subtlety lies in utmost emptiness.
Nameless, it is the origin of heaven and earth; named, it is the mother of the myriad things.
The nameless is the mystery’s root. The Dao/Way is empty, yet its use is inexhaustible.
Profound, it seems the ancestor of all things.
Between heaven and earth, does it not resemble a great bellows?
The gate of the mysterious female is called the root of heaven and earth.
Heaven and earth endure long because they do not live for themselves—thus they attain long life.
They give life without possessing, act without relying, lead without dominating: this is called profound virtue/power.
Holding to the ancient Dao/Way, one governs present existence.
To know the ancient beginning is called the thread of the Dao/Way.
When the myriad things arise, I observe their return.
Affairs accomplished, tasks complete, the common people all say, “We are naturally so.”
Cut off sageliness, abandon wisdom, and the people benefit a hundredfold.
The bearing of great virtue/power follows only the Dao/Way.
By surveying the many beginnings, how do I know the nature of the many beginnings?
That which bends is preserved whole—this means bending oneself to respond to affairs preserves wholeness.
That which is crooked becomes straight—this means yielding oneself to advance others achieves straightness.
That which is hollow becomes full—this means holding to humility ensures constant fullness.
That which is worn becomes new—this means guarding simplicity and frugality brings daily renewal.
Having little ensures attainment—this means embracing the One without deviation incurs no loss.
Having much leads to confusion—this means pursuing many paths brings disorder.
Therefore, the sage embraces the One as the model for the world.
“Rare words are natural”—this means that through words one awakens to the Dao/Way without clinging to words, aligning with nature.
There is a thing formed in chaos, born before heaven and earth.
Silent! Vast! It stands alone and does not change, circulates without cease.
I know not its name; I style it “Dao/Way,” and by force call it “Great.”
Within the realm, there are four greats, and the ruler occupies one.
This means the ruler is the master of human spirit, upon whom the rise and fall of the myriad things depend.
Humans emulate earth, earth emulates heaven, heaven emulates the Dao/Way, and the Dao/Way emulates spontaneity.
Gravity is the root of lightness; stillness is the lord of restlessness.
“Good traveling leaves no tracks”—this means embodying true nature, one’s actions leave no traces, and the heart accords with the Dao/Way.
“Good words leave no flaws”—this means transcending forms to seek meaning, where principle is realized and the heart forgotten.
“Good reckoning requires no tally”—this means unifying all with the One without generating other views.
“Good closure needs no bolts yet cannot be opened”—this means the heart is free from the delusion of chasing phenomena, and phenomena are free from the burden of arousing the heart.
“Good binding needs no cords yet cannot be undone”—this means the heart merges with the Dao/Way; though unbound, it cannot be untied.
Thus, the sage is always good at saving people, so none are abandoned.
Always good at saving things, so none are discarded—this is called inheriting illumination.
Know the masculine, yet keep to the feminine;
know the white, yet keep to the black;
know the honorable, yet keep to the humble.
This means that containing virtue/power within, one returns to simplicity; with constant virtue/power in use, one scatters to become vessels.
Once entering forms and vessels, there must be refinement and coarseness.
The sage employs them as the chief of all materials.
Thus, great governance does not sever—this means the sage uses the Dao/Way to govern the multitude without harming their natural state.
The Dao/Way in the world is like valleys to rivers and seas.
“Those who die yet do not perish are long-lived”—this means death is the end of physical principle, while perishing is premature fate. Longevity is the fulfillment of one’s allotted span. Those who know contentment and act with effort attain heaven’s constancy. To die without perishing is to fulfill one’s allotted span—this is called longevity.
Grasping the great image, the world comes.
Coming without harm, it rests in great peace.

When transformation stirs with desire, I shall pacify it with the Unnamed Unhewn—this refers to the Dao/Way.

Lose the Dao/Way, then virtue/power follows;
Lose virtue/power, then benevolence follows;
Lose benevolence, then righteousness follows;
Lose righteousness, then ritual follows.

All things under heaven are born of being,
Being is born of non-being.

Luminous virtue/power appears dim;
Advancing the Dao/Way seems like retreat;
The level Dao/Way resembles unevenness.

Supreme virtue/power is like a valley—this means emptiness that embraces all things.
Great purity seems tarnished—this means the capacity to remain immaculate while containing impurity.
Vast virtue/power seems insufficient—this means great accomplishment that holds to humility.
Established virtue/power seems unstable—this means achieving merit without self-display.
Embodied reality seems mutable—this means purity and unity that harmonizes with radiance.

The great square has no corners—this means no petty adherence to sharp angles.
The great vessel is slow to complete—this means no pursuit of quick results.
The great tone is scarcely heard—this means no adornment with trivial sounds.
The great image has no form—this means responsiveness to all things.

The Dao/Way lies hidden, without name—this means its function remains unmanifest.

The Dao/Way generates the One,
The One generates the Two,
The Two generate the Three,
The Three generate the myriad things.
The myriad things bear yin and embrace yang,
Blending qi to achieve harmony.

In practicing the Dao/Way, daily diminish—
Diminish and further diminish,
Until reaching non-action.

Thus, block the apertures, close the gates,
And to the end of life, one will not toil—
This means not indulging the six senses’ delights,
So the gate of misfortune closes,
And one remains untroubled to life’s end.

Open the apertures, aid one’s affairs,
And to the end of life, one cannot be saved—
This means opening the senses to fulfill desires,
Thus inviting misfortune that cannot be remedied.

To avoid bringing calamity upon oneself is called following constancy—
This means not incurring personal disaster,
And thus secretly employing the true, constant Dao/Way.

It is also said:
The knowing do not speak;
The speaking do not know.

Speech exists to convey meaning through sound,
Like one who knows music—
Recognizing tones through strings,
The heart knows the sound,
Yet the mouth cannot transmit it.
Those who deeply comprehend the subtle and wondrous do not speak.

The highest say: The knowing do not speak;
Those who speak do so to rescue others.

It is further said:
The superior person studies the Dao/Way, receiving it with spirit;
The middling person receives it with the heart;
The inferior person receives it with the ears.

Those who listen with spirit penetrate the formless;
Those who listen with the heart know inner conditions;
Those who listen with the ears hear external sounds.

It is also said:
The knowing do not speak;
The speaking do not know.
Thus the sage declares:
I practice non-action, and the people transform themselves;
I have no affairs, and the people enrich themselves;
I love stillness, and the people rectify themselves;
I have no desires, and the people return to simplicity.

Cultivate it in oneself, and the world transforms itself—
This is the Dao/Way of deep roots and firm stems, of long life and enduring vision.

When the Dao/Way governs the world,
Its spirits do not act as gods.
The Dao/Way is the mystery of the myriad things;
To act is to ruin it,
To grasp is to lose it.
Therefore the sage practices non-action and so does not fail,
Holds to nothing and so does not lose.

The *Scripture of the Supreme* states:
The chaotic qi transforms into perfected beings,
Soaring with the times,
Possessing names yet no forms.

The *Scripture of Immortals* states:
Divine immortals ascend lightly—these are celestial immortals,
Ranked in the Great Clarity,
Their names recorded in secret registers.

The *Scripture of Esoteric Essentials* states:
The grotto-palaces of the Five Marchmounts—
In an instant, one becomes an earthbound immortal,
Preserving spirit and form,
Far from care and calamity.

It is also said:
The Nine Palaces of the Great Clarity all have officials—
The highest are called the Grand August, the Purple August, the Jade August;
Collectively, the highest are called Lords of the Great Dao/Way,
Next are Perfected Ones and Perfected Ministers;
Among them are Censors.

Whenever called "Supreme," it denotes the honor of a single palace—
Virtue/power so lofty it has no flaw,
Thus it is called "Supreme."

It is further said:
The immortal is a river;
The body is a boat.

To cross the river and reach the shore—why rely on a boat?

The *Statutes of the Grand Perfection* states:
The *Jade Emperor’s Register* contains one hundred and eight Lords of the Dao/Way,
Where herb-gathering immortals are appointed according to their karma.

The Three Good Paths are the sagely, the perfected, and the immortal.
The highest rank is called sagely,
The middle rank is called perfected,
The lowest rank is called immortal.
Between the Three Clarities, each has its proper station.
The sagely ascend to the Jade Clarity,
The perfected ascend to the Highest Clarity,
The immortals ascend to the Great Clarity.
In the Jade Clarity are the palaces of the Great Emperor,
Where emperors, kings, dukes, ministers, officials, and commoners are all addressed as "sagely"—
Such as Sagely August or Sagely Emperor.
Men and women, noble and base, each has its hierarchy.
In the Highest Clarity are the Dark Capital, Jade Capital, Seven Treasures, and Purple Tenuity,
All addressed as "perfected."
In the Great Clarity is the Palace of the Great Ultimate,
All addressed as "immortal."
The ranks and hierarchies of the Highest Clarity and Great Clarity,
Including the order of men and women,
Are the same as those of the Jade Clarity.

The *Scripture of the Great Grotto* states:
From life one attains the Dao/Way,
From the Dao/Way one attains immortality,
From immortality one attains perfection,
From perfection one becomes a Lord of the Highest Clarity.

The *Scripture of the Five Talismans* states:
The *Twenty-Four Perfected Charts*—
The numinous treasures of the Five Marchmounts.
Whoever obtains them will surely ascend as an immortal,
Striding through the Great Clarity.
To obtain the methods of the Dao/Way, first bathe and cleanse away filth,
Then acquire the *Eastern Well Chart*.
To stabilize the Five Emperors and command mountain spirits,
Acquire the *Marchmount Chart*.
To commune with divine spirits and master immortal arts,
Acquire the *Eight Histories True Forms Chart*.
To master the Five Phases’ kitchens,
Acquire the *Six Jia Spirit-Communion Chart*.
To preserve one’s body and summon celestial spirits,
Acquire the *Nine Palaces Purple Chamber Chart*.
To uphold the methods of the Dao/Way,
Acquire the *Great Clarity Chart*.
To follow the Dao/Way in accord,
Acquire the *Chaos-Unity Chart*.
To comprehend the workings of the Dao/Way,
Acquire the *Western Ascent Preservation Record Chart*.
To master transformations,
Acquire the *Numinous Transformation Chart*.
To tread the Great Dao/Way,
Acquire the *Nine Heavens Chart*.
To shed one’s bodily form,
Acquire the *Nine Transformations Chart*.
To conceal and preserve the spirits guarding the body,
Acquire the *Nurturing the Body Chart*.
To stabilize the body and guard the numinous treasure,
Acquire the *Embracing the Shadow Chart*.
To cultivate tranquility and preserve unity for the body’s sake,
Acquire the *Nurturing the Body Chart*.
To nurture the will in stillness,
Acquire the *Sincerity and Will-Preservation Chart*.
To attain purity and whiteness, summoning the mushroom spirits,
Acquire the *Mushroom Spirit Jade Maiden Chart*.
To command the Six Dings,
Acquire the *Six Yin Jade Maiden Chart*.
To attain the immortal register,
Acquire the *Nine-Nine Daoist Immortal Chart*.
To ingest the qi of the Dao/Way,
Acquire the *Guiding and Pulling Chart*.
To govern the arts of the Dao/Way,
Acquire the *Grotto’s August Treasure Chart*.
To perform transformations,
Acquire the *Reclining Breath Chart*.
To refine the Nine Elixirs and Golden Liquor before the furnace,
Acquire the *Great One Chart*.
To ascend the Five Marchmounts in search of divine mushroom herbs,
Acquire the *Mountain-Opening Mushroom Herb Chart*.
To preserve spirit and form, distinguishing deviant spirits,
Acquire the *Bright Mirror Chart*.

The *Scripture of the Highest Clarity* states:
The qi that is guarded follows where the spirit is born.
Where the spirit abides, qi abides;
Where the spirit departs, qi departs.
When qi scatters, it becomes clouds and mist;
When it coalesces, it becomes form and shadow.
Emerging, it becomes an immortal;
Transforming and entering, it becomes the True One.
Above, it binds the Three Origins;
Below, it binds the myriad things.
In stillness, it serves as the omen of the body;
In motion, it serves as the omen of the spirit.

The *Scripture of the Grotto Perfection* states:
Whoever reads the *Hidden Book of the Great Elixir and Grotto Perfection*,
Able to study it with precision and insight,
And through resonance comprehends the profound,
With clouds returning to release the primal darkness and savor the radiance of the Great Clarity,
Is fit to be a Master of the Mysterious Center.

Ge Hong’s *Biographies of Divine Immortals* states:
From Fuxi to the Three Dynasties,
Illustrious Daoist masters appeared in every generation.
Laozi, in particular, attained the Dao/Way with exceptional refinement.
Inwardly, he embodied spontaneity;
To rightly determine the root and branches,
One should rely on historical records,
Along with scriptures of immortals and esoteric texts for mutual verification.
Other popular accounts are largely false and deceptive,
Later Daoists having privately added to them—
These are not authentic texts.
He composed the *Virtue/Power of the Dao/Way* in two scrolls,
And Yin Xi practiced his teachings.
By the Han, Empress Dou favored the words of the Yellow Emperor and Laozi,
And Emperor Wen along with the Dou clan’s relatives were all ordered to study them.
Thus, Zhuang Zhou and his followers took Laozi as their patriarch.

The *Scripture of the Grand One Perfected of the Great Unity* states:
All lofty perfected immortals have masters,
Who transmit the *Three Caverns’ Treasured Scriptures of the Highest Clarity*.
Without a master, the Dao/Way cannot be accomplished—
How then could one ride the Eight Radiance Dragon Chariot?
How could one ascend the Great Ultimate and Jade Towers?
In learning the Dao/Way of the Highest Clarity,
How could one achieve flight in the flesh?
If one is negligent toward the master’s path,
One loses even a night-shining pearl.
Thus, the Dao/Way is inherently difficult to know;
Even sages and worthies revere their masters,
For this is how the Dao/Way endures.

The *Luminous Writ of the Great Empyrean* states:
Heaven and earth spread qi—
The truth of the master’s teaching.
Perfected immortals ascend to sageliness—
Without a master, none succeed.
The heart cannot be its own master;
To take the heart as master is to court failure.

The *Scripture of the Treasure Mystery* states:
To restrain partiality and deviation,
One must return to the central and correct.
Able to reach the flowing end,
One returns to the original source.
The Dao/Way is fundamentally formless,
Yet through words, images are established.
Though spoken of as emptiness in use,
In truth, it is without substance.

The *Canon of the Dao/Way* states:
To regulate killing and life is Heaven’s role;
To follow nature and destiny is humanity’s.
Those who do not oppose Heaven do not kill;
Those who do not oppose humanity do not attack.
To govern thus is the ultimate of the Dao/Way.

The *Records of the Seven Sages* states:
The Red Lord of the Southern Marchmount descended to teach,
Transforming his traces to become a Daoist,
And with six disciples, all revealed their names.

The *Scripture of the Lord Emperor of the Great One* states:
Those who seek the Dao/Way must rectify their hearts—
Then even Heaven and Earth cannot oppose them.

Those who abandon the burdens of sensual desire without a backward glance, shun glory and profit to distance themselves, willingly endure cold and hardship to preserve contemplation, and delight in quiet retreat behind hidden walls—only then may one speak of learning the Dao/Way.

The *Scripture of the Three and Five in Harmonious Motion* states:
Heaven is the manifested form of the Dao/Way.
Its responses unfold gradually,
Guided by interaction.
Among the mysterious symbols and empty patterns,
None surpass the Three and Five.
When the Three and Five move in harmonious sequence,
Their revolutions are inexhaustible,
And the Three Powers align in perfect measure.
The Great One is Heaven.
Heaven receives the singular qi,
Vast and clear in its purity.
The Dao/Way is the accumulation of Heaven’s numinous power.

The *Scripture of Ascending Mystery* states:
The profound subtlety of the Dao/Way arises from spontaneity,
Born from the unborn,
Preceding what precedes all else.
It pervades beyond all bounds,
Dispersing spirit and transforming qi,
Serene and without superior,
Governing and guiding all heavens.

The *Inner Chapters of the Mysterious and Wondrous* states:
The Great Dao/Way arises from non-action,
And is the ancestor of the ten thousand things.

The *Scripture of the Orthodox Unity Perfected* states:
The purity and truth of the Dao/Way cannot be conveyed by words.
Words are but a means to express meaning.
Through the establishment of the Mysterious Capital,
The transformation of Orthodox Unity draws near to truth.

The *Scripture of the Treasured Mystery* states:
Rectitude aligns with the Dao/Way;
Alignment gives voice to aspiration.
Aspiration and speech reside in rectitude,
And rectitude severs all deviation.
Through fasting, purification, and the recitation of scriptures,
The Dao/Way of immortality naturally manifests.
The greatest attainment of immortality lies with the Most High.
The Most High speaks not,
Yet words respond to resonance.
This resonant response is the way of trust,
Manifesting as scripture.

The *Scripture of the Three Sovereigns* states:
Seek the natural,
Liberate the self to stand in the Dao/Way.
The Three Luminaries shine forth,
And Heaven and Earth remain constant.

The *Scripture of Wisdom* states:
Speak to a ruler, and wisdom benefits the state;
Speak to a father, and kindness extends to the child;
Speak to a teacher, and love embraces the multitude;
Speak to an elder brother, and fraternal conduct prevails;
Speak to a minister, and loyalty serves the sovereign;
Speak to a child, and filial piety honors the parents;
Speak to a friend, and trust strengthens the bond;
Speak to a wife, and devotion is given to the husband;
Speak to a husband, and harmony fills the household;
Speak to a younger brother, and reverence upholds propriety;
Speak to a farmer, and diligence is encouraged in tilling the land;
Speak to a Daoist, and the discourse halts at the Dao/Way;
Speak to a foreigner, and each guards their own domain;
Speak to a servant, and caution guides their service.

The *Scripture of the Most High* states:
Draw near to the wise and learned,
And broadly inquire into the good Dao/Way.
In the discussions of the worthy,
One must not cling stubbornly to a single view.
It further states:
In the latter age, how should Daoists conduct the rituals when expounding scriptures and teaching the Dharma?
If expounding the *Five Thousand Characters*,
Follow the rites of the *Numinous Treasure*.

The *Three Caverns Treasured Scripture* states:
A single master of the Three Caverns who transmits the Dharma to save the world
Surpasses a thousand yellow-robed Daoists.
It further states:
On Great Mount Mao stands a bronze and iron cauldron,
Capable of holding four or five *hu*,
Exquisitely and finely wrought.
It rests at the mountain’s highest point,
Buried eight *chi* deep in the earth,
Covered by a slab of stone.
On auspicious days,
Daoists from near and far ascend the mountain to behold it,
Where no grass or trees remain.
They pile stones to form a small altar.
Once, a small tiled hut stood there,
But it was toppled by the wind.
Its two handles represent the sun and moon;
Its three legs represent the Three Powers.
Forged from the bronze of Feather Mountain,
It appears and vanishes through divine transformation.

The *Declarations of the Perfected* states:
To the southwest of Great Mount Mao lies Four-Flat Mountain,
Commonly called Square Mountain.
Beneath it is a grotto chamber,
Named Square Terrace.
The grotto has two entrances visible on the mountain’s exterior,
Connecting to Huayang,
And is called the Secluded Abode of the Separate Realm.
Those who attain the Dao/Way dwell there.
It further states:
Cultivate the self,
And one’s virtue/power becomes true.
The noble person establishes the self,
Taking morality and the Dao/Way as their duty,
Purity and stillness as their teacher,
Great Harmony as their friend,
Mystery as their silence.
With the Dao/Way, they exhaust the ultimate,
Govern the root,
And seek what precedes all signs.
Those who do good reward themselves;
Those who do evil punish themselves.
Thus, without contention, there is nothing they cannot overcome;
Without speech, there is nothing to which they do not respond.
It further states:
Those who study the Dao/Way with utmost sincerity
Should transmit the Dao/Way to learners.
Master Fei said:
My teacher, the Red Pine Master of the Southern Marchmount,
Is the Perfected of the Great Void.
Formerly, the Most High instructed Laozi in virtue/power to attain the Dao/Way;
The Red Pine Master transmitted the Dao/Way to me, and I attained immortality.
It further states:
The ten superior trials of the immortal path must all be passed
Before transmission is granted.
These twelve matters constitute the great trial,
All overseen by the Perfected of the Great Ultimate.
How can one not be cautious?
Formerly, Qingwu the Elder, disciple of Pengzu,
Received the teachings of an enlightened master
And mastered the wondrous principles of immortality.
He entered Mount Huayin to study the Dao/Way.
After twelve trials over the years,
Three remained unpassed.
Later, he ingested golden fluid and ascended to the Great Ultimate.
The Lord of the Dao/Way deemed him to have failed three trials,
Thus, he was but an immortal,
Not a Perfected.

It further states:
Master Fei said that learners of the Dao/Way face nine perils.
If one examines them carefully,
Immortality is not far off.
The perils are:
Having aspiration but no opportunity,
Having opportunity but no companions,
Having companions but no aspiration,
Having aspiration but not meeting a teacher,
Meeting a teacher but not learning,
Learning from a teacher but not diligently,
Diligently practicing but not upholding the Dao/Way,
Or having an unsteady aspiration.
With wholehearted devotion,
One need not rely on companions to succeed,
Nor await resonance to act—
This is the broad essential of learning immortality.
If the teacher is burdened by sorrow,
The disciple’s comings and goings lack goodness.
Without a teacher, learning the Dao/Way will not succeed.
With the heart fixed and the eyes visualizing,
One sees the teacher as scripture.
What is not transmitted by the teacher
Must not be taught to others,
Lest it confuse later learners.
Thus, one must not seek the Dharma without transmission.

When serving a teacher,
Do not choose based on nobility or baseness,
Nor doubt age or youth.
To say, “I am older while they are younger,”
Or, “They are base while I am noble,”
Is to fail to grasp the essential equality of true orthodoxy.
Among people, none are noble or base—
Those with the Dao/Way are revered.
As the saying goes:
An elder need not be advanced in years;
What matters is broad knowledge and deep insight to be a teacher.
One must not say,
“They studied after me,
How can they now reverse and become my teacher?”
Those who harbor such thoughts
Are not learners of the Dao/Way.
One should humbly yield,
Cede ability,
And defer to virtue,
Following only what is good.
One must not insist on being right while others are wrong.

To attain the Dao/Way and deliver the world, none succeed without a teacher. Learning with a teacher is like a tree having roots. When great wisdom is achieved, it can then cultivate lesser wisdom—just as a tree’s roots produce seeds, and those seeds in turn grow roots, generation after generation, ensuring the species endures. Following a teacher transforms the Dao/Way; when one’s Dao/Way surpasses the teacher’s, one returns to instruct the teacher. This is what is meant by “the Dao/Way is noble, the person is base”—the principle is thus.

All former teachers must be revered and distinguished. Why? The root teacher is the foundation of learning, like a mountain: each basket of soil gradually builds its height. The root teacher is the starting point of enlightenment, while later teachers bring completion. It is like fine attire and adornments—all matters settled, yet without the final crowning, one cannot conduct human affairs. To harbor disdainful thoughts is to misunderstand: in discourse and instruction, the teacher serves as a model for others. If the teacher does not embody the Dao/Way, how can they resolve doubts?

In ancient times, when sages and worthies pursued learning, finding the right teacher was called “rebirth.” Without the right teacher, it was called “confusing the scriptures.” Without a teacher, the Dao/Way does not arise spontaneously. *The Scripture of Great Peace* states: The superior person studies the Dao/Way to assist the emperor’s virtue of cherishing life. The middling person studies the Dao/Way to deliver their family. The inferior person studies the Dao/Way merely to liberate themselves.

It also says: Speaking obstructs the Dao/Way’s completion; excessive speech brings harm. Silence ensures ten thousand years without misfortune. It further states: With a good teacher, even the lowly and common may become virtuous. Virtue, unceasing, leads to worthiness; worthiness, unceasing, leads to sageliness; sageliness, unceasing, leads to profound knowledge of the true Dao/Way. Guarding the Dao/Way without cease leads to immortality; immortality, unceasing, aligns one’s spirit with Heaven. The spirit, unceasing, merges with primordial qi. Attaining primordial qi, one encompasses the eight directions of Heaven and Earth—all things receive this qi and live. Such is the merit of a good teacher. Without a good teacher, one loses the path.

Thus, the transmission from teacher to teacher is firmer than metal and stone. To falsely claim transmission without a teacher is to invite deviation. Abandoning one’s teacher is to abandon the true Dao/Way—self-imposed ruin. The Dao/Way has lineage teachers and ancestral teachers.

*The Jade Record of Settling the True* states: In cultivating the mind, one must not forget even for a moment; only then does the spirit settle. Settled, one enters the Dao/Way, its signs manifesting externally. Guard one’s speech, lest it disturb things; moderate one’s diet, lest greed arise. Wear coarse, quiet clothing, embracing simplicity; dwell in humble seclusion, upholding stillness. Be reverent in all things, avoiding insult; do not presume to lead, to escape jealousy and slander. Maintain pure faith from beginning to end, subtly guiding transformation. Advance and retreat with harmonious light, practicing teaching in secret. Blunt sharpness, resolve entanglements—illuminate the Dao/Way in due time. In action and stillness, transformation reveals the swiftness of divine response.

It also says: The Perfected of the Nine Palaces enter and exit through the Yellow Gate, inquiring about the Dao/Way at the Crimson Terrace. Thus, terraces and gates are placed to the left and right of the Dao/Way to govern extraordinary qi and await the comings and goings of the Perfected.

*The Scripture of the Dao’s Foundation* states: Consuming wheat is beneficial, for wheat contains the sweet beginning. Daoists who master qi eat wheat to transcend the world. It also says: Aligning with the Dao/Way without speech attains the truth of non-being. Day and night without sleep, the light of sun and moon merges; without hunger or thirst, one practices the embryonic breathing of tortoises and dragons. It further states: Those who eat grains are called grain immortals; if they practice without ceasing, they may prolong their longevity. Those who abstain from grains may transcend the world.

It also says: Do not sell my Dao/Way to seek money; do not force my Dao/Way upon the powerful and honored; do not diminish my Dao/Way to flatter the slanderous.

*The Scripture of the Yellow Court* states: Immortals and Daoists who refine qi do not possess spirits—it is the result of nurturing life, focusing harmonious qi. If a Daoist fears and preserves the spirit, they may sound the Heavenly Drum, its resonance reaching the Great Ultimate.

*The Regulations of the Supreme Perfected* states: Daoists studying scriptures and cultivating practices should prioritize the *Five Thousand Characters*. It also says: The Dao/Way has stillness and movement—qi transforms into form, wisdom transforms into sound. It further states: The Emperor’s teaching is the Dao/Way; the Sovereign’s teaching is virtue; the King’s teaching is benevolence.

*The Master Who Embraces Simplicity* states: Seeking a teacher requires depth and breadth, like crossing the vast sea or reaching distant isles—one’s strength may be lacking, but never should one lament scarcity. What the tiger and leopard discard, the fox and rat covet; what Tao Zhu fled, Yuan Xian lacked. Focus the mind, rely on the teacher, follow the method to practice the Dao/Way—deliver the self, transcend the world, and benefit in eternal prosperity. Serve the teacher with utmost reverence, with attaining the Dao/Way as the goal, observing their demeanor and awaiting their countenance. Failing to fully illuminate the teacher’s Dao/Way incurs ineradicable sin. Learning the Dao/Way with a teacher and clearly serving them prevents harm and chaos from arising.

*The Scripture of the Threefold Non-Being and the True One* states: One who masters the *Great Cavern Scripture of Guarding the One* becomes a teacher.

*The Scripture of the Great Clarity* states: Heaven and Earth rely on the Dao/Way as their resource; the sage relies on the Dao/Way as their teacher. “Resource” means upholding the Dao/Way to nurture all life; “teacher” means instructing those who do not know to achieve completion. It also says: One who masters the *Great Cavern Scripture of Guarding the One* becomes a teacher. Thus, venerating and establishing the root and branches to perfection clarifies the bitterness of Heaven’s warnings, fulfills the expectations of the divine spirits, and ascends the steps to begin. Therefore, teachers and friends fortify the outer; the Three Ones mirror the inner. The Lord of Heaven delights in their words; the infant rejoices in their dwelling.

*Laozi* states: Heaven and Earth rely on the Dao/Way as their resource; the sage relies on the Dao/Way as their teacher. “Resource” means upholding the Dao/Way to nurture all life; “teacher” means instructing those who do not know to achieve completion.

*The Scripture of the Purple Palace of the Highest Clarity* states: Studying scriptures without a teacher’s transmission is stealing Heaven’s treasure.

Receiving without oaths or trust violates Heaven’s Dao/Way. *The Perfected Scripture of the Eight Simplicities* states: The Supreme Mysterious Person’s equality with Heaven and Earth is valued for their ability to teach and guide one another. The earlier awakened return to guide the later awakened, reversing the flow to return to the One Source.

The Heavenly Perfected Sovereign declares: All you gentlemen have accumulated learning to extinguish kalpas and perfect the Dao/Way’s work. Having received these texts to return among the living, you all transcend the void and tread the emptiness, ascending to the Golden Gates to receive titles of spontaneity. Such matters are profound and distant, beyond the clarity of the mortal world. Examining those who prolonged their lives, we find: Master Night Radiance of the Gate of Envy learned from Master High Mound; Master Stone Duke learned from Master Vast Cliff; and Master Grand Peak studied the Five Refinements of the Numinous Treasure’s kalpa-extinction and the transmission of celestial ascent under the Golden Mother.

It further states: *The Orthodox Unity Scriptural Texts* warn: If one seeks profit through street-corner methods, obscures the proper canon, transmits errors through misguided practice, and misleads later generations—later generations, shallow and careless, rashly follow the easy path without seeking lofty virtue—then greed for empty fame, fame without substance, will turn hoped-for blessings into calamity, deepening the disaster. If transmission is entrusted to the unworthy, the Dao/Way is not bestowed in vain. One must ever fear that the frivolous and superficial will swiftly generate slander, inviting disaster and incurring grave offenses. Thus, trust is established, and the heart’s sincerity becomes the basis for bestowal, with distinctions made in the act of transmission and reception.

*The Scripture of the Cavernous Perfection* states: In cultivating the Dao/Way of the Great One, one must avoid seeing blood and filth, and weeping is also forbidden. *The Scripture of Great Possession* states: Those who receive the precious scriptures of the Highest Clarity must not weep. *The Scripture of the Mystic Mother’s Eight Gates* states: In storing the essence of the Golden Flower and the Feminine One, one must strictly guard against weeping, which disturbs the body with excessive sorrow.

*First Section of the Daoist Canon Complete*
*Second Section of the Daoist Canon*

The Perfected Ones, Above

*The Scripture of the Supreme* states: Within the Great Tenuous Heaven, there are twenty-four intermingled qi, yellow and variegated, coalescing—possessing names but no qi, transforming into Perfected Ones. The accumulation and completion of the Dao/Way entrusts form and establishes shadow; soaring with time, possessing names but no bodies, these are called Perfected Ones.

*The Scripture of the Eight Simplicities* states: Those who diligently cultivate and attain the Dao/Way shall inscribe it upon petal-tablets and carve it in jade script, ascending to the rank of Left Perfected Lord of Highest Clarity. It further states: Dragon robes, phoenix mantles, and tiger belts are all offerings presented to the Thearch by the Perfected of the Armies.

*The Declarations of the Perfected* states: The Central August Lord is a disciple of the Heavenly Thearch. From birth, he knew the essentials of long life and the methods of celestial transcendents. Early in life, he encountered profound resonance, whereupon the Supreme bestowed upon him *The Nine Perfected Scriptures of the Thearch* and *The Eight Secret Chapters of the Dao/Way*. Upon completion of the Dao/Way, he was granted scriptures and became the Perfected One of the Great Ultimate. It further states: The Perfected One of Pure Emptiness received the *Three Leaping Methods* from the Perfected One of the Primal Simplicity; the Perfected One of Paulownia Cypress cultivated the *Sword-Releasing Method*. Possessing *The Supreme’s Leaping Sun Script*, he attained the rank of Perfected One of the Lower Origin. It further states: Those who do not know the Hidden Dao/Way of Returning to the Origin may not have their names inscribed among the Highest Perfected. The Return to the Origin is the day of the Supreme’s renewal; on that day, one must constantly contemplate and dwell upon auspicious matters. It further states: Falsehood is the illness of virtue; ostentation is the calamity of the body.

Those who cling to stagnation are the cause of loss; those who bear shame and disgrace stain their conduct. Only after dispelling these four flaws may one inquire into the Dao/Way. One with a heart of lewd ostentation cannot practice the Dao/Way of the Highest Perfected. Yesterday, I witnessed the names of such individuals being struck from the registers of the Palace of Pure Emptiness, and their cases were further examined and handed over to the Three Officials—how could one not be cautious?

The talents of the Perfected Immortals of the Purple Tenuity shine inwardly and are discerning outwardly. Their names are recorded in the Great Ultimate, inscribed in gold upon the Eastern Land. Once the inner obstructions are stilled, one must accumulate without cease.

It further states: Those who examine the root of the Dao/Way become Perfected Ones of the Highest Clarity. Those who fully master the esoteric methods of the Perfected Immortals and perfect the *Dao of the Thorny Obstruction* become Perfected Ones of the Nine Palaces. If one fully possesses each of these Dao/Way, then one becomes a Perfected One of the Great Ultimate.

It further states: Refining the form in the Great Yin, altering one’s appearance before the Three Officials, receiving instruction in transforming the spirit, bathing in radiance to exchange qi, and moving in harmony with the four seasons—thus may one become a Perfected One.

*The Scripture of the Golden Root* states: The Heavenly Chart and Jade Pass are where the host of Perfected Ones gather for feasts and revelry. It further states: Above the Heavenly Pass stand six-tiered jade terraces, where the Perfected Ones of the Highest Lord assemble for banquets. It further states: In the northern hall of the Jade Guardian’s Azure Palace hangs a golden lattice, upon which rest golden seals, phoenix-stamped tallies, jade tablets, cinnabar writings, feathered canopies, and the ritual robes of those who attain perfection.

*The Scripture of Great Possession* states: In the Azure Palace of Jade Splendor are treasured scriptures and jade instructions, which are bestowed upon those who become Perfected Ones. It further states: *The Supreme’s Primal Numinous Cavern Mystery Scripture* transforms the Three Perfected. *The Scripture of the Great Cavern* says: The Dao/Way has Three Perfected, which must never leave the body. The Purple Radiance transforms the luminous form, and the Three Lights illumine the Perfected.

*The Jade Scripture of the Great Cavern* states: Within the Great Nonbeing Mountain lies the Cavern Palace’s Jade Portal, atop the lofty peaks of Mount Emei, where the names of all Perfected Immortals who attain the Dao/Way are inscribed. It further states: Above the clouds stands the Palace of Highest Clarity, its gates flanked by two towers—left the Golden Tower, right the Jade Tower—guarded by feather-robed sentinels. Within flows the Jade Mushroom and Flowing Radiance Spring, where golden inscriptions record the names of the soaring Perfected Immortals and Flying Transcendents. It further says: Within the Jade Clarity is the Palace of Great Radiance, where the Jade Perfected gather for feasts and revelry. It further states: The Nine Perfected Lords of the Immortals are the sovereigns who enforce the prohibitions of the Highest Lord. The *Washing of the Tassels* is the Pool of the Imperial River. It further states: The Highest One of the Supreme Origin is the overseer of the myriad immortals.

The Perfected One of the Sacred Peaks’ True Qi, the Perfected One of the Highest Lord, treads the path of the Five Stars to descend into the chamber.

*The Scripture of the Great Cavern* states: The Crimson City and Vermilion Windows are the transcendent realm of the Highest Clarity, the inner abode of the Supreme Unity’s Three Perfected Treasure Hall. It further states: The Perfected One of the Highest Clarity, the Grand Marshal of the Host of Immortals and Master of Longevity Methods, ascends the Azure Terrace of the Great Emperor’s Vast Wave Mountain, entering the twin jade caverns to drink deeply of the Purple Radiance Mushroom Nectar. It further states: Those who preserve the spirit through longevity love mountains and waters, for benevolence and wisdom govern their movement and stillness. Those who rely on benevolence are tranquil and long-lived; those who rely on wisdom are active and joyful. One should submit a petition, sending one’s name to exalt benevolence and wisdom, inscribing it in cinnabar on a white slip to transfer one’s register to the Highest Clarity. Kindling the incense burner and bowing, one wraps the slip in green paper and green silk, binding it to a rock upon a cliff. Boarding a boat upon the waters, one reads the petition midstream, attaching one’s name to it—thus may one surely summon the Perfected.

*The Inner Instructions of the Nine Perfected Central Scripture of the Highest Clarity* states: The Duke of the Jade Guardian was sent down by the Primal Simplicity to welcome those of the Nine Perfected. It further states: Those who wish to practice the methods of the Nine Perfected must purify themselves in a secluded chamber, for the Heavenly Thearch records their deeds.

*The Regulations of the Supreme Perfected* states: The Feathered Immortals and Attendant Gentlemen of the Upper Capital Bureau oversee the ranking of positions. They govern the Jade Perfected and the Perfected Ones of the Highest Lord within the Flowery Chambers of the Five Peaks. Without one’s name in the immortal registers, one may not witness them. When the cinnabar slips are reviewed and names are recorded in the Southern Palace... It further states: The Golden Tower of the Vacuous Sovereign is the most noble and exalted of the Jade Emperor’s domains, named *Self-So*, for none can make it so, and none can make it otherwise. Harmonizing one’s light with others, appearing similar yet remaining distinct—only those who attain the Dao/Way can comprehend this.

It further states: In the Highest Clarity’s Yu-Yu Heaven are Three Perfected Officials who govern those guilty of excessive punishment, secret malevolence, treachery, jealousy toward the worthy, vacillation, and defilement or disrespect toward the Perfected Ones.

*The Hidden Writings of Jade Clarity* states: Those whose names are inscribed in the Golden Lattice become Perfected Ones of the Three Heavens, bearing the Tiger Talismans of the Perfected Sovereigns at the Highest Ultimate’s supreme rank. The Highest Perfected ride winged dragons; the Middle Perfected hold purple staffs; the Lower Perfected attend the Great Ultimate’s tripartite chariot. It further states: The Supreme Tenuity is where the Heavenly Thearch commands the Perfected Ones of the Supreme Tenuity to exhort the host of spirits. It further states: The Jade Emperor of the Highest Sovereign commands the Dark-Feathered Perfected One to welcome the Heavenly Thearch of the Supreme Tenuity, and further commands the Perfected One of the Highest Lord to open the pearl-studded coffer, bringing forth *The Hidden Writings of the Jade Perfected* and *The Scripture of the Dark-Feathered One* to transmit to the sovereign of the Heavenly Thearch of the Supreme Tenuity.

*The Scripture of the Jade Characters of the Inner Sounds* states: The Perfected Ones scatter incense in the Jade Court. It further says: They disperse the hundred-harmonized incense and scatter the blossoms of the five clouds to behold the Flying Heavenly Perfected Ones. It further states: The Perfected Ones of the Four Poles oversee the registers of human destiny, constantly riding the *Mengzhen* chariots to review the records of human transgressions. It further states: The Nine-Splendor Perfected One governs within the Southern Upper Palace, reviewing human merits and transgressions, with the Three Officials presenting their reports.

It further states: The Heavenly Perfected Sovereign says: The great Brahma’s hidden language of the Inner Sounds of the Heavens, in its natural jade characters, was commanded by the Highest Lord to be annotated and explained in its correct pronunciation by the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign, sufficient to enlighten and deliver the heavenly and human realms.

*The Hidden Instructions for Ascending Perfection* states: The Jasper Terrace of Kunlun is where the true scriptures are reviewed and established. The highest grade resides in the Highest Clarity, comparable to the dignity of emperors and sovereigns. The middle grade dwells in the Middle Dao/Way, equivalent to the ranks of dukes and ministers. The lowest grade resides at the end of the Three Origins, akin to the ranks of great officers. The scriptures of the Three Perfected grades each have their proper order.

The *Sanmei* Perfected, riding a wind-and-cloud dragon chariot, descends to guard those who observe the fast. The *Taisu* Perfected transmits the method for dispelling nightmares in beginners. The *Jinhua* Perfected engraves the *Great Cavern Upper Scripture* upon the eastern wall of the casement in the Jade Forest Hall of the Celestial Emperor’s Purple Tenuity Palace. The *Taixu* Perfected expounds the *Scripture of the Great Raven*, while the *Taiji* Perfected recites the verses of the Queen Mother of the West. The *Dianjin* Perfected examines the good and evil of men, and the *Miaoxing* Perfected reckons the reckoning of kalpas.

It is further said: On the midday of the *Lichun* day, the *Taiji* Perfected regularly convenes with all immortals in the *Taiji* Palace, engraving jade tablets to record the names of immortals. By the midday of the *Chunfen* day, at the Jasper Terrace of Kunlun, the *Taisu* Perfected gathers all immortals to review and establish the true scriptures. The Jasper Terrace of Kunlun is the palace of the Queen Mother of the West, known as the Western Jasper Upper Terrace, where all the secret texts of the Heavenly Perfected are contained. The *Taisu* Perfected governs upon the White Water Sandbar, where the true scriptures are established.

On the midday of the *Lixia* day, the Five Emperors of Highest Clarity convene with all immortals in the Purple Tenuity Palace, where the Four Perfected Ones deliberate upon the merits and transgressions of those who seek the Dao/Way. By the midday of the *Xiazhi* day, the Three Officials of Heaven gather at the River of Life’s Command to review and determine the sins and blessings of all people, increasing or decreasing their allotted years. On the midday of the *Liqiu* day, the Perfected Ones of the Five Peaks proceed to the Central Yellow Chamber to establish the sacred maps and efficacious medicines of the world. By the midday of the *Lidong* day, the *Yangtai* Perfected assembles the ranks of immortals to determine those newly attained to the Dao/Way, who are then first entered into the *Record of Named Immortals*. On the midday of the *Dongzhi* day, all immortals proceed to the *Fangzhu* Palace, where the Azure Lad of the Eastern Sea engraves their names in golden script within the inner characters of the immortal register.

All who study the Dao/Way should regularly, at midnight and midday, offer repentance for their transgressions, whereby their sins shall be erased, and they may refine themselves and return to goodness, seeking long life and transcendence. At the *Qiufen* season, when qi resides in clarity and emptiness, it is the true day of Great Harmony. On this day, all the Perfected and immortals hear grievances, expose corrupt officials, and all the immortal officials within their jurisdictions impeach and report the merits and transgressions of Daoist practitioners everywhere, as well as the sins of sentient beings deserving of life or death. Thus, the *True Record of Immortal Taboos* states: "If you wish to ascend to heaven, be cautious at the autumnal equinox; no sin, great or small, shall escape notice." These are the essential words of Master Zhongyang of the Vermilion Fire Cinnabar Mound Palace.

It is also said: These words derive from the *Arrayed Records*, wherein the Azure Lad transmitted the sayings of the Ancient Perfected to the Gong family, stating that sins and blessings, however minute, are engraved in the registers of the Cinnabar City. Nothing is concealed—every hidden virtue and every secret evil, however slight, is meticulously recorded.

It is further said: The Dao/Way of the Highest Perfected comprises seven scriptures: first, the *Supreme Shang’s Text of Racing the Sun*; second, the *Supreme Shang’s Chapter of Binding Neighbors and Racing the Moon*; third, the *Supreme Shang’s Eight Simplicities Chapter of Racing the Stars*; fourth, the *Flying Heavenly Scripture of the Grand Tenuity*; fifth, the *Supreme Great Cavern True Scripture*; sixth, the *Purple Text of the Numinous Book of the Golden Watchtower*; and seventh, the *Central Scripture of the Nine Perfected*.

The rank of the Highest Perfected corresponds to the emperors of all heavens. When they proceed, they are preceded by thirty-seven colored banners and ten thousand Perfected Ones.

The Dao/Way of the Middle Perfected comprises six scriptures: the *Hidden Book of the Great Elixir*, the *Mysterious Text of the Nine Perfected*, the *Golden Writs of the Supreme Shang*, the *Upper Scripture of the Fangzhu*, the *Inner Text of the Three Sovereigns*, and the *Purple Book of Oral Instructions and Registers*. The rank of the Middle Perfected belongs to the ranks of ministers and chancellors of Highest Clarity. They bear purple plumes and hold jade tablets, serving as attendants to the Jade Emperor.

The Dao/Way of the Lower Perfected comprises eight scriptures: the *Seven Transformations of Highest Clarity*, the *Eight Arts of Concealing the Earth*, the *Jade Book of the Mysterious Sovereign*, the *Cavern Scripture of the Divine Continent*, the *Central Methods of the Purple Court*, the *Yellow Dao Register of Descents*, the *Central Chapters of Plain Memorials*, and the *Jade Book of the Upper Origin*. The rank of the Lower Perfected corresponds to the ranks of great officers of Highest Clarity. They bear five-colored banners and streamers, flying in inverted reflection.

It is further said: Those who obtain and behold the *Sacred Arrayed Records* shall have their names written in dark thread and memorialized to Highest Clarity, whereupon they shall be appointed as immortal ministers. If they can perform the true affairs of the Golden Watchtower, they shall be enfeoffed as great officers. This is because the *Arrayed Records* are weightier than the *Purple Texts*. Merely seeing them is not merely a matter of receiving and wearing them; rather, it means understanding the relative importance of the scriptures contained therein, the ladder of seeking the Dao/Way, and pursuing study accordingly. Thus, it surpasses the mere observance of the singular affairs of the *Purple Texts*.

The *Jade Register of the Supreme Sovereign* states: The Twenty-Four Perfected Ones, who bear jade registers as they traverse mountains and rivers, shall have the spirits of rivers and seas come forth to welcome and clear their path. The *Hidden Book of the Numinous Treasure* states: The *Zhongji* Perfected governs the registers of human lifespans; the *Jiuhua* Perfected presides over the karmic retributions of the Nine Dark Realms, determining life and death; the *Taiyuan* Perfected receives the celestial talismans and delivers the souls of the long night; the *Taiji* Perfected governs the Jade Cavern Prefecture of the Red City, overseeing the records of life and death on Mount Tai; the *Sanyuan* Perfected governs the practice of the Dao/Way in the Purple Tenuity.

The *Jade Instructions of the Red Book* states: On the fourteenth day of every month, the Celestial Perfected Sovereign of the Supreme Emperor commands the Envoys of the Great One to descend and travel together with the Envoys of the Northern Zhengdu and the Earls, inspecting the merits and transgressions of men and spirits, reporting them to the Upper Offices. Additionally, the Eight Divine Envoys of the Great One of the Kalpa descend with the Three Officials to inspect the good and evil of heaven and earth, reporting them accordingly. They also dispatch the Nine Divisions of Censor-Officers to patrol the Five Peaks, the Three Palaces, and the Water Palaces, rectifying ghostly affairs, overseeing the merits and transgressions of men, and reporting them to heaven.

The *White Feather Scripture* states: The *Tai* Perfected, ascending a white simurgh chariot and driving a black phoenix from the Nine Sources, is unmatched in virtue from heaven downward. Moreover, the *Taiji* Perfected possesses the fine countenance of an immortal, which fundamentally arises from a compassionate heart that nurtures all things. Only then can one attain transcendence. If one cannot restrain one’s nature, the immortal countenance shall be ruined. Thus, in cultivating the Dao/Way and meeting the Perfected, one must take essence and thought as the foundation, spirit as the root, and enter contemplation by preserving spirit. Stillness and mindfulness must come first.

The *Great Kalpa Scripture* states: The *Shangjing* Perfected leads the world’s forces to release the Mother of the Great Flood of the Upper Origin, dredging the myriad rivers. The *Scripture of the Empty Sea* states: The *Hejian* is the hidden abode of heavenly beings, where upon jade towers are arrayed the halls of the Perfected and immortals. Moreover, the Highest Perfected, whose bodies are imbued with true qi, possess luminous jade eyes.

*The Southern Perfected Transmission* states: Yesterday, I accompanied Shu Jia to the Palace of Pure Emptiness to review the records of Perfected Immortals’ gains and losses. Recently, forty-seven were abruptly removed, while only three were promoted. Among them, Nei Mingzhenzheng is truly exceptional.

The Nine-Palace Perfected enter and exit through the Yellow Gate and Crimson Terrace. The space between them is the Dao/Way, and thus the terraces and gates are placed to its left and right to observe the extraordinary qi of the Perfected as they come and go.

*The Scripture of the Supreme Orthodox Dharma* states: The Nine Perfected are formed from the true qi of the Nine Heavens. The Upper, Middle, and Lower Three Perfected are born of the Grand Clarity, the settled qi of the Primordial Beginning. Each is assigned palaces in sequence. The officials guarding the Upper Clarity Palace are the Supreme Lord of the Great Dao, sovereign of the myriad Perfected. Dwelling in the Jade Hall, he composes the sacred scriptures of the Supreme Emperor, which serve as treasured canons in the Jade Clarity Palace to guide later students toward attaining Perfection.

*The Scripture of the Three Origins’ Precepts* states: The Purple Tenuity Palace observes the rites of extending life. It is also said that the Jade Controller of the Vermilion Emperor, Yujingdu, governs the Crimson Yang Terrace in the south, overseeing the Upper Perfected.

Master Jinglin of the Perfected said: Through diligent cultivation over many lifetimes, one’s thoughts turn to the Perfected and one’s aspirations to the numinous. The August Mirror perceives this devotion to the Supreme Ultimate, inscribing one’s name upon the Jade Register. Thus, in fine script upon the Palace of Purple Emptiness, in vermilion upon the Eastern Florescence Pavilion, one’s name is carved in the Upper Clarity, recorded in cinnabar and brocade ledgers.

*The Numinous Chapters of the Empty Cavern* states: The Perfected pluck the *ao* zither, blow the flutes of the Nine Phoenixes, and play the reed pipes of the Divine Continent. Their music soars, its echoes cascading a thousand fathoms.

*The Later Sage’s Arrayed Records* states: The Later Sage of the Golden Gate of the Upper Clarity, in his youth, delighted in the Dao/Way and rejoiced in the Perfected. In the Purple Tenuity Palace of the Upper Perfected Celestial Emperor, he was bestowed the Purple Elixir, the Rigid Cinnabar, and the Phoenix Seal, enabling him to dwell in the Upper Clarity, wander the Supreme Ultimate, descend to govern the various heavens, and be enfeoffed to oversee the multitudes.

*The Immortal Records* states: In practicing the affairs of the Great Unity and the Dao/Way of the Perfected, one must not bow in physical prostration—only in the heart, without bending the form. Contemplating the Perfected and practicing the Dao/Way, one’s understanding becomes boundless. Manifestations appear in due time, and ascent to Perfection is swift.

*The Upper Chapter of the Black Register* states: The Sagely Perfected and Immortals together practice virtue and power, all venerating the Supreme Mystery.

*The Scripture of Precept Texts* states: The Supreme Perfected dwell in the Immortal Courts; all who attain immortality in the world must first pass through here.

*The Scripture of the Natural Jade Characters* states: Within the Seven Treasures Grove lies the pleasure garden of the Upper Perfected and the playground of the Perfected.

*The Jade Book of the Grand Empyrean* states: The Jade Scion of the Primordial August, ascending to the Supreme Perfected, governs the Two Modes. In the Mysterious Garden, he holds the Jade Register; among the myriad immortals, he oversees the earthly realm; over the Five Marchmounts, he commands the Upper Perfected; at the Three Passes, he presides over the boundless. Below, he governs the Cavernous Sources, and from heaven downward, none are not subject to him.

It further states: The Three Origins Lord of the Grand Simplicity receives the numinous harmony of the Jade Emperor’s upper qi. Thus, he coalesces within the Void, embracing the true and radiant, his mechanism wondrously merging with the spirit, his luminous Dao/Way encompassing the Nine Mysteries. His breath precedes all signs, responding to all things in accord—this is the congealing of the Supreme.

*The Jade Scripture of the Four Illuminations of the Supreme* states: The Dao/Way of the Perfected Immortals takes the ears and eyes as its foundation. Indulgence in lust dims the eyes; excessive affection dulls the ears. These two afflictions arise from within and rush outward. There is no other remedy—only by enhancing clarity and ease. Yet one must refrain from such indulgences, purifying the heart and severing desires, casting aside lust and greed. This is called "strictness at the outset." Safeguarding the paired gates, opening the nine portals, morning saliva ascending to the Mud-Pill Palace, one is arrayed among the Upper Perfected. Vision extends far, hearing reaches the faintest sounds—this is the loftiness of the Perfected Immortals, surpassing mere acuity of ears and eyes.

*The Pearl Satchel of the Three Caverns* states: The Highest Jade Clarity’s hidden inscription on stone reads: Dengdu Mountain lies in the north, containing an empty cavern within which are six palaces. This inscription is carved on the northern wall of the palace to restrain the myriad malevolent forces, preventing their wanton violence. Those who study the Dao/Way and carry this inscribed stone will have their names stricken from the Northern Feng Register and their lives spared in the Southern Palace, becoming Perfected.

*The Scripture of Great Peace* states: Those who attain the Dao/Way in later study possess varying ranks, ascending to the ultimate Sagely Perfected Immortals.

*The Scripture of the Jade Register of Settled Perfection* states: Those who wish to settle their minds must first receive the Jade Register of Settled Perfection from the August Sovereign of the Uppermost. This is the foremost essential for students. Only by first settling the mind can the name of an immortal be secured—this is the Orthodox Unity of the Three Heavens, the register first bestowed to determine one’s immortal name.

*The Scripture of the Supreme* states: The Jade Clarity is like jade—unyielding and indestructible, unstained by slander. Unwavering and pure, all defilements are exhausted, singular and unadulterated—thus is one called a Perfected.

*The Cinnabar Slips of the Supreme* states: All who study the Dao/Way and dwell in the position of the Perfected have their names entered in the Southern Palace.

*The Scripture of the Three and Five in Harmonious Practice* states: Harmonizing virtue and entering the Dao/Way is called "Perfected." The Supreme dispatches the Four Poles Perfected to welcome them, bestowing the texts of the Three Heavens’ Numinous Registers in the Upper Clarity Palace.

*The Eight Radiant Scriptures of the Upper Clarity* states: After a hundred days of concentrated contemplation, the Perfected descend in form.

Ge Xuan’s *Preface to the Five Thousand Characters* states: Through concentrated contemplation, one’s aspirations reach far and high, prompting the Supreme to send Perfected to descend and confer the subtle and profound principles. It further states: In tranquil contemplation, awaiting the Perfected, the myriad wonders respond in harmony. Inwardly observing one’s form and shadow, spirit and qi endure; embodying virtue and power, the hundred spirits submit in awe.

*The Feminine Unity Chapter of the Great Cavern* states: A golden countenance shines in the Eastern Florescence; a jade form delights at the Emperor’s Gate. The spirit illumines the Five Elders, leaping through the Three Origins. Crowned with treasured radiance, one floats among the Nine Dawns, dispersing forms and scattering light, attaining the rank of Upper Perfected.

*The Scripture of Ascending Mystery* states: One must seek the Dao/Way and pursue the Perfected with loyalty and integrity, reforming evil and embracing goodness. Only then can one become a Perfected.

*The Scripture of the Three Origins’ Jade Tallies* states: On the ninth day of the ninth month in the gengyin year of the sexagenary cycle, the Primordial Beginning convened an oath at the Palace of Supreme Purity, bestowing the Jade Tallies of the Three Origins to be transmitted to later disciples. Those whose mystic names correspond shall become Perfected of the Supreme Purity.

**Section Two of the Daoist Canon Concludes**
**Section Three of the Daoist Canon: The Perfected Below**

*The Records of Immortals Gathered* states: The Queen Mother is the Metal Mother of Mount Tortoise. The essence of the Western Florescence’s purest qi transformed and gave birth to the Metal Mother, who emerged already soaring, dwelling in the utmost yin origin, her position paired with the West. She nurtures all beings, and her palaces reside in the gardens of Kunlun within the precincts of Mount Chong, the Parks of Langfeng. Her city spans a thousand *li*, with twelve towers—none may reach it save by chariots of jade or feathered wheels. Her disheveled hair and tiger teeth are not her true form but the numinous manifestation of the Metal Realm. The Primordial Beginning conferred upon her the Register of the Nine Lights of Mount Tortoise under the governance of the Myriad Heavens’ Primordial Unity, empowering her to command the ten thousand spirits, marshal the host of Perfected, and lead the feathered retinues of all heavens. At the celestial feasts of the Heavenly Emperor, she presides over the precious scriptures of the Supreme Purity, the jade texts of the Three Caverns—all transmissions and initiations fall within her purview.

During the reign of the Yellow Emperor, the Queen Mother dispatched envoys riding white deer to his court, presenting him with a terrestrial map. Later, during the reign of Emperor Shun, she sent messengers bearing a white jade ring and an expanded terrestrial map. Thus, the nine provinces of the Yellow Emperor were extended to twelve. She also bestowed upon Shun a jade flute to harmonize the eight winds.

*The Verified Era of the Divine Emperors* states: The Queen Mother’s realm lies in the Western Wilderness. All who attain the Dao and receive scriptures pay homage to her at the gates of Kunlun.

Wang Bao, styled Zideng, purified himself for three months, whereupon the Queen Mother bestowed upon him the *Seven Dawns’ Luminous Scripture of Jade Blossoms*. Mao Ying, following the Western City’s Perfected Lord, journeyed to the White Jade Tortoise Terrace to pay homage to the Queen Mother and seek the Dao of longevity. The Queen Mother transmitted to him the *Scripture of Mystic Perfection* and granted him the *Precious Writs of the Youthful Scatterer* for dissemination in the four directions.

During the reign of King Mu of Zhou, he bridged the Weak Waters with beams of giant turtles, fish, and soft-shelled turtles to ascend the wilds of Kunlun’s Mystic Gardens and the Parks of Langfeng, where he met the Queen Mother. They sang the *Ballad of White Clouds*, and he carved an inscription at the foot of Yan Mountain before returning.

Emperor Wu of Han, devoted to the Dao of longevity, in the first year of the Yuanfeng era, ascended Mount Song to construct the Terrace of Seeking the Perfected. After purifying himself and contemplating the Dao, the Queen Mother descended on the seventh day of the seventh month in a chariot of purple clouds, drawn by nine-hued mottled dragons. She bore the staff of the Heavenly Perfected, the seal of adamantine spirit, and a robe of yellow brocade, its golden radiance resplendent. Her sash was woven with patterns of flying clouds, her crown the *Celestial Grand Perfected’s Dawn Tassel*, her slippers adorned with phoenixes of square jasper. Her celestial bearing was majestic, a being beyond mortal comparison.

Alighting from her chariot, she leaned upon two attendants to ascend the dais, seating herself facing east. She commanded her attendants to bring peaches, which they presented on a jade platter—seven in total. Four she gave to the Emperor, and three she consumed herself. The Emperor wished to collect the pits for planting, but the Queen Mother said: “This peach bears fruit but once in three thousand years. The soil of the central lands is too meager; it will not grow here.”

When asked about the Dao of longevity, she replied: “To scorn glory and delight in humility is itself excellent. The Dao of nurturing life and the essence of governing the body lie in ceaseless cultivation. Those who seek longevity must first master their own bodies, firmly guard the Three Ones, and preserve the root of spirit. Let clarity and purity ascend to the Muddy Pellet; let the Three Palaces be fully defended within the Crimson Palace. Let the Yellow Court’s earthly forces remain unscattered—this is what is meant by breathing the Great Harmony, preserving the natural, and embodying the true essential Dao.”

“As for the supreme elixirs of the Most High, they are the marvels of the Celestial Emperor. The wondrous herbs of the Lower Yin and the layered clouds are all medicines of the immortals. Those who obtain the highest grade age only after heaven’s decree, for these are consumed by the Most High—treasures not for middling immortals. The middle grade, if attained, allows one to wander after heaven’s decree, for these are consumed by the Heavenly Perfected—beyond the reach of lesser immortals. The next rank of medicines includes the Nine Elixirs, Golden Liquor, Purple Rainbow’s Floral Essence, the Ninefold Transmutations of the Great Clarity, the Five Clouds’ Nectar, Mystic Frost and Crimson Snow, the Three Yellows’ Ascension, Eastern Sea’s White Fragrance, the Flying Life of the Dark Continent, the Eight Stones and Thousand Fungi, the Nine Lights of Majestic Joy, the Western Flow’s Stone Gall, the Eastern Sea’s Azure Coin, the Remnant Roots of High Mounds, the Jade Fields of Accumulated Stones, the Great Numinous Returning Elixir—stored in golden orchids, the Crimson Grass of Eternal Light, the Flying Youth of Cloud Children. These are consumed by flying immortals, unknown to earthbound immortals.”

“The lesser medicines—such as fuling, calamus, sesame, and Solomon’s seal—can extend one’s years. Though they do not grant boundless longevity, they bestow a radiant complexion and the status of an earthbound immortal. Seekers of the Dao must first rely on these steps, gradually advancing to greater heights. If one can master breath and ingestion, safeguarding spirit and qi, this is the natural essential Dao of the highest grade.”

“Moreover, the heavens bestow spirit upon the individual, the earth bestows form, and the Dao bestows qi—even the myriad plants and trees are the same. The body takes the Dao as its root; how can one not nurture spirit and secure qi to preserve one’s form? When form and spirit are both whole, this is what the supreme sages prize.”

The Queen Mother commanded the Lady of the Upper Primordial to present the Emperor with the *Writings of the Eight Assemblies*, the *True Charts of the Five Peaks*, the *Talismans of the Five Emperors and Six Jias’ Spirit Flight*—twelve items in all. Yet he could not apply their teachings and was much perplexed. Later, after three sacrifices to the Queen Mother, she descended again, placing the transmitted scriptures upon the Cypress Beam Terrace, where they were consumed by heavenly fire. Li Shaojun departed by dissolving his form, and the affair of the witchcraft arose, leaving the Emperor ever more remorseful.

Furthermore: The Great Mao Lord Ying governed the southern slopes of Mount Juqu. In the second year of the Yuan Shou era, on the yiyou day of the eighth month, the Perfected Lord of the Southern Peak, the Red Lord, the Western City’s Perfected Lord Fang, and the Azure Lad Zhuge descended with the Queen Mother into Mao Ying’s chamber. The Queen Mother also commanded the Lady of the Upper Primordial to transmit to Ying’s younger brothers, Mao Gu and Mao Zhong, the *Hidden Writ of the Grand Empyrean*.

Later, the Purple Spirit Primordial Lady Wei Huacun purified herself in fasting upon the Hidden Primordial Terrace of Mount Yangluo. The Queen Mother and the Golden Portal Sage Lord descended into the terrace, riding the Eight Radiance Chariot together to the Clear Void Upper Palace, where they transmitted four scrolls of the *Jade Clarity Hidden Writ* to Lady Wei. At that time, the Perfected Lords of the Great Void sang the *Song of the Supreme Ultimate*, and the Queen Mother said:

*"Wandering the boundless mystery’s edge,
Ten thousand currents never pause.
Once this moment passes, reunion waits
Till kalpas end and heaven-earth collapse.
Seek the scene within the nothingness—
Neither death nor life shall bind you then.
Clothed in the Dao of spontaneity,
Serene contemplation merges with the Great Obscurity.
The Southern Peak’s true trunk stands firm,
Jade’s radiance gleams in essence’s glow.
Those who bear no burden in their tasks
Empty their hearts to receive the numinous.
A joyous gathering by the Crimson River’s bend,
Together we delight without end."*

The Queen Mother then returned to Tortoise Terrace.

The *Scripture of the Three Ones* states: The Yellow Emperor roamed the Spirit Terrace beneath the sheer cliffs of Mount Qingcheng, where he beheld the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign dwelling in a house of azure jade, its groves of yellow jade, its curtains of kingfisher silk, with attendants all celestial beings.

It further states: Gao Qiuzi, a man of the Shang dynasty, loved the Dao and entered the Six Radiance Mountains. For years, he studied only the *Yellow Plain Daoist Scriptures* and ingested tree essences. Later, he consumed the *Vast Elixir*, attained earthly immortality, and wandered the Five Peaks. He then drank the *Golden Liquid* and became a Perfected Lord of the Central Peak.

It further states: Guo Chongzi, also of the Shang dynasty, was a disciple of Perfected Lord Peng. Once, while traveling in the mountains, bandits exhausted Chong. His disciples wished to pursue and capture them, but Chong said, "Let them go." Later, the bandit entered official service, and Chong praised him. The man visited repeatedly, but each time he declined, saying, "I was once a thief and cannot accept the commendation of a great gentleman." He then took his own life. Later, Chong attained the Dao, but the Perfected Lord of the Supreme Ultimate deemed him guilty of causing a death and thus unfit to become a Perfected Lord. If even an excess of goodness can lead to another’s demise, how much worse the consequences of evil?

It further states: During the reign of Duke Zhuang of Chu, the market overseer Song Laizi would sweep the marketplace daily. After some time, an old beggar entered the market, singing as he wandered through the day:

*"The Celestial Court blooms with twin flowers,
The mountain’s source reveals yin’s perversity.
At dawn, mount the Heavenly Steed,
Come to the Great Perfected’s home.
The Perfected has no way to hide,
And thus dispels a hundred demons."*

He sang this while begging, yet none in the market understood—only Laizi suspected he was a Perfected Lord, though he did not fully grasp the song’s meaning. He then followed the old man and became his disciple. After more than a decade, the old man transmitted to him the Dao of Middle Immortality. Laizi now resides on the Central Peak. The beggar was Perfected Lord Feng Yanshou of the Western Peak, a man of the reign of King Xuan of Zhou.

*"Celestial Court"* refers to the space beneath the two brows, the bridge of penetrating vision, also called the *Flowering Court*. *"Mountain’s source"* is the base of the nose, the root of the philtrum, where it slightly enters the valley. *"Heavenly Steed"* refers to the hands. Pressing the hands to the base of the nose severs the hundred perversities.

It further states: Perfected Lord Yin Xi was a grandee of Zhou. As Keeper of the Pass, he was fond of learning from youth, skilled in celestial patterns and esoteric weft-texts, such that ghosts and spirits could not conceal their forms from him. Neither glory nor disgrace altered his countenance. His heart longed for freedom, his nature profoundly tranquil. One day, ascending a tower to gaze in all directions, he saw a purple vapor advancing westward from the eastern horizon. He said, "The yang numbers are exhausted, the Nine Stars align, and the years and months converge—this must herald an extraordinary person passing through." He then purified himself, swept the road, and awaited the arrival. When Laozi crossed the pass, Yin first instructed the pass officers: "If an old man riding a black ox in a thin-planked cart appears, do not let him pass. Detain him and report to me." As expected, he arrived. The officers reported, and Yin requested a brief delay.

Yin Xi, bearing his official seals and ribbons, performed the rites due to a master, but Laozi firmly declined. Yin Xi said, "I wish you would compose a book for me, expounding the meaning of the Great Dao, that I may receive and practice it." Thereupon, Laozi wrote the *Classic of the Dao and Its Virtue* in two scrolls, the upper and the lower. Yin Xi then departed together for the Dark Continent to assume the office of Supreme Minister.

The *Biography of Su Lin* states: Lin, styled Zixuan, was a native of Qu Shui in Puyang. His father, Xiu, concealed his virtue and hid his brilliance, dwelling on Mount Heng. From youth, Lin was endowed with extraordinary conduct. He first studied under Master Qin Gao of Zhao, receiving the Way of refining qi to prolong life. Later, he studied under Master Qiu of Mount Hua, who taught him the art of returning the spirit, declaring, "You are a true person." He was then to be introduced to Master Juan, but before this could be accomplished, Master Qiu imparted the true essentials to Lin. The master said, "To become a true person upon the earth, you must first expel the Three Corpses." Subsequently, Lin received from the True Person of Purple Yang over two hundred essentials of the Dao. As for guarding the Dark Elixir Chamber and the Cavern Palace, the Three Primordials True Person fully inscribed his name above. Lin became the True Person of the Central Marchmount.

The *Biography of Lord Mao* states: Ying, styled Shushen, was a native of Xianxiang. His father, Zuo, had three sons, of whom Ying was the youngest. From youth, Ying was endowed with extraordinary conduct, transcending worldly customs and resisting conformity. He sought neither fame nor advancement and kept no company with the unworthy. He entered Mount Heng, where he read the *Laozi* and the *Book of Changes* and consumed pine needles, remaining secluded in the mountains for six years. His concentrated devotion to the Dao and sincere aspiration evoked a mysterious response. In a dream, the Jade Maiden of the Great Mystery held a jade knife and led him, saying, "In the Western City, there is a Lord Wang who has attained the true Dao. You may take him as your master." At dawn, he set out in search of him and, upon reaching the Western City, purified himself for three months. At last, he beheld Lord Wang. Ying then bowed his head twice in reverence and earnestly entreated the art of longevity. He was permitted to reside in the Tower of Flowing Radiance within the Western City, in the Upper Palace of Gold and Jade, where he attended Lord Wang day and night, performing the duties of a servant, holding his towel and sandals. For seventeen years, he remained single-minded and unwavering. After two more years, Lord Wang commanded his carriage to ascend White Jade Turtle Mountain, where he paid homage to the Queen Mother in the Azure Forest Palace, taking Ying with him. When Lord Wang prostrated before the Queen Mother, Ying also bowed twice and presented himself before her, receiving the essential Way of governing the body. After practicing these arts for several decades upon returning home, during the reign of Emperor Yuan of Han, celestial officials descended to welcome him and escort him across the Yangtze to reside on Mount Juqu. Thereupon, the August Emperor of Heaven dispatched an edict conferring upon him golden and purple jade tablets, appointing him Supreme Minister of the Eastern Marchmount and True Person of the Great Prime, Controller of Destiny and Divine Lord. He was granted a staff adorned with purple feathers, ten spirit banners of absolute efficacy, a lotus-flower cap, a purple robe embroidered with feathers, a carriage of cinnabar and azure drawn by striped dragons, a canopy of jade and curtains of brocade, a green jade tablet of authority, a pair of flowing-fire pearls, a banner of moon-bright brocade, a black staff with white feathers, a golden bell and jade dish, the rich essence of purple jasper, the golden elixir and jade nectar, and two administrations on Red City Mountain and the Jade Cavern Palace. Above, he was enrolled in the Upper Clarity; below, he presided over the Great Ultimate.
