He was enfeoffed to govern the vast heavens and the lands of Wu and Yue, to oversee the Registers of Life and Death on Mount Tai, to record the attendance of the host of perfected beings, to determine the golden roster of destiny, to preside over the transmission of the Dao to disciples, and to examine and verify the ranks of immortals.

At the time, Lord Mao’s younger brother was appointed to an office with a salary of two thousand bushels. As he prepared to assume his post, many from his hometown came to see him off. Lord Mao was also present and said, "I, too, have an appointment. On such-and-such a day, I shall assume my office." The guests said, "We wish to see Lord Mao off as well." He replied, "There is no need for any expense. I have what is needed for the journey." When the appointed day arrived, a grand banquet was held. The curtains were of green silk, the mats layered in white felt, and rare delicacies and exotic fruits were arrayed in abundance. Musicians performed in harmony, their music audible for miles. Over a thousand attendants accompanied them. The civil officials wore crimson robes with white sashes, while the military officers were clad in martial attire, their armor gleaming. Lord Mao then ascended a carriage adorned with a feather canopy and departed.

In the third year of the Xingning reign of the Jin dynasty, on the fourth day of the seventh month, he first descended to the home of Lord Yang at night. He wore a green brocade skirt, a purple feathered robe, and a hibiscus coronet. Seven attendants entered the household with him: one bearing a purple feathered staff, one holding the ten spirit banners of absolute efficacy, one carrying a green jade document case, one grasping a golden bell, and three bearing white ivory boxes in crimson robes. Thereafter, he descended frequently, and his disciples welcomed and awaited him.

The immortal Li Zun composed his biography, which has become renowned in the world.

The *Pearl Bag of the Three Caverns* states: Wang Bao, styled Zideng, was a seventh-generation descendant of Wang Ling of the Former Han. He consumed the azure essence of earthly grains and traversed precipitous peaks as swiftly as a flying bird, crossing vast waters without bridges or ferries. He also ingested the cinnabar essence of morning clouds and azure radiance, enabling him to see to great distances. The Supreme Lord of the Great Dao dispatched the Left Mystery Attendant of the Orthodox Unity, bearing a canopy, to confer upon him a jade tablet with a vermilion inscription and bestow upon him a banner of red silk and white feathers. He was titled True Person of Pure Emptiness.

The *Declarations of the Perfected* states: Master Red Pine, the Rain Master during the time of the Yellow Emperor, was titled True Person of the Great Ultimate. It also states: Han Weiyuan, the True Person of the Nine Doubts, once studied under Song Dexuan of the Central Marchmount. Dexuan was a man of the time of King Xuan of Zhou. He ingested the *Spiritual Flight of the Six Jia* and attained the Dao, gaining the ability to travel great distances, repeatedly conceal himself, and master the Way of the Dark Mystery. He now resides on Mount Song. After a long time, Weiyuan followed and attained his Way, becoming the True Person of the Nine Doubts.

It further states: Pei Xuanren, a native of Yangxia in You Fufeng, was born in the second year of Emperor Wen of Han. After Pei attained the Dao and was about to enter seclusion, his disciple Deng Yun also attained the Dao. Pei led Deng to Mount Taihua and entered the Western Cavern’s Chamber of Dark Stone. After thirty-two years, five elders suddenly appeared and bestowed upon Pei the divine mushroom’s protection. He was also titled True Person of Pure Emptiness.

It also states: Wang Zhongfu, the True Person of the Central Marchmount, from youth cherished the Dao of immortality. He constantly practiced absorbing the Two Radiances and the method of consuming auroral essence. After over forty years, he perceived no benefit, and his son, who also practiced these arts, ascended as an immortal after eighteen years. Later, the Southern Perfected suddenly descended to Zhongfu’s home and instructed him, saying, "Your brain lacks sufficient essence, and your fluids do not flow. Though you have connected with the true radiance and consumed auroral essence, it has not yet benefited your body."

Wang Zhongfu then turned to medicinal treatment for his ailments while simultaneously cultivating the true Dao. After accumulating years of practice, he finally achieved success. Now, he resides on the Mystic Continent, receiving scriptures, serving as the True Person of the Central Marchmount, and overseeing the Bureau of the Nine Mysteries.

It further states: Fan Bociz, a native of Guiyang, originally followed worldly affairs. Suddenly afflicted by madness, his illness persisted for years. Hearing of Daoist Master Shen’s reputation for effective healing, he left home to seek treatment. After fifty days, his illness was cured. Later, he entered Mount Tianmu, consumed sesame seeds, and meditated with focused intent for seventeen years. He then ingested cinnabar and attained the Dao, becoming the True Person of Primordial Unity.

It further states: Xu Mi, styled Sixuan, also named Mu, was appointed Chief Clerk of the Protectorate by Emperor Jianwen of the Jin. Though outwardly immersed in worldly duties, he inwardly cultivated the study of the true Dao and became an Upper Clarity True Person.

It further states: The Purple Void Primordial Lady oversees the Bureau of Destiny for the Upper Perfected. The Lady Wei of the Southern Marchmount, a disciple of the Jade Clarity Void, was named Huacun and served as the teacher of Yang, the Controller of Destiny. She was the daughter of Wei Shu, Duke Wenkang of the Jin and Minister of Education from Rencheng. At twenty-four, she married Liu Youyan of Nanyang. When Youyan served as Magistrate of Ji County in Xiwu, the Lady fasted and meditated on the Dao, secluding herself for a hundred days. On a midnight in the twelfth month, the Azure Lad and four perfected beings, including Lord Wang, descended together and bestowed upon her thirty-one scrolls of the Upper Scriptures. During the chaos in Luoyang, the Lady crossed the Yangzi and settled in Yuzhang. She followed Yu Pu to Ancheng Commandery in Jiangzhou and remained there. At eighty-three, in the ninth year of Emperor Cheng’s Xianhe reign, the Azure Lad and Pure Void descended again, transmitting the method of sword liberation. Claiming illness, she concealed her transformation, riding a cloud chariot to Mount Yangluo. The following day, forty-seven perfected beings descended to instruct her in the Daoist methods.

After sixteen years, the Queen Mother of the West descended with the Southern Pole of the Golden Towers to welcome the Lady. Together they journeyed north to the Jade Towers beneath the Supreme Clarity Palace, where she received the divine phoenixes and dragon pennants, a tiger-skin sash, a cinnabar flying skirt, ten tasseled banners of radiant splendor, flowing-gold fire-bells, nine-tiered mushroom canopies, nine-colored tablets, twin pearls of lunar brilliance, the talismans of the divine tiger, and embroidered tiger banners. These were bestowed upon the Jade Maidens of Western Florescence, along with an eight-scene flying chariot and a dark nine-dragon carriage. She was further granted the jade-edged golden script of the Great Lord Emperor of Fusang, and enfeoffed as the Purple Void Primordial Lady, overseeing the life-mandates of the Supreme Perfected, governing all who study the Dao, the registers of life and death, and the supervision of the Three Bureaus, adjudicating transgressions and examining sins.

She also received the azure jade tablets and cinnabar registers from the Sacred Lord of the Golden Towers, and was titled Lady of the Southern Crucible, granted a curved morning flying canopy. She was charged with governing the Great Huo Mountain’s Terrace of the Heavenly Terrace Range. Below, she instructed and taught those destined to become perfected immortals. Each month, she ascended twice to Jade Clarity, thrice to the Great Simplicity, and four times paid homage to the Jade Dawn. She roamed and feasted in Fusang, summoned the celestial perfected, compiled the divine registers, inscribed texts across the nine heavens, assisted in the mandate of the Eastern Florescence, aided the Imperial Dawn, soared through the great auroras, and guided the reins of the nine voids. In the Xingning era, she descended to Lord Yang. She was also bestowed the *Upper Scriptures of Xu Yuan*.

From then on, she descended frequently. The Jade Clarity Void commanded her disciple Fan Miao to compose an *Inner Biography* to reveal her to the world.

It is further said: The Perfected Consort of Ninefold Splendor of the Purple Clarity Upper Palace, in the third year of the Xingning era of the Jin, appeared at the age of thirteen or fourteen. She wore a cloud-brocade skirt, cinnabar above and azure below, with an embroidered silk sash at her waist. Over ten small bells, green in hue with alternating yellow, hung from her right sash. On her left, she bore a jade pendant, her fingers adorned with golden rings, her arms bound with white pearls. Her hair was coiled atop her head, the rest cascading to her waist. One attendant, clad in vermilion with azure insignia, carried a satchel over a foot long to hold books—some ten scrolls, their white jade clasps inscribed with the characters *Jade Clarity Divine Void Inner Perfected Purple Primordial Cinnabar Scripture*. Another attendant, dressed in red, bore a white jade casket bound with crimson cords, both aged seventeen or eighteen. From then on, she descended frequently, bestowing scriptures and composing poems.

The *Biographies of the Perfected* states: Ma Mingsheng was a native of Linzi in the state of Qi. His original surname was Bo, given name He, and courtesy name Junxian. While serving as a county clerk, he was wounded by bandits but encountered the Supreme Perfected Primordial Lady, who gave him medicine that instantly healed him. He followed her to a stone chamber on Mount Tai, where golden couches and jade tables stood amidst treasures and marvels beyond mortal reach.

Her devotion was indeed most earnest, and so the Supreme Perfected Primordial Lady bestowed upon him the method of long life, saying: "What I have received and practiced is the *Great Harmony Natural Dragon Embryo* body, which is fitting only to transmit to the Perfected of the Three Heavens—it cannot be taught to beginners." Later, he followed Master Anqi, ingesting elixirs to ascend as an immortal and become a Perfected.

Master Pei the Perfected had thirty-four disciples: eighteen studied the true Dao, while the rest pursued the path of immortality.

**Section Three of the Daoist Canon Concludes**
**Section Four of the Daoist Canon: Heavenly Immortals**

The *Heavenly Immortals Rank* states: Those who soar through the clouds, their spirits transformed and bodies light, are called Heavenly Immortals, also known as Flying Immortals.

The *Scripture of Precepts for the Multitudes of Divine Immortals* states: In the great mountains facing the east of Kuaiji, there are palaces of Heavenly Immortals, their halls and eaves wrought of gold and jade.

The *Golden Root Scripture* states: Above the Heavenly Gates stand layered jade terraces, the place where all immortals come and go.

The *Jade Clarity Inscribed Stone Hidden Inscription* states: Those who wear the *Hidden Script of the Jade Emperor* shall become Supreme Immortals.

The *Scripture of Precept Texts* states: In the northwest of Heaven lies the Hall of Immortals, where ranks and offices are assigned, and names are recorded in the Nine Palaces and Five Dipper Immortal Bureaus. The Central Heaven has east, west, south, north, and center—each with stone cities aligned to their directions, where all offices and departments are arrayed within the Dipper.

The *Later Sage’s Arrayed Records* states: Those whose names are inscribed in the *Mysterious Jade Register* within the Dipper are all Supreme Immortals.

The *Concealed Instructions on Ascending to Perfection* states: The Three Clarities and Nine Palaces each have their retinues, with the left generally superior to the right. Their highest ranks are collectively called *Dao Lords*; next are *Perfected Ones*, *Perfected Lords*, and *Perfected Ministers*. Among them are titles such as *Imperial Censor* and *Jade Gentleman*, with many official positions. Female Perfected are called *Primordial Ladies* or *Ladies*, their ranks comparable to *Immortal Lords*. Both male and female immortals take their governing domains as titles, all with left and right designations. Those titled *Supreme* are revered within their respective palaces. There are also the *Right Immortal Lord of Great Clarity*, the *Left Immortal Lord of Penglai*, the *Immortal Marquis of Great Ultimate*, the *Immortal Overseer*, *Immortal Gentleman*, and *Immortal Guest*.

The *Register of August People* states: From the Three Symbols’ radiant illumination to the accumulation of countless kalpas, the formation and dissolution of Heaven and Earth are beyond full recounting. The era of Tang Yao marks the end of a minor kalpa. After the *dinghai* year, in the *jiashen* year, the *yang* and *nine-six* qi converge and separate. At the beginning of *renchen*, the cycle completes nine revolutions. By the *gengzi* year, a red star appears in the east, and a white comet emerges from the Moon’s Grotto.

After Tang Yao, forty-six *dinghai* years mark a minor kalpa; after fifty-five *dinghai* years of the Zhou, reaching *renchen* and *guisi*, it becomes a great kalpa. When the Six Harmonies merge into oneness and the Two Ways wax and wane, the cyclical kalpa turns, and an immortal’s rank begins its first rotation.

The *Golden Root Lower Scripture* states: There are records of immortal ranks—advancement, demotion, promotion, and degradation—along with the rites of the *Jade Dawn* attendant immortals.

The *Register of Assembled Immortals* states: During the Later Han, Princess Nanyang descended to marry the Commandant-Esquire Wang Xian. The princess had long revered the supreme Dao. As the Han dynasty fell into chaos, she told Xian: "You must preserve yourself—only thus can you prolong life. If you idly follow the times, advancing and retreating with the world, I fear you will not escape the suffering of separation or the peril of pursuit." Xian, however, fixated on worldly gains, did not heed her words. The princess then entered Mount Huayin and departed forever. Xian followed her into the mountains but found no trace. Suddenly, on a ridge, he saw a pair of vermilion slippers. When he took them, they turned to stone, and the mountain was named Princess Peak.

It also states: Zhang Zhengli, at the end of the Han, studied the Dao on Mount Heng. He ingested yellow essence and received the *Rainbow Radiance Elixir* from the Lord of Western City. Troubled by the difficulty of obtaining the medicine, he traveled to Guangzhou as a Daoist, where he obtained both inner and outer *penetrating cinnabar* and cultivated the method of *guarding the One*. He ascended as an immortal.

The *Perfected Petition* states: Zhang Zhen of Nanjun, a scholar of the classics from youth, lived during the reign of King You of Zhou. He often sighed: "In this fleeting human life, each day brings us farther from our origin." He composed over a hundred scrolls of Daoist texts, mastering the Five Phases and expounding their subtleties, with nurturing life and curing illness as his guiding principles.

Later, he entered Kongtong Mountain and ascended as an immortal.

It is also said: Wang Yuan, styled Fangping, was a native of Donghai. He was recommended as a *Filial and Incorrupt* candidate and appointed Gentleman of the Palace, eventually rising to the rank of Grand Master for Palace Attendants. A man of vast learning, he was especially versed in the essentials of celestial patterns, apocryphal texts, and the *River Chart* and *Luo Scripture*, enabling him to foresee the rise and fall of the realm. When Emperor Huan of Han ascended the throne, he repeatedly summoned Wang, who refused to appear. The court then compelled local authorities to transport him to the capital by force, yet he remained silent, head bowed, uttering not a word. The emperor had him inscribe over four hundred characters on the palace gates, all foretelling future events. Displeased, the emperor sent him back to his hometown. There, Chen Dan, a former Grand Commandant of the same commandery, built a chamber for Fangping’s Daoist practice and served him day and night. Fangping remained in Chen’s household for over forty years. Later, he told Chen, "I shall depart." The next day at noon, he passed away. The following day, he was indeed dead. Realizing Fangping had ascended as an immortal, Chen lamented, "Master, you have left me."

It is also said: Yan Qing, a native of Kuaiji, was poor and often made charcoal in the mountains. One day, a man spoke with him, though Yan did not recognize him as an extraordinary person. Before parting, the stranger gave Yan a scroll, saying, "You are destined for longevity, so I entrust this to you. Keep it in a clean vessel and place it in a high location." Yan accepted it. Later, he mastered its arts and ascended as an immortal on Mount Huo.

It is also said: Zhang Ling, styled Fuhan, was a native of Feng in Peiguo. Originally a great Confucian scholar, he later studied the Dao of longevity and obtained the *Scripture of the Nine Cauldrons*. Hearing that Shu was rich in famous mountains, he entered Wuhu Mountain and composed over twenty scrolls of Daoist texts before ascending as an immortal.

It is also said: Zhao Guangxin, a native of Yangcheng, crossed the Yangtze during the late Wei period and entered Xiaobai Mountain in Shan. There, he studied the Dao and received the *Mysterious Center* teachings from Zuo Ci, along with the method of *penetrating vision*. After years of practice, he traveled through commanderies and states, sometimes selling medicine, though none recognized him. He often came to the capital to purchase cinnabar and refine the *Nine Radiance Elixir* before ascending as an immortal.

It is also said: Guo Jingshi, in the early Jin, studied the Dao in Jishan of Lujiang. He received oral instructions from Meng Deran and ingested black sesame and the *Mysterious Elixir* before ascending as an immortal.

It is also said: Zhao Bowei, a native of Dongjun, studied in his youth under Master Zhang of Handan and Ying. Later, on Mount Song, he received the *Scripture of the Jade Girdle and Golden Pendants*. After completing his cultivation, he ascended as an immortal and was placed in charge of the immortal registers, recording those who attained the Dao.

It is also said: Li Fanghui, a man of the Jin Emperor Wu’s reign, studied the Dao on Mount Hua. He received from Guan Chengzi the method of *steaming cinnabar and ingesting wood*, and later from Zhou Shouling of Sumen the *Cinnabar Radiance* technique. For fifty years, he cultivated purity of heart and inner vision before ascending as an immortal.

It is also said: Li Xiu composed forty scrolls titled *The Source of the Dao*. In his work, he wrote: "The weak can restrain the strong; yin can obscure yang. Always act as if treading over abysses or walking on rotten ice—such is the Dao of longevity." He lived to four hundred years with an unaging countenance before ascending as an immortal.

Liu Xiang’s *Biographies of the Immortals* states: Ma Shihuang was the horse master of the Yellow Emperor. Later, when horses fell ill, dragons emerged from the water to heal them. One day, he ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Wang Ziqiao, the Crown Prince Jin of King Ling of Zhou, was fond of playing the *sheng* pipe to mimic the cry of the phoenix. Master Fuqiu took him to Mount Song, where after thirty years he ascended as an immortal.

Ge Hong’s *Traditions of Divine Transcendents* states: Su Xiangong, named Lin and styled Zixuan, lived during the reign of King Wu of Zhou. His family resided by the Qu River in Puyang. Orphaned young, Lin was known for his benevolence and filial piety. Though poor and often tending cattle himself, upon attaining the Dao, whenever his mother craved fresh food, he would place a spoon in a vessel, take money, and depart—only for the food to appear. His mother said, "The nearest fish market is in Bian County, over a hundred *li* away. Are you deceiving me?" Xiangong knelt and replied, "I do not lie." The next day, her brother arrived and recounted seeing Xiangong at the Bian County market. Only then did she marvel at his divine powers. Later, he ascended as an immortal. A white crane alighted on the northeastern tower of the commandery city, scratching the floorboards with its talons as if writing in lacquer: "The city walls remain, but the people are not the same." To this day, the former residence of Xiangong still stands, much like that of Ding Lingwei.

It is further said: Shen Wentai, a native of Jiuyi, obtained the method of the *Crimson Spring Divine Elixir*, the *Earth Talisman* technique for reversing aging, and the *Way of Restoring Youth*. His ingestion of the elixir proved highly effective. Wishing to journey to Kunlun, he lingered for many years before transmitting the teachings to Li Wenyuan, saying, "Without removing the *Earth Talisman*, consuming elixirs and practicing the Dao will be of no benefit." Wenyuan thus received his esoteric instructions and later ascended as an immortal. Wentai also taught the method of boiling cinnabar in bamboo-root juice and the *Yellow Spirit* technique for expelling the *Three Corpses*.

It is further said: Shen Xi, a native of Wu Commandery, studied the Dao in Shu and could heal the sick, earning great gratitude and virtue. Later, he encountered a feather-robed emissary bearing a jade tablet inscribed with a blue-jade script, which he presented to Xi. Unable to decipher it, Xi looked away for a moment—only for a great fog to arise. When it cleared, the emissary had vanished. Xi returned home and later ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Chen Anshi, a native of Jingzhao, worked as a hired laborer for Guan Shuben. Naturally kind and benevolent, he served Shuben, who was fond of the Dao. Two Daoists, posing as scholars, accompanied Shuben to observe and test him. Unaware of their true nature, Shuben grew increasingly negligent toward them. The scholars then asked Anshi, "Do you desire the Dao?" He replied, "I have no means to know of it." They said, "If you truly desire the Dao, meet us tomorrow at dawn beneath the great tree north of the road." Anshi agreed and arrived early, but saw no one. "Have the scholars deceived me?" he wondered. After three appointments, he arrived early once more, and they bestowed upon him an elixir. Later, he ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Wu Mu, a native of Chang’an, served as a minor county clerk in his youth, overseeing cases and extorting the people. When the people sued him, he fled into the mountains and forests. Starving for days, he came upon a stone chamber where he met Master Sun, who instructed him to cultivate millet and sesame, sweep, and perform menial tasks. After four years, the master transmitted the Dao to him. Later, he ingested an elixir and ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Dong Weinian, of unknown origin, dwelled in the White Community of Luoyang during the late reign of Emperor Wu of Jin. He slept on bare earth, his clothes tattered, and often swallowed a stone, going days without food. Sometimes he begged for work in the marketplace, and though people observed him, he never spoke. Occasionally, he composed poems, but none knew his ultimate fate.

It is further said: Xiao Shi, a man of the time of Duke Mu of Qin, was skilled in playing the xiao flute and could summon peacocks and white magpies. The duke’s daughter, named Nongyu, favored him, and he was given her in marriage. Thereupon, he taught Nongyu to mimic the cry of the phoenix. After more than ten years, phoenixes came and alighted, and the duke built the Phoenix Terrace where the couple resided. After several years, they ascended as immortals. Thus, the people of Qin built the Phoenix Maiden Shrine in the Yong Palace, and the sound of the xiao flute has endured through the ages.

It is further said: The Master of the Riverbank—his name and origins unknown—during the reign of Emperor Jing of Han, built a thatched hut by the river. The emperor, reading the *Laozi*, admired its words but found some passages unclear. Hearing of the master, he sent to inquire. The master presented two scrolls of plain silk to the emperor, saying: "Read these to resolve your doubts, but do not show them to the unworthy." Later, the master ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Huang Ziyang, from his youth, knew the Dao of longevity. He secluded himself in Mount Boluo for over ninety years, eating only peaches and drinking from stone springs. Later, he encountered Sima Jizhu, who transmitted to him the *Eightfold Guidance to Immortality*. Thereupon, he transcended the world and ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Master Wang, a native of Yangcheng, dwelled in Hugu Valley, unaware of the passage of time. When Emperor Wu of Han ascended Mount Song, Dongfang Shuo and others accompanied him. Suddenly, they saw a divine being over ten feet tall. The emperor bowed in reverence and asked him who he was. The being replied: "I am a man of Mount Jiuyi. Hearing that the Central Marchmount bears stone calamus, an inch long with nine joints, which grants longevity when eaten, I have come to gather it." Suddenly, the divine being vanished. The emperor then gathered and ingested it.

The emperor, troubled by internal heat and vexation, had his attendants all ingest it, and they too gained prolonged vitality. Only Master Wang, having heard the divine being’s instruction to consume it, gathered and ate it, then ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Liu Gen, styled Jun’an, was a native of Chang’an in Jingzhao. Well-versed in the Five Classics from youth, he lived during the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han. He entered the precipitous stone chambers of Mount Song and once declared: "The supreme medicines include the nine-times-cycled Returning Elixir and the Golden Liquid of the Great One; next are substances like mica and realgar, which also confer longevity. Below these are the herbal medicines, which cure illness and replenish qi. At best, they may extend life by several centuries; at least, they preserve one’s innate endowment. If one truly seeks immortality, one must first stabilize the mind and will, eliminate desires, and only then may receive the divine formula of the *Five-Colored Root Scrolls*." Later, he entered Cock’s Head Mountain and ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Yin Changsheng, a native of Xinye, was a kinsman of Empress Yin of the Later Han. Though born into wealth and nobility, he disdained worldly glory. Learning that Ma Mingsheng had attained the arts of transcending the world, he sought him out. Upon meeting, he served him with the reverence of a charioteer. For over a decade, he never wavered. Mingsheng said: "You have truly attained the Dao." He then entered Mount Qingcheng and transmitted to him the *Scripture of the Great Clarity Divine Elixir*. After taking leave, Yin later ascended as an immortal on Mount Pingdu.

The *Fengsu Tong* states: During the reign of Emperor Ming of Han, the Palace Secretary Wang Qiao served as Magistrate of Ye. Each month on the first day, he would appear at court. The emperor, knowing he arrived without carriage or escort, secretly ordered the court astronomers to observe him.

When Wang Qiao was about to depart this world, a pair of cranes would always arrive from the southeast. The court astronomers, seeing them as wild ducks, cast their nets and caught a single shoe. Upon presenting it to the Imperial Workshop for identification, it was recognized as the official footwear issued to the Palace Secretary four years prior. Each time Wang attended court, the drum at the gate of Ye would sound without being struck, its resonance heard throughout the capital. Later, a jade coffin descended from the heavens before the hall. Wang declared, "The Heavenly Emperor summons me." He bathed, lay within the coffin, and the lid sealed itself. He was buried east of the city, where the earth formed his tomb. The people established a shrine in his honor, known as the Shrine of Lord Ye.

The *Three Caverns Pearl Bag* states: Hu Gong Xie Yuan, a native of Liyang, sold medicines in the market at a fixed price, curing all who sought his remedies. He would tell his patients, "After taking this medicine, you will vomit such-and-such a thing, and you will recover on such-and-such a day." His words never failed. Daily, he amassed tens of thousands of coins, which he distributed to the poor and destitute in the marketplace. Fei Changfang, the magistrate of the market, recognized his extraordinary nature. Later, Changfang visited Hu Gong, who took him away and transmitted the arts of healing before sending him back. Lord Shi Ya later ascended as an immortal. Dai Gongbai possessed over ten scrolls of the *Yellow Writ of the Grand Tenuity*, which had been passed down from Hu Gong’s master.

It is further said: Yue Zichang, a native of Qi, was devoted to the Dao from youth. He traveled to Mount Huolin, where he ingested the *Red Pine Powder of Giant Sesame* and eventually departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Wei Shuqing, a native of Zhongshan, consumed mica. His son, Du Shi, entered the mountains and encountered his father. Shuqing instructed him, "In the northwest corner of my study, beneath the great pillar, lies a jade casket containing a scripture. Retrieve it and follow its instructions." Du Shi returned home and found it exactly as described. After ingesting the five-colored mica, he ascended as an immortal.

It is further said: Wei Boyang, a native of Wu, was devoted to the Dao and refused official service, sealing himself away to cultivate his lofty aspirations. Later, he entered the mountains, ingested the divine elixir, and departed as an immortal. He composed the *Triplex Unity*, which expounds the principles of elixir-making through the hexagrams of the *Book of Changes*. Yet the world, unaware of the divine elixir’s true nature, often interprets it through yin-yang theories, entirely missing its essence.

It is further said: Yin Gui, styled Gongdu, was a native of Taiyuan. Well-versed in all manner of texts, he turned to the Dao in his later years and regularly consumed Solomon’s seal. Though he lived over a hundred years, his predictions of the world’s rise and fall, safety and peril, fortune and misfortune never failed to prove accurate. He later entered Mount Taihe and departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Dongguo Yannian, a native of Shanyang, ingested the *Flying Spirit Powder* and could write in the dark of night. His body emitted a radiance that illuminated small objects, revealing their colors. One day, dozens of men riding tigers and leopards arrived to welcome him. Yannian then journeyed to Mount Kunlun and departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Wang Zhen, a native of Shangdang, began his Daoist studies at seventy-nine. He walked with such ease that he seemed to fly, possessing the strength of many men. You Yuanjie served Zhen for over a decade. Zhen transmitted to him the method of steaming and ingesting the minor elixir, and Yuanjie’s appearance never aged. The villagers estimated Zhen’s age to be over four hundred years. Later, he ascended Mount Nüji and departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Ping Zhongjie, a native of Hedong, withdrew to Mount Cangwu during the Jin dynasty when the Jie Hu disrupted China. There, he received the *Preserving the Mind* teachings from Master Song. After forty-five years of unwavering devotion, his body became suffused with true qi, and he later departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Ge Xuan was skilled in transformation but careless in his personal conduct. Initially residing on Mount Chang, he later moved near Mount Gaizhu. Though capable of riding tigers and commanding spirits, he had yet to receive an immortal office. He often kept company with Xie Zhijian, Huang Ziyang, and Guo Shengzi. Ge Xuan was the great-uncle of the *Master Embracing Simplicity* and the disciple of Zheng Siyuan. His whereabouts were unknown to his contemporaries, though it was said that immortals in the Eastern Sea sent him letters, addressing him as "Immortal Lord."

It is further said: Lu Miaodian, a female Daoist from Mount Jiuyi, was devoted to the Dao from birth. One day, she suddenly told her mother, "Among those who attain the upper limits of human longevity, few truly succeed. Joy and sorrow, grief and delight—these daily harms are nothing compared to burying one’s true nature and drowning in the mundane stream." A Daoist passing by her home transmitted to her the *Yellow Court Scripture of the Great Cavern* and said, "The trouble is that people cannot know, and even if they know, they cannot cultivate; even if they cultivate, they cannot refine; even if they refine, they cannot persist. Not only will they incur the penalties of the celestial statutes, but they will also suffer endless retribution." Miaodian heeded his words and entered Mount Jiuyi, where she endured countless demonic trials without wavering. On the mountain, a stone basin held an inexhaustible spring, and a great iron mortar appeared, its origin unknown. Both remain on the mountain’s stone altar, alongside the unmistakable imprints of an immortal’s shoes and an ancient mirror, three feet wide. A crescent-shaped ancient bell is housed in the Wuwei Abbey. Miaodian later departed as an immortal.

It is further said: Xie Ziran, a female Daoist from Guozhou, possessed an extraordinary demeanor. Her family lived at the foot of Mount Dafang, whose summit bore an ancient statue of Lord Lao. Ziran prostrated herself before it and refused to descend the mountain. Her mother followed her, and they moved to the mountaintop. Thereafter, Ziran constantly recited the *Scripture of the Dao and Its Virtue* and the *Inner Chapters of the Yellow Court*. At the Kaiyuan Abbey, she received the *Purple Void Treasure Tallies* and resided on Mount Jinquan. The mountain featured a stone altar surrounded by misty bamboo groves. For thirteen years, she remained awake day and night, until two seals appeared on her knees, slightly smaller than an official’s seal, their four edges crimson and inscribed with six ancient characters resembling white jade. Suddenly, clouds enveloped the Jinquan sanctuary, lingering over the valley for a long while. She then departed as an immortal.

The *Inscription on the Jinquan Stele* states: In the heavens stands the White Jade Hall, its walls inscribed with the names of lofty immortals and perfected beings, much like the records on mortal walls. At times, vermilion script appears beneath their names, noting: "Descended to the world to serve as such-and-such an official or post." Ziran also inscribed several characters on the eastern wall of her dwelling, all conveying the essence of the Dao. The original calligraphy remains.

It further states: Wang Fengxian was a girl from a common family in Dangtu County, Xuanzhou. Having attained the Dao, she often expounded to others on the principles of loyalty, filial piety, integrity, and uprightness, as well as the teachings of purity, detachment, frugality, and restraint—essential instructions for cultivating the self and practicing hidden virtue. Thus, people near and far revered her, offering gold and jade in abundance, though she turned away without a glance. Later, she entered Dongting Mountain and departed as an immortal without illness. Auspicious signs of clouds, cranes, and rare fragrances accompanied her ascension.

**End of Scroll Four of the Daoist Canon**
**Scroll Five: Earthbound Immortals**

The *Records of the Grand Historian* states: Penglai, Fangzhang, and Yingzhou lie within the Bohai Sea to the east, not far from humanity. Many have reached them, for they are home to various immortals and wondrous medicines. Their creatures and beasts are all white; from afar, the islands appear like clouds.

The *Esoteric Essentials Scripture* states: By accomplishing three hundred virtuous deeds, one may attain the state of an earthbound immortal, dwelling within the grotto-palaces of the Five Sacred Mountains.

The *Baopuzi* states: Peng Zu remarked that in the heavens, many exalted officials and newly ascended immortals hold lowly ranks, serving numerous superiors—only to find their labors ever more arduous. Thus, they do not urgently seek celestial ascent but remain among mortals for eight hundred years.

The *Accounts of Anomalies* states: Atop Mount Lu stand three stone beams, each dozens of yards long yet scarcely a foot wide. Gazing down, one sees only an abyssal void. During the Xiankang era of the Jin, Jiangzhou Governor Yu Liang invited Wu Meng and his disciples to ascend the mountain for sightseeing. Passing over one of the beams, they saw an old man seated beneath an osmanthus tree, holding a jade bowl to catch sweet dew, which he shared with Meng, who in turn distributed it among his disciples. Proceeding further, they came upon towering terraces and vast halls, their chambers adorned with gold and jade, their utensils beyond recognition. Speaking with Meng, the old man seemed as familiar as if they had long shared jade paste for days on end.

The *Annals of Master Pei* states: The Western Mystery’s Three Caverns span a thousand *li*, and on the Western Mountains stand two palaces—one for citrons, one for pomelos—encircled by ninefold golden walls. Hidden passageways tunnel through the caverns, linking to the Mystic Continent and Kunlun, realms beyond mortal reach. Master Pei and Master Zhou each dwell within.

The *Illustrated Register of the Five Peaks* records: The cavern of Mount Qingcheng spans two thousand *li*, lying within Shu Commandery, where the Yellow Emperor paid homage to the Five Peaks’ Venerable Lord. The *Records of Famous Mountains* further notes: To the north it adjoins Mount Bozhong, to the south Mount Emei, and to the east it extends to Chengdu, its ridges resembling a walled city. The mountain bears a crimson cliff, where Celestial Master Zhang once resided; his traces remain to this day.

The *Biography of Lady Wei* recounts: The cavern of Red City’s Cinnabar Mountain spans three hundred *li*, where the roots of the sun and moon’s staffs reside, their three luminaries’ radiance illuminating the depths. The *Illustrated Register of the Five Peaks* states: This mountain lies in Luojiang of Kuaiji, its northwest holding Red City. According to the *Annals of Master Mao*, the Director of Destinies of Huolin governs the Jade Cavern Palace of Red City’s Cinnabar Mountain. During the Yongming era of the Qi, a vast flock of pigeons suddenly arrived from the northwest, descending upon Huomen Stream. The valley filled for miles, trampled underfoot as if startled by some unseen force. By nightfall, they flew back toward the northwest—likely creatures from the Celestial Springs Lake of Red City’s Upper Capital.

Mount Luofu’s cavern spans five hundred *li*; the *True Records* calls it the Tiered City. Ge Hong sojourned here in distant Jiaozhou before attaining transformation. The *Annals of Master Mao* states: The cavern of Mount Gouqu spans one hundred fifty *li*. In Qin times, it was known as the Altar of Goujin. During the Han, the Three Mao Lords attained the Dao and came to govern this mountain.

The *Five Talismans* records: Mount Linwu spans four hundred *li*, also named Baoshan, situated within Lake Tai. Beneath it lies a cavern secretly connecting the Five Peaks, called the Heavenly Queen’s Separate Palace. After Yu the Great tamed the floods, he concealed the Five Talismans here. King Helü of Wu once dispatched the Dragon Might Elder into the mountain to retrieve them.

The *True Records* states: Beneath Baoshan lie stone chambers and silver halls, a hundred *li* in circumference. There are also hidden springs of white mushrooms, their waters purple-hued. It further notes: The cavern of Chengyu Mountain spans three thousand *li*. The Director of Destinies of Zhou once resided in Mount Heng before the Jade Maiden of the Supreme Mystery instructed him to journey to the Western City’s Master Wang. He went, and this was the mountain. It also says: Within the depths of the Profound Sustainer, there are thirty-six grotto-heavens. Beyond the Eight Seas, other mountains likewise hold cavern-palaces—some a thousand *li* or five hundred *li* in scale, not counted among the thirty-six grotto-heavens. The Five Peaks and famous mountains all possess cavern-palaces, some thirty or twenty *li* in extent, serving as abodes for immortals and transcending the tally of lesser heavens.

The *Records of Famous Mountains* states: The cavern of the Peak Grotto spans a hundred *li*, nestled in the tranquility of Zhongnan’s Great Unity. Some call it the Cassia Sun Palace, rich in numinous wonders. Mount Wangwu’s cavern winds ten thousand *li*, named the Lesser Heaven of Pure Emptiness. According to the *Inner Annals of Master Wang*, it lies within Qinshui County of Henan, the source of the Ji River. To the north stands Mount Taihang, to the southeast Mount Song, and within its cavern-heaven’s mouth, the sun, moon, stars, clouds, flora, and myriad beings differ not from the mortal world. Palaces and towers gleam in reflection, adorned with gold and jade carvings—all dwellings of earthbound immortals, the abode of Lord Wang of Pure Emptiness.

The *True Records* states: These are the so-called Sunlight Terraces of the various heavens, where all who attain the Dao gather. Mount Weiyu rises from the sea, the dwelling of Sima Jizhu. It further notes: The cavern of Mount Kuocang spans three hundred *li*, an auxiliary to the Eastern Peak’s mandate. Located southeast of Kuaiji, it is a haunt of the host of emperors. The mountain teems with divine marvels, and its Hall of Crimson Clouds stands as a solitary peak, its cliffs and ridges towering above all others. Atop the solitary height of Maoxuan Ridge, the Director of Destinies buried six thousand *jin* of cinnabar, two *zhang* deep, sealed with a slab of stone. The springs on either side of the mountain run faintly crimson; those who drink from them attain longevity. The Heavenly Emperor’s Altar of Mount Mao stands precisely at the cavern-heaven’s center, above the Mystic Window. Long ago, the Azure Lad of the Eastern Sea rode his wind-borne flying wheel chariot to inspect the grotto-heaven and once came here.

Liu Xiang’s *Biographies of the Immortals* states: Red Pine, the rain master of Shen Nong’s time, ingested water jade. Ascending Mount Kunlun, he often lingered in the Western Queen Mother’s stone chamber, rising and falling with the winds and rains before ascending as an immortal. It further records: Yu Quan of Mount Huai was the Herb-Gathering Elder, fond of eating pine nuts. His body grew fur, his eyes square pupils, and he could fly. It also notes: Master Guangcheng was an ancient immortal dwelling in a stone chamber on Mount Kongtong. When the Yellow Emperor heard of him and sought him out to inquire into the essentials of the Dao, Master Guangcheng said: “You govern the world, yet clouds fly without waiting to gather, and plants wither without waiting to yellow. How can you speak of the supreme Dao?” The Yellow Emperor withdrew and fasted for three days before bowing in obeisance to the wind. Master Guangcheng then said: “The essence of the supreme Dao is dim and obscure; see nothing, hear nothing, embrace the spirit in stillness. The body will right itself—you must be serene, must be pure. I shall depart through the Gate of the Boundless and wander the Wilds of the Infinite.”

It further states: The Master of White Stone was a disciple of the Central Yellow Daoist. He often boiled white stones for sustenance, hence dwelling on White Stone Mountain. He also ate dried meats, drank wine, and consumed grains. He could walk three to four hundred *li* a day without his appearance aging. It also records: The Lord of Yellow Mountain cultivated the arts of Peng Zu and, at over a hundred years old, retained a youthful countenance. After Peng Zu departed, he compiled his teachings into a scripture. It further notes: The *Scripture of the Six Jia of Supreme Purity* states: Song Xuande was a man of King Xuan of Zhou’s time. He ingested the Six Jia Spirit-Flight Talismans, attained the Dao of true numina, and dwelled on Mount Song. It also says: Li Yiqí was a man of Shu. He was often seen in the world.

Yan Dao practiced his arts among the people, dwelling in a cave at the corner of the city walls of Shu. When Liu Bei sought to march east to avenge Guan Yu’s grievance against Wu, he summoned Yiqi and held him in great esteem. Asked about the campaign against Wu, Yiqi did not speak but instead requested paper, upon which he drew tens of thousands of soldiers, horses, and weapons, then tore them all to pieces. He also drew an official, dug a pit, and buried it, then departed without another word. Liu Bei was displeased. Later, as foretold, his forces were crushed by Wu, suffering a catastrophic defeat—of over a hundred thousand men, only a few hundred returned, their armor, weapons, and supplies nearly all lost. Liu Bei fell ill with rage and grief, dying at the Palace of Eternal Peace. Yiqi spoke little; when questioned, he gave no answer. If people of Shu came to him with worries, he would say: "Fortune and misfortune follow their own signs—simply observe whether their countenance is gloomy or joyful." Later, he entered Mount Langye and was never seen again.

It further states: Feng Junda, a man of Longxi, consumed yellow essence for over fifty years. He entered Wushu Mountain, where he refined his practice for over a century, occasionally returning to his hometown. He often rode a black ox, dispensing medicine to cure the sick, and was known only as the Black Ox Daoist. When locals asked how long he had lived, he would not answer. Later, he entered Tiger Hill Mountain and ascended as an immortal.

It also says: Wang Zhongdu was a man of the Western Han. From his youth, he cultivated the Dao and practiced filial piety under Emperor Wen. On a bitterly cold day, he ordered Zhongdu to ride alone in a chariot drawn by four horses through the Shanglin and Kunming parks, circling the lakes at full speed. The charioteer, clad in fox fur, shivered violently, nearly freezing to death, while Zhongdu’s complexion remained unchanged, his body warm and his qi radiant as flame. In the height of summer, when surrounded by raging fire, his body did not sweat. Later, his whereabouts became unknown.

It further records: There was a man called Jiqiugong, a Daoist of Mount Tai. When Emperor Wu of Han made his eastern inspection and reached Mount Tai, Jiqiugong came to greet him, wearing a *zhangfu* cap and yellow robes, holding a zither. He said: "Your Majesty, do not ascend the mountain, lest you harm your feet." The emperor insisted, but after climbing a few *li*, his feet indeed grew sore, just as predicted—though he concealed it. Thus, he merely performed the sacrifices and returned, ordering a shrine built for Jiqiugong and assigning a hundred households to serve it.

It also says: Dai Meng, originally surnamed Yan, named Ji, styled Zhongwei, lived during the reign of Emperor Ming of Han. He entered Mount Hua and Mount Wudang, where he received the *Jade Pendant Scripture of the Golden Seal* and the *Stone Essence Golden Light Talisman* from Master Pei. He also obtained the *Yellow Writ of the Grand Tenuity*, enabling him to traverse the famous mountains.

It further states: Zuo Ci, styled Yuanfang, was a man of Lujiang. Well-versed in the Five Classics and astronomy, he saw the Han dynasty’s decline and devoted himself to Daoist cultivation on Mount Tianzhu, where he obtained the *Nine Elixirs Golden Liquid Scripture* from a stone chamber—a method of the Grand Purity. His teacher was Li Zhongfu. Later, Ge Xuan became his disciple. When Cao Cao heard of him, he summoned Ci and asked about his Daoist studies. Ci did not answer, enraging Cao, who sought to kill him. A feast was prepared, but Ci suddenly vanished. At the end of the Jian’an era, he crossed the Yangtze, seeking mountains and entering grottoes. He dwelled on Mount Xiaokuo, his complexion radiant.

It also says: Wang Yao, styled Boliao, was a man of Poyang. He often healed the sick, and all recovered. Yao possessed a small box, several inches long, and one of his disciples, surnamed Qian, followed him for over a decade without ever seeing it opened. One evening, as rain fell and darkness deepened, Yao instructed Qian to carry the box on a nine-jointed staff, and they set out on a path they had never traveled before. After journeying over ten *li*, they ascended a small hill and entered a stone chamber. Two men were already there. When Yao arrived, they took the box, opened it, and removed three five-tongued bamboo flutes. Each played one for a long while, then returned them to the box. They bade farewell to the men in the chamber, and upon returning home, Yao donned a single-layered *fenge* robe, carried the bamboo box himself, and departed, never to return. Thirty years later, his disciple saw Yao beneath Mount Mati, his appearance even younger—he was evidently an earthbound immortal.

It further states: Chen Zihuang, a man of Jiyin, obtained a recipe for *zhu* (atractylodes) and consumed it, ceasing to eat grain. Initially over seventy and frail, after taking the elixir, he grew youthful again. He lived among the people for many years before entering Mount Huo and departing.

It also says: Ge Hong, styled Zhichuan, was a man of Langye. He disdained honors and titles, living in seclusion. Devoted to the arts of immortals and Daoist techniques, he seldom socialized. On Mount Yuhang, he encountered He Duodao and Guo Wenju, exchanging glances but no words. His great-uncle, Ge Xuan, had achieved immortality in the Wu era and transmitted his alchemical methods to his disciple Zheng Yin, styled Siyuan. Hong studied under Yin and mastered all his teachings.

The *Biographies of Daoist Scholars* states: Bao Jing, styled Taixuan, was walking toward the capital on the twentieth day of the eighth month in the first year of the Taixing era. As he reached Dragon Mountain, he saw a youth ahead, handsome and dignified, walking swiftly despite traveling on foot. Jing secretly followed for several *li* but could not catch up, finding it most strange. He asked: "Sir, you seem to be one who has attained the Dao." The youth replied: "I am Yin Changsheng of Zhongshan."

It further says: Jie Xiang, styled Yuanze, was a man of Kuaiji. Proficient in the Five Classics and skilled in composition, he later pursued the Dao. Hearing of the *Scripture of the Returned Elixir*, he searched the world for it in vain. His teacher then entered the mountains to meditate deeply and encountered a man who bestowed the *Scripture of the Returned Elixir* upon him, saying: "Attain this, and you will become an immortal—do nothing else." Xiang took his leave and returned. Once, he visited his disciple Luo Yanya’s dwelling. In the main hall, scholars were debating the meaning of the *Zuozhuan*, their arguments unresolved. Xiang overheard and clarified the matter. The scholars, realizing he was no ordinary man, secretly memorialized the Wu ruler to recommend him. Xiang wished to leave, but the Wu ruler summoned him to Wuchang, holding him in great esteem and addressing him as "Master Jie." He was granted a residence, furnishings, and a thousand *jin* of gold. Later, Xiang claimed illness and died in an instant.

The imperial decree ordered his burial and the construction of a temple in his honor. Whenever the Master personally conducted sacrifices, white cranes would alight upon his seat, lingering before departing.

It is further said: Li Gen, styled Zice, was a native of Xuchang. Formerly, he visited the household of Wu Taiwen in Shouchun, where disciples, knowing of his Daoist arts, secretly observed his belongings and found a scroll of the *Plain Book*, in which he had recorded his study of the Dao and the days of his medicinal regimen. Taiwen also recounted that Gen had learned from Tongzifang, though Gen was but an earthbound immortal.

It is further said: Boshanfu was a man of Yongzhou. He entered the Hua Mountains and remained there for two hundred years without visiting human dwellings. He could recount the good and evil deeds, merits and faults of one’s ancestors as if witnessing them firsthand, and he knew the fortunes and misfortunes yet to come.

It is further said: Liu Zheng, a native of Pei, was a man of lofty talent and vast learning, ever seeking out rare and wondrous knowledge. If another surpassed him, even a servant or slave, he would take them as his teacher. He pursued the arts of nourishing life and ingested elixirs, living over four hundred years.

It is further said: Wang Lie, styled Changxiu, was a man of Handan. He regularly consumed yellow essence and lead, living over two hundred years. His steps were as swift as flight, and he had mastered all manner of texts. Ji Kang held him in great esteem and often studied with him. Together, they entered the Taihang Mountains and saw a fissure in the earth from which flowed a green stone marrow. Lie gathered the marrow, shaping it into pellets that resembled grains of rice in texture and taste. He carried some back, intending to gift it to Kang, but upon inspection, it had turned to green stone. When struck, it rang clear. Kang then accompanied him to the site, only to find the mountain restored as before. Lie later entered the Baodu Mountains in Hedong, where he discovered a stone chamber containing a stone shelf. Upon the shelf lay two scrolls of the *Plain Book*, its characters unknown. He memorized several dozen and showed them to Kang, who recognized them all. Delighted, Lie returned with Kang to read the text, but upon arrival, the stone chamber had vanished. Lie whispered to his disciples: "Shuye [Kang] has come to attain the Dao." According to the *Scriptures of Divine Immortals*, every five hundred years, mountains open once, and their stone marrow emerges. Those who obtain and consume it gain long life. Later, none knew where Lie had gone.

It is further said: Bu Zheng, styled Xuanzhen, was a native of Badong.

In his accounts of Qin Shi Huang’s reign, events unfolded as if before one’s very eyes. At the end of the Han, he led dozens of disciples into Wu, teaching them the methods of absorbing qi, refining stone marrow, and the minor elixir arts. He lived to the age of four hundred.

It is further said: Jiao Guang, styled Xiaoran, was a native of Hedong. He regularly consumed white stones, boiled until soft as taro. Often entering the mountains to gather firewood, he would carry bundles to give to others. When Wei received the abdication, he took leave of his acquaintances and departed, his whereabouts unknown.

It is further said: Sun Deng, of uncertain origin, often dwelled at the mountain gate, sitting in an earthen hollow while playing the zither and reciting the *Book of Changes*. In winter, he wore only a single garment, yet when the weather grew bitterly cold, observers saw his hair—over ten feet long—cascading down to cover his body. Though generations passed, his countenance remained unchanged. He possessed no other belongings and did not eat. When Yang Jun served as Grand Tutor, he sent for Sun Deng, who answered none of his questions. Yang Jun then presented him with a cloth robe, but upon leaving, Sun Deng borrowed a knife, cut the robe in two, and placed the separate halves at Yang Jun’s gate, foretelling his impending execution. At the time, Ji Kang of Kuaiji once visited Sun Deng, who refused to speak with him. Ji Kang then posed challenging questions, but Sun Deng continued playing his zither, unperturbed. After a long while, Ji Kang departed. Sun Deng remarked: "Ji Kang’s talent is great, yet his wisdom is shallow—he lacks the means to preserve himself."

It is further said: Bo He, styled Zhongli, was a native of Liaodong. He entered the Earth Lung Mountains to study under Dong Feng.

Dong Feng transmitted to him the method of circulating qi and consuming wood essence, saying to Bo He: "My Dao ends here. Without the divine elixir or golden cinnabar, I cannot wander the world without restriction. You are still young and strong—broaden your search."

Bo He then traveled to West City Mountain to study under Master Wang. The Master taught Bo He the *Great Dao Formula*, saying: "Within this mountain’s stone chamber, gaze intently at the northern wall. When you see writing upon it, you will attain the Dao." After three years of gazing, Bo He finally discerned the characters—ancient inscriptions carved by those who came before. They were the *Divine Elixir Formula of the Great Clarity Central Scripture*, the celestial writings of the Three Sovereigns in large script, and the *True Forms of the Five Peaks*, all etched into the stone. Bo He recited the ten thousand words, but where their meaning eluded him, Master Wang imparted the secret: "To become an earthbound immortal, go to Linlü Mountain."

It is further said: Gong Song, a native of Langye, was learned in literature and authored two hundred scrolls of Daoist texts. By ingesting mica, he became an earthbound immortal.

It is also said: Li Changzai of Shu Commandery devoted himself to the Dao from youth. He was often seen at the foot of Tiger Longevity Mountain. Tao Qian’s *Record of the Peach Blossom Spring* states: During the Tai Kang era of the Jin, a fisherman from Wuling followed a stream, losing track of distance. Suddenly, he came upon a grove of peach blossoms, their fragrant petals lining the banks in vivid splendor, scattered petals drifting like confetti. When the grove ended, he found a mountain with a small opening so narrow at first that only after four or five steps did it suddenly open into a vast expanse. Houses stood in rows, the sounds of chickens and dogs carried through the air, and the clothing of men and women was no different from that of the outside world. Seeing the fisherman, they were startled but prepared wine and food for him. They explained that their ancestors had fled the turmoil of the Qin, bringing their families here, and had since remained cut off from the outside. When asked what era it was, they knew nothing of the Han, Wei, or Jin. After leaving, the fisherman reported this to the prefect, who sent men to follow him back, but they became lost and could not find the place again.

*The Declarations of the Perfected* states: Liu Ping of Pei studied the Dao under Ji Qiuzi and regularly ingested quartz. Though over three hundred years old, he retained a youthful appearance. Once in Chang’an, nobles who heard of his mastery came to pay their respects. Over a hundred people followed him, and when he encountered bandits, he admonished them: "You call yourselves men, yet your hearts are like wolves. Teaching one another to block roads, endangering others for your own gain—this is the way of corpses piled in the marketplace, flesh fed to crows and kites." One bandit suddenly prostrated himself in terror and fled. Later, Liu Ping entered Mount Taibai and, after decades, returned to his hometown with an even more youthful countenance.

It is also said: Yin Si, styled Shaolong, was a native of Anding. On the night of the fifteenth day of the first month in the fifth year of Yuan Kang of the Jin, he sat in his house and sent his son to observe the moon for anything unusual. His brother reported: "There will soon be a great flood. I see a man in the moon wearing a raincoat and bearing a sword." Yin Si looked for himself and said: "The man in the moon wields a sword and crouches with a spear—great chaos is coming. After thirty years, there will be a brief respite." Later, Yin Si vanished without a trace.

It is further said: Huang Chuping of Danxi was fifteen when his family sent him to herd sheep. A Daoist, seeing his sincerity, took him to a stone chamber in Mount Jinhua, where he remained for over forty years, never once thinking of home. His elder brother, Huang Chuqi, searched for him for years until he met a Daoist in the marketplace who told him where to find him. Chuqi followed the Daoist and was finally reunited with his brother.

Upon finishing their conversation, Chuqi asked where the sheep were. Chuping replied, "They are nearby to the east." Chuqi went to look and saw only white stones. Chuping then went and shouted at the stones, which transformed into tens of thousands of sheep. Realizing his brother had attained the Daoist Way, Chuqi rushed home to join him in consuming pine resin and fuling, living thus for five hundred years. Chuping changed his name to Master Red Pine, while Chuqi took the name Red Lu Ban.

It is further said: Lü Gong, styled Wenjing, was gathering herbs in the Taihang Mountains when he suddenly encountered someone who bestowed upon him an immortal formula. Having attained the Way, he sent Gong away, saying, "You may now visit your hometown." Later, when Lü Xi, a descendant of Gong, became a Daoist, the people revered and served him. Gong’s message reached Xi’s home, and upon knocking at the door to inquire, a servant came out and asked where he had come from. Gong replied, "This is my home." Xi, hearing this, rushed out in joy and bowed. Gong then transmitted the divine formula to Xi before departing. Xi was already eighty years old at the time, but after consuming the formula, he regained his youth. He lived to two hundred years before entering the mountains, and his descendants never aged thereafter.

It is further said: Shen Jian of Danyang came from a family of officials. Fond of the Dao and unwilling to serve in office, he studied the arts of consuming elixirs and dietary regimens. He could heal illnesses and move swiftly, sometimes vanishing and returning. After over three hundred years of this, he disappeared without a trace.

It is further said: Xu Yuanyou’s third son, named Kou, styled Xiang, and known in childhood as Wangfu, abandoned worldly affairs and dwelled at the foot of Mount Leiping, diligently cultivating his practice. He often wished to journey early to the grotto heavens and had no desire to linger long in the mortal world.

He then journeyed to the Northern Grotto. In the sixth year of Taihe of the Liang dynasty, at his former residence on Mount Mao, he passed away at the age of thirty. Thereafter, he dwelled in the square halls of the mountain grottoes, often coming and going from the Four-Square Terrace. Later, he ascended as a Perfected Immortal of the Highest Clarity.

It is further said: Ma Mingsheng of Linzi served as a county clerk. While pursuing bandits, he was wounded, but encountered the Grand Perfected, who healed him with a divine pellet. Later, he became a disciple of Anqisheng and received the Great Clarity elixir. He lived in the world for five hundred years before departing in the Guanghe era of Emperor Ling of the Han.

*The Records of Immortals Gathered* states: Yang Ping, whose original name is unknown, dwelled on Mount Yangping and possessed many arts of transformation. When asked, he would say, "I am but an immortal of the Yangping Grotto." He claimed that on the three great festivals of the Three Primes each year, the perfected immortals of the heavens would descend to roam the grotto-heavens, observing the good and evil of the world, the life and death of mortals, the rise and fall of states, and the occurrence of floods, droughts, winds, and rains—all of which were reported in advance within the grottoes. The dragon spirits and the deities of temples that received blood sacrifices were all governed by the grotto-fiefdoms. The immortal bureaus within the grottoes were like the prefectures, counties, and villages of the mortal world—too numerous to record in detail. Having spoken, he departed. Here ends the fifth section of the Daoist Canon.

**Section Six: Liberation Through Corpse Transformation**

*The Transmission of the Perfected King of Xicheng* states: The Way of transformation through liberation is not one where the corpse fails to accompany the spirit in metamorphosis.

*The Upper Scripture of the Precious Sword* says: The methods of corpse liberation include those who die and then revive; those whose heads are severed yet emerge from another side; and those whose forms remain but whose bones vanish. It further states: Corpse liberation is the refining and shedding of one’s original true form, the hidden departure of the five constituents. Though it ranks among the lower grades of immortality, the endowment it confers is not insignificant. It is what is meant by "concealing the three luminaries" and "sinking into the earth in broad daylight." Those who cultivate the lower form of corpse liberation may never again gaze upon their homeland—this is the Way of the higher liberation. Their names are recorded on the Purple Registers, and the Three Bureaus may no longer scrutinize their flaws. Though they attain hidden transcendence, their worldly aspirations remain unfulfilled, and they may not return, thus their wanderings are without fixed abode.

It also states: One who drinks an elixir dissolved in water and embraces grass while lying down, then perishes in an empty chamber, is said to have achieved liberation through martial means. It further says: Only the eightfold purity of the highest rank is recorded in the registers of the celestial lists, received but not enacted; all others achieve corpse liberation in broad daylight and become flying immortals.

*The Hidden Instructions on Ascending to Perfection* says: At the moment of corpse liberation, when death comes by blade, flood, fire, or excruciating pain, the suffering is no different from that of ordinary mortals. Only after death does the spirit depart, while the form remains behind as a sign.

It further states: Dong Zhongju, a native of Huainan, practiced qi absorption and bodily refinement from a young age. Though he lived over a hundred years, he never aged. Once falsely imprisoned, he departed through corpse liberation. It also says: Qing Pingji, a man of Pei, died during the reign of Emperor Gaozu of Han. Yet by the time of Emperor Guangwu, he had not aged. Later, he departed through corpse liberation.

*The Declarations of the Perfected* says: Gu Huan, styled Yuanping, was a native of Wu Commandery. During the Yongping era of the Qi dynasty, he died on Mount Shan in Shanyin and was buried in Leyu Village, Yanofficial. A tree with interlocking branches grew upon his grave, and the county magistrate Jiang Shantu submitted a memorial on the matter. Huan had departed through corpse liberation. It further states: Xin Xuanzǐ, styled Yanqi, was a native of Dinggu in Longxi. Fond of the Dao, he was crossing the Changliang Ford of the Qin River when he drowned and departed through liberation. It also says: Zhang Zuchang, a man of Pengcheng, came north during the Wu dynasty. Entering the grotto chambers of Fang Mountain, he feigned death in a carriage accident and concealed his transformation in a secluded abode, where he cultivated the practice of guarding the One. It further states: Liu Pinghe, whose given name is unknown, served as the magistrate of Pinghe in Jiujiang during the late Han. Practicing medicine, he performed acts of virtue, healing others’ illnesses as if they were his own. While traveling, he encountered the immortal Zhou Zhengshi, who transmitted to him the Way of hidden preservation.

Residing in the grotto chambers of Fang Mountain, he regularly absorbed the morning qi of the sun and moon, his countenance remaining youthful. Later, he departed through liberation. It further states: Those who receive the Great Precepts and die undergo extinction and refinement of the spirit, ascending to replenish the celestial offices—this is called liberation. It also says: When a person dies, one must examine their form. If they appear as in life, their feet uncyanosed, skin unwrinkled, and eyes undimmed, these are all cases of liberation. Ascending by daylight is itself immortality, not an instance of liberation; those who achieve liberation through elixirs do not qualify. Those who transform through the ingestion of divine pills cannot return to their hometowns, for the Three Offices seize them. Departing by daylight is called upper liberation; departing at midnight is called lower liberation; departing at dusk is called the steward of the underworld.

The *Qiongwen Siji Pian* states: Those who obtain the *Central Scripture of the Nine Perfected* ascend through daylight liberation. Some say: The *Feathered Flight Scripture* is light. The *Liuji Pian* also states: Those who possess the *Divine Book of Purple Mushrooms* or the *Five Elders’ Treasure Scripture* achieve liberation. The *Biographies of Divine Immortals* records: Jie Xiang, styled Yuanze, was a native of Kuaiji. Sun Quan of Wu held him in high regard, often saying, “Master Jie, hasten your departure.” Sun Quan refused to listen. Xiang feigned illness, and Sun Quan sent attendants to bestow upon him a box of fine pears. In an instant, Xiang died and departed through liberation.

It further states: The Nine Flowers Sanctuary of the Purple Clarity Upper Palace instructed Lord Yang: “Seek the Way of the Liberated Sword to ensure an auspicious end. Exhaust yourself in silent departure, harmonizing the traces of concealment and revelation.” It also says: Ge Xuan, styled Xiaoxian, received the *Nine Elixirs and Golden Liquid Scripture* from Zuo Ci. He regularly consumed wood and told his disciple Zhang Feng: “I shall depart through liberation. On the twelfth day of the eighth month, I will depart.” When the appointed time arrived, Xuan donned his robes and cap, his breath ceased, yet his complexion remained unchanged—he departed through liberation.

It further states: Shi Yagong, named Xie Yuan, was a native of Liyang and a disciple of Fei Zhangfang. When the Daoist Li Yiqi departed with two disciples after many years, Zhangfang and the two disciples all transformed and vanished through liberation. It also says: Bao Shuo, styled Taixuan, was a native of Langye and lived during the reign of Emperor Ming of Jin. Yin Jun, the father-in-law of Ge Hong, transmitted to him the method of liberation. Another account states: Jing was a native of Shangdang, a descendant of Bao Xuan, the Han dynasty Minister of Justice. Cultivating the body and nurturing nature, he departed through liberation at over seventy years of age. There was one Xu Ning who studied under Shuo. One night, Ning heard the sound of a zither in Shuo’s chamber and inquired about it. Shuo replied: “Ji Shuye once manifested his traces at the Eastern Market, but in truth, it was a martial liberation.”

The *Jin Zhongxing Shu* records: Ge Hong was appointed magistrate of Goulou but was detained in Guangzhou by the regional inspector Deng Yue, who refused to let him proceed. Hong remained on Mount Luofu, refining elixirs for years. Suddenly, he wrote to Yue, stating he would travel afar to seek herbs. When Yue received the letter and hastened to bid farewell, Hong had already passed. At eighty-one, his complexion was as in life; his body was as light as empty clothing when placed in the coffin—he departed through liberation.

The *Biographies of Daoist Scholars* states: Wu Meng, styled Yunshi, possessed Daoist arts. When Yu Liang heard of his divine marvels, he respectfully welcomed him to Wuchang. Soon after, Meng sought to return home, claiming his allotted lifespan had ended and requesting a coffin. Yu Liang, grieved, immediately sent him off. Meng died fifty *li* from home, his form appearing as in life.

It further states: If the Six Conducts remain unmastered and past cultivation is meager, one enters the middle rank, achieving liberation and transformation. Below this, one undergoes proper burial. Those with shallow merits and inferior practices descend to the lower stages. Those who excel achieve extinction and rebirth. After rebirth, one cultivates the Dao according to the measure of their merits before attaining the Way.

The *Tai Shang Taixiao Langshu* states: Those who study the highest methods and enter the mountains and forests, consuming divine herbs, may, due to karmic conditions, achieve liberation and harmonize with the world. Though their rites differ greatly from the worldly, they use neither coffin nor outer casket. They sweep the mountaintops and the depths beneath the trees, covering themselves with a single blanket upon the earth.

The *Tai Shang Tai Zhen Ke* states: When making offerings to ancestors, one should discern whether they have returned. Those who ascend through merit and virtue, with descendants of benevolence and filial piety, may transform their forms and return to wander—these are akin to liberation.

The *Biography of the Golden Watchtower Sage* states: The *Divine Book of Purple Text*, also called the *Five Elders’ Treasure Scripture*, grants liberation to those who possess it and attainment of the Dao to those who practice it. The *Biography of the Azure Lad of the Eastern Sea* records: The *Baodong Guanjing* states: Those who possess the *Upper Mystery of the Numinous Purchase* ascend through daylight liberation.

The *Baopuzi* states: Among the Daoist groves are five types of liberation talismans; the present *Tai Xuan Yin Sheng Fu* is one that liberates from illness. The *Biographies of the Immortals* records: Ning Feng, the Pottery Master during the time of the Yellow Emperor, burned himself in fire and ascended and descended with the smoke. The *Zhen Gao* states: Ning Feng consumed stone brains, and fire was his medium—this was a fire liberation.

It further states: Sima Jizhu, a man of the reign of Emperor Wen of Han, received the Way of the Liberated Sword from Xiling Zidu. Residing in the Great Abundance Palace on Mount Weiyu, he consumed the essence of bright cinnabar and embraced the radiance of the morning sun. His appearance was like that of a woman, with a beard three feet long. He had one son, named Fayu, and one daughter, named Jihua, both of whom obtained the *Scripture of the Perfected Dao*. It is said that Jizhu ascended in concealment after consuming divine powder, though his head and feet were in separate places. This resembles the method of martial liberation. Those who undergo martial liberation cannot remain in the Great Ultimate, yet his daughter still studied the *Cave Scripture*, indicating she cultivated a separate, loftier method.

Shou Xuanbai of the White Guard secluded himself on the eastern peak of Mount Taimao. He could conceal his form and often appeared in the guise of Jie Yan, a disciple of the White Lamb Master. He now resides on Fang Mountain in Jian’an. Yan was initially executed by Sun Quan but departed through liberation.

It is further said: Elühua was a female immortal. In the third year of the Shengping reign of Emperor Mu of Jin (jiyou, 359 CE), on the tenth day of the eleventh month, she descended to the household of Yang Quan, claiming to be a native of Mount Nanshan. Quan, styled Daoxue, was the grandfather of Yang Xin, a Gentleman of the Yellow Gate during the reign of Emperor Jianwen of Jin. Both Quan and Xin secretly cultivated the essentials of the Dao, delighting in the profound and savoring the true. Elühua declared: "For all those who cultivate the Dao, regard noble rank as a passing traveler and gold and jade as mere tiles and pebbles—thus may they attain longevity." Thereupon, she transmitted to Quan the method of *corpse liberation*, and he too concealed his radiance and departed through transformation.

It is further said: Lady Wang, the Central Marquis, received from her nephew Jin the Dao of *flying liberation and the untying of the net*. It is further said: Cai Tiansheng, a native of Shanggu, sold incense in his youth upon the wilds. Of benevolent nature and fond of the Dao, he once encountered the River Earl’s youngest daughter selling incense on Mount Tianshan.

It is further said: Han Chong, styled Changji, was a native of Wu Commandery. A man of the reign of Emperor Ming of Han, he was fond of the Dao from his youth. The immortal Wang Zhangxuan of the Forest Chamber once transmitted to him the method of *Flowing Pearl Elixir*, which Chong reverently cultivated. After it proved highly efficacious, Zhangxuan bestowed upon him the method of *concealed liberation* and departed, entering the Great Huo Mountain to transcend the world as the Supervisor of the Right within the Central Bureau. The *Records of Daily Activities of the Han* states: When Li Shaojun was about to depart, Emperor Wu dreamed of ascending a high mountain with him, where he saw an emissary proclaiming the summons of the Great One. Upon waking, he said to his attendants, "Shaojun is about to depart." Several days later, Shaojun indeed fell ill and died, then departed through liberation.

The *Red Writ of the Numinous Treasure* states: The *Three Primes’ Royal Talismans* and the *Five Chapters of Numinous Treasure True Writ* both emerged from the Purple Tenuity Palace atop Jade Capital Mountain in the Great Mystery Metropolis. This writ averts the baleful influences of the *nine cycles of yang* and the *one hundred six calamities*, aligning with their reckonings to deliver the bodies of cultivators. Within the Mystery Metropolis, this scripture is possessed; those who bear it may ascend as sages to the Grand Clarity. Should their merit and virtue remain unfulfilled, they may yet attain *corpse liberation*.

It is further said: She Qi, styled Guangping, was a native of Jingzhao. At the beginning of the Jian’an era, he came to the Jiangdong region to serve Sun Ce. Later, he encountered Master Jie Yan, who transmitted to him, recognizing him as an extraordinary person.

Having bowed twice and received its incense fire, the Maiden then taught him the method of paying homage to the Heavenly Thearch and August Sovereign, after which he departed through *corpse liberation*, concealing himself upon the Square Terrace.

The *Traditions of Lord Lao* states: The Nine Perfected and Five Minerals briefly enter the Grand Yin. Only after passing through the Three Bureaus may one obtain the method of *upper liberation*.

It further says: The Purple Yang Duke transmitted the method of *sword liberation* from the Western City. After cultivating and wearing the divine sword for seven years, he inscribed vermilion talismans and departed through transformation. If one employs the *Crooked Dawn* to fly essence and inscribe them, one may instantly transform, vanish, and conceal oneself, whereupon the Grand Unity dispatches auspicious radiance and treasure robes to welcome them.

It further says: Wang Yuan, styled Fangping, upon observing Cai Jing’s bone configuration, knew he was destined for *corpse liberation* and imparted to him essential teachings. Fangping wore a *Far-Wandering Cap*, a vermilion robe, a tiger-headed pouch, multicolored sashes, and a yellow-hued sword; his beard was sparse, and his stature moderate.
