The *Scripture of Dignified Conduct* states: Purification and fasting bring luminous blessings; to deliver others, one must act before oneself, aligning with the will of the Mysterious. Another version of the daily practice states that those who receive the *Red Writ of the Numinous Treasure* must first purify and fast.

The *Scripture of the Eastern Minister of Destiny* states: The former master, Lord Wang, was once bestowed the *Upper Scripture of the Mysterious and True of the Hall of Light* by the Most High. He purified, fasted, and stilled his roots, visualizing the sun and moon while swallowing the fluid of their radiant effulgences. Practicing this in secret is the Way of the Highest Perfected. The *Scripture of the Mysterious and True of the Most High* requires a prior covenant before practice, and only after practice may one hear of it—this is the Way of jade pendants and golden earrings. In the past, Ji Wei maintained purification for three years, devoting himself to reverent contemplation before attaining it. His body radiated divine light before he received the scripture—this is the true and essential Way of the Mysterious, concise yet not cumbersome. I have long treasured and concealed it within my sleeve, sharing it only with those who guard its secrecy.

Those who seek the divine mountains should first purify and fast before ascending. In the past, Zuo Ci purified and fasted for three months, paying homage to the numinous mountain. After three years of utmost sincerity, the Two Lords of Mount Mao led him forward.

It further states: The *Jade Scripture of the Inner Radiance of the Yellow Court* records that the Great Emperor Lord of Fusang commanded the Spirit King of Yang Valley to transmit it to the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, with nine days of purification and fasting for its transmission.

It further states: The *Scripture of the Three Primordials and the True One*, guarded by the Golden Portal Emperor Lord, was transmitted by the Little Lad of the Eastern Sea to Master Hua, who passed it to Master Su, who then transmitted it to Lord Zhou. The transmission required purification for a hundred days, or fifty, thirty, or seven days. One person was transmitted to every forty years, with a total of ten recipients. Later, the Sage Dao Lord commanded the King of Pure Numinosity of the Lesser Existence Heaven to compile the comprehensive register of the Upper Perfected Immortals. The Lady of Purple Primordiality transmitted it to Lord Wang, who passed it to the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, Wei, who transmitted it to Lord Yang, who then passed it to Xu Yuan, with three or seven days of purification and fasting for its transmission. The *Writ of the Phoenix Perfected* was bestowed by the Most High upon the Left Perfected of the Great Ultimate, who transmitted it to the Lord of the Square Cauldron of the Eastern Sea and the Blue Lad. This, too, was passed among the Perfected, with three days of purification and fasting for its transmission. After wearing it for nine years, one may behold the Two Primordial Lords in the Golden Portals of Supreme Clarity.

It further states: The *Scripture of the Wisdom of the Most High* was entrusted to the Upper Minister by the Most High. The Lady of Purple Primordiality transmitted it to Lord Wang, who passed it to the Southern Perfected, who then transmitted it to Lord Yang. It is now bestowed upon Director Xu Yuan, with fifty days of purification and fasting for its transmission.

It further states: The *Hidden Writ of the Great Cinnabar on Flying to Perfection* concerns the method of visualization. Lord Yang merely copied one scripture to recite and share with the Director. It is also the *Dragon Writ of the Nine Perfected*, but without the method of purification and fasting, it cannot be practiced. The *True Sayings* contains the method of morning audience with the Great Simplicity, stating that those who receive the *Revolving Central Cavern* and visualize the *Hidden Writ of the Great Cinnabar* in the Three Primordials’ Caverns refer to this, though the details are incomplete. There was once a Lord Zhou who studied and annotated the matters of the Cavern Chambers, but it was merely an excerpt. This scripture’s language and annotations outline the method of practice, yet without the original text, its essential meaning remains incomplete.

The *Records of the Famous Mountains* states: On Great Mount Mao, there is a small cave mouth blocked by stone. Only with utmost sincerity and purification may one enter and wander within.

To the east of Mount Mao lies another small cavern, its mouth no larger than a dog’s burrow, barely wide enough for a person to enter. Yet the deeper one ventures, the more expansive it becomes. A massive boulder seals the entrance, leaving only a cup-sized aperture, guarded by the mountain spirits. This boulder occasionally shifts aside, and those who seek it with earnest purification may pass through more easily than through the common cave mouths.

Those who aspire to the Way of divine transcendence should first purify themselves through fasting and vigil. Then, the Three Lords Mao of Mount Juqu will appear to them, bestowing the essential Dao. To enter the cavern’s gate at Juqu, one must pass through five portals. Only those who maintain resolve and purification for three months may ascend and enter.

The *Scripture of the Nine Heavens* states: The Jade Aide of the Supreme Minister fasts and bears the ritual staff, attending the Great Purity.

The *Dharma Wheel Scripture* says: The Immortal Duke fasted, and before a full year had passed, the celestial perfected descended into his cold chamber. It further says: Meditate upon the true with fasting, seal the mouth, and guard the tongue.

The *Great Precepts of the Numinous Treasure* declares: Without receiving the great precepts, prolonged fasting is in vain.

The *Bright Statutes of the Four Poles* states: All who study the Supreme Clarity Dao must honor their lineage master and enter seclusion with fasting.

The *Supreme Statutes* says: Whenever scriptures are transmitted by a master, true officials stand guard, and fasting must precede recitation.

The *Scripture of the Feminine Unity and the Five Elders* says: One must cultivate good conduct daily, eat only at noon, and fast for a full year before receiving the *True Scripture of the Great Cavern*.

The *Vermilion Register of the Supreme Lord’s Cinnabar Tablets* states: The Dao has long since drifted from the sages, and errors abound in the transmission of precepts and statutes. If doubts arise that the master cannot resolve, one may fast for a month and seek confirmation through numinous response. The divine immortals will descend and reveal the answer to the seeker.

The *Scripture of Transmission* says: In fasting, simplicity is supreme, for the spirits first reflect the body’s purity.

The *Records of the Assembled Immortals* recounts: On the Dark Garden of Kunlun, the Perfected of the Orthodox Unity appeared to one who endured hardship with fasting, reciting scriptures and revering the Dao.

The *Jade Writ of the Grand Night* says: Three books are to be established—one for permanent safeguarding, one for ritual fasting, and one for study. They should always be kept in the chamber where one resides, placed upon a separate stand. One must handle them personally, never allowing them to be mishandled. When copying scriptures, one must first fast. If the scripture contains illustrations, these may be bound separately, each with its attendant officials and keepers of the images.

The true officials, when questioned about the scriptures, say: Without a master to uphold the Dao, fasting and recitation yield no response.

The *Scripture of the Jade Pendants and Golden Girdle Ornaments* says: The assembled perfected ascend the Grand Jade Terrace after fasting for three months.

The *Scripture of Kongtong* states: The Supreme Lord of the Dao fasted upon the peaks of Luofu in the Western Jade Land of Xina. It further says: The True Person of the Great Ultimate transmitted the *Green Essence* to Lord Wang. During the transmission, they fasted for ten days. Over two thousand six hundred years, it was passed to ten individuals. The Jade Seal of Leimaiya was transmitted to Lady Wei of the Southern Marchmount; they fasted for five days, and by ingesting it, one could abstain from grain and expel corpse-worms. Lord Wang traveled the world, arriving at Tortoise Mountain, where he fasted for three months. He then fasted for three years before journeying to the Great Simplicity.

Returning to Western City, he fasted for another three months. Receiving scriptures from Perfected Zhou, he had earlier encountered the Central Yellow and Old Lord wandering in Cinnabar City, where he begged for the Dao of long life and deliverance across the world. The Lord transmitted to him the Dao of the Supreme Perfected, whereupon he returned and ascended the stone chamber of Mount Chang, fasting and purifying his thoughts. After many years had passed, he departed as an immortal.

The *Traditions of Daoist Scholarship* states: Zuo Dun, styled Shangyin, was a native of Leimaiyang. Cloudyang Mountain is none other than Mount Mao. Fifteen *li* west of Dun’s mountain abode stood a stone chamber; two *li* to the southwest was another stone chamber, each capable of holding several dozen people. Elders of the southwestern chamber transmitted that a bronze ox had emerged, along with bronze worms and bronze scrolls, and the place was thus called the Bronze Chamber. Winding inward to profound depths, it stood to the north, connecting to the Flowing Pool, and the cavern led to Kunlun. On each of the Three Primes’ fasting and purification days, Dun went to the two chambers to pray and cast talismans, always coiling his hair into the form of a Buddha’s topknot.

It further says: Lu Xiujing, styled Yuande, was a native of Wuxing. In the seventh year of the Taishi era, he led the assembly in establishing the Three Primes’ Open-Air Fast. The *Scripture of the Supreme Perfected’s Upper Granary and Primordial Upper Record* states: In every realm where living beings dwell, purity is scarce and turbidity abundant, with defilements entwining one another. If good conduct is not established, perverse *qi* will invade, and fierce demons will guard and test. Those who study the higher teachings fast and purify themselves, concentrating their thoughts and barring the clamor of the dusty world. Unwholesome entities intrude and depart—all are defiled and turbid. One must choose an auspicious day to fast and purify, wear the talisman of *po-yan*, and thus ascend to Jade Purity.

*Daoist Canon, Ninth Section Concluded*
*Daoist Canon, Tenth Section*

**Nurturing Life**

The *Scripture of Great Peace* states: The Dao of nurturing life lies in calming the body and cultivating *qi*, avoiding joy and anger. When one is free from worry, longevity naturally follows. It further says: One is the beginning of numbers, the Dao of life, the origin of primordial *qi*, and the great guiding principle of Heaven. Thus, one must guard and contemplate the One. If you wish to nurture old age and preserve longevity, guard the One most steadfastly. Harmonize your *qi* and remain tranquil externally, abiding with the One. If your *qi* flows like a spring’s source, what harm can befall your body? This is called the true treasure, and old age and decline will depart of their own accord.

It also says: In the time of the Three Sovereigns of antiquity, people’s *qi* was pure, and they deeply understood the utmost essence of Heaven and Earth. Thus, they all studied the true Dao and thereby attained the impartiality of Heaven and Earth. The method of seeking the Dao begins with stillness as its foundation. Once the heart and spirit are clear, they unite with the Dao, dispelling ignorance and illuminating all like the midday sun. Those who do not study this Dao are like those dwelling in a dark room, lost and disoriented. Hence, the sagely and wise hasten to its pursuit.

The *Scripture of the Supreme* states: Guarding the One brings true stability to the source of the heart; guarding stillness preserves the spirit and forgets the form. When *qi* is settled and pervades the formless, the Dao is accomplished, and the true descends.

The *Scripture of the Three Primes and the True One* states: To embody the hundred spirits, the ears are the windows of the Imperial Lord, the eyes are the sun and moon of the Great One, the nose is the hill and mountain of the Three Primes, the mouth is the crimson abyss of the Crimson Palace, the eyebrows are the canopy of the White Prime, the hair is the essence of the Forest of the Bright Hall, the tongue is the dragon axle of the Primordial Flower, the teeth are the might of the Stomach Palace, the hands are the external aid of the Gallbladder Spirit, the feet are the numinous gate of the Kidney Prime, and the utmost yin is the true mechanism of the Grotto Chamber.

It further says: Juanzi taught Su Lin the Dao of guarding the Three True Ones. Later, Lin returned to Juanzi’s chamber of stillness, but Juanzi was no longer there. He left behind a written scroll in his sleeping quarters for Lin, which read: "The Five Pecks and Three Ones are secrets of the Great Emperor. After twelve years of concentrated contemplation, the Three Ones will appear and transmit their scripture to you. If the Three Ones alone are indestructible and everlasting, how much more so for those who guard them? One who guards the Three Ones will have their name inscribed on the Jade Tablet. How much more so for one who meets the Three Ones? By further contemplating the Grotto Chamber, one becomes a Duke of the Upper Clarity. By further understanding the Three Primes, one becomes a successor to the Five Emperors. How does the Golden Watchtower’s Imperial Lord ride the swift clouds and traverse the Ten Heavens? It is through the Dao of the Grotto Chamber and the Three Primes’ True One."

Scholars of the world all revere guarding the One. They must ensure the heart is unadorned and the spirit concentrated, the body devoted and sincerity evoked. Thus, a hundred thoughts do not arise, and the essence of intent does not scatter. Simply focus inwardly for three months, binding the mind to one spirit, not dispersing but concentrating the *qi*, achieving harmony through the utmost simplicity. Those who attain it swiftly do so because simplicity scatters and truth departs, while artificiality and falsity arise, giving rise to strife and chaos. Thus, the One is not swiftly perceived, and the spirit does not immediately respond—not because it does not wish to abide with those who contemplate it, but because those who do not concentrate their thoughts lack discernment. Hence, it takes years of accumulated effort to sever the ties of the mundane.

The method of the Three Ones is the first chapter of the *Upper Clarity’s* true scriptures, the jade Dao of the Most High, the ford of divine immortality, and the wondrous secret of the host of perfected beings. If you can guard the One, the One will guard you; if you can see the One, the One will see you. The One requires the body to stand, and the body requires the One to live.

The precepts of guarding the One warn against lack of concentration. If concentration is not sustained, if duration is not prolonged, if prolonged effort is not refined, if refinement is not steadfast, and if steadfastness is not enduring, then the Three Ones depart, and the body becomes an empty dwelling.

The *Scripture of the Five Talismans* states: One who knows the One knows all; one who does not know the One knows nothing. The One is the most noble, the title without equal. If you desire longevity, the Three Ones must be understood. When you hunger for the One, the One provides sustenance; when you thirst for the One, the One provides drink. The One can generate yin and produce yang, propelling the cycles of cold and heat. Its greatness cannot be concealed by the Six Directions, and its smallness cannot be discerned by the tip of a hair. When one is at leisure and prepared, the One does not depart. When one contemplates the One with diligence, the One can communicate with the divine. By moderating drink and restraining food, the One remains and breathes. Knowing the One is not difficult; the difficulty lies in persevering to the end. Knowing the true and not acting is the same as not knowing. Seek it unceasingly, and you will ascend to Jade Clarity.

It further says: Nurture your *qi* to preserve your body. It also says: Those who consume *qi* always maintain a youthful countenance.

*Laozi* states: The Dao’s words are subtle and profound; you have yet to distinguish them. Grasp their essentials and be cautious not to lose them. First reduce your desires and do not let your mind wander. Dwell in seclusion and stillness, refining your chamber of fasting. Even ten thousand scrolls of cinnabar scriptures are not as good as guarding the One. Restrain your thoughts to settle your will, calm your body to pacify your spirit, treasure your *qi* to preserve your blood. Forget thoughts and worries, focus inwardly, and your body and spirit will unite. Contemplate stillness to await the true, and the myriad wonders will respond and converge. Concentrate your essence and accumulate spirit without mingling with external things—this is called purity. Return the spirit and ingest *qi*, abiding in stillness without movement—this is called the Dao.

It further says: Those who skillfully nurture life walk on land without encountering rhinoceroses or tigers; they enter battle without being harmed by armor or weapons. The rhinoceros has nowhere to thrust its horn, the tiger has nowhere to place its claws, and weapons have nowhere to lodge their blades.

The *True Scripture of the Supreme* states: The One has no form; seeking it is difficult, and guarding it is easily lost. It is easily lost because of weak perception and desires clogging the heart’s gate. Only in vast emptiness and non-action does guarding the One reside. All accumulation that has not reached its limit proceeds gradually. One must clearly recognize the spirit and *qi* of the Three Primes—their appearance, names, and the cycles of their presence and absence. They are born and reside in the Three Palaces, and corpse poison departs of its own accord. The sacred and true scriptures of immortality are transmitted according to the cause.

The *Scripture of the Eight Simplicities* states: In studying the utmost Dao, one must settle the heart, eliminate afflictions, and purify the body, understanding change and rectifying thoughts. When the body is pure, the heart becomes settled; when the heart is settled, the Dao is accomplished; when the Dao is accomplished, the true descends.

To store the One and guard the spirit, the essential lies in proper transformation. Proper transformation arises from settling the heart; when the heart is settled, perception becomes clear; when perception is clear, one meets the Dao.

The Perfected of the Great Ultimate also said: The ancients who cultivated the Dao practiced profound stillness to quiet the spirit, contemplated the true and preserved the primordial. They gradually guided the unrefined, returning perception to its source in spirit. Knowing, they could see; seeing, they could follow; following, they could practice; practicing, they could persist; persisting, they could accomplish; accomplishing, they did not dwell.

Is the virtuous person in the world like a bellows? They do not contend with the myriad things, yet their power constantly returns to them. This is due to their humility and desirelessness. Desire is the root of misfortune and harm; non-being is the origin of Heaven and Earth. None know its root, none know its source. The sage eliminates desire to enter non-being, thereby aiding their person.

The *Scripture of the Great One Cavern-Truth* states: The two ears are called the high windows of the Six Harmonies. It also says: The center of the teeth is named the Palace of Receiving Life. Further, it says: In the Dao of nurturing life, the ears and eyes are the masters. Scattered vision dims the eyes; excessive listening closes the ears.

The *Inner Transmission of Master Pei* says: Those who seek the Dao must first make the eyes clear and the ears keen. Moreover, the ears and eyes are the ladder for seeking the true and the gateway for gathering the numinous—success or failure depends on them.

The *Scriptures of the Immortals* say: In nurturing life, not causing harm is the foundation. This is a crucial teaching.

The *Scripture of the Great Clarity* states: All beings that contain qi value life. Life is the great power of Heaven and Earth; no power surpasses long life. Those who attain long life must transcend the body. They do not harm other beings with their bodies—not merely refraining from harm, but aiding others while forgetting themselves. Forgetting themselves, yet their person is not forgotten—this is the way of those who skillfully nurture life. The true Dao nourishes the spirit, and the spirit can soar and transform.

The *Scripture of the Three Primes* says: The Dao of nurturing life must cherish qi and preserve the spirit. One must not engage in loud speech or shouting, lest the spirit be wearied and qi damaged. Therefore, perfected persons and Daoists constantly practice exhalation and inhalation to harmonize the six fluids.

The *Scripture of the Mysterious Manifestation* says: The physical form is merely the vessel of life, not the means by which life generates itself. Life generates itself through plain simplicity as its substance, qi as its origin, and spirit as its form—this is the palace and courtyard of life. Nurturing the spirit through non-action, unfolding the gate of profound mystery, coming and going in the realm of formlessness, resting in the boundless—this is what is called attaining the life-source of mysterious clarity.

It also says: External distractions should be cut off, and internally one should focus on the mysterious true. Only then can long life be preserved.

The *Scripture of the Wondrous True* says: The Daoist plans for life, not for fame. Their mind is free of worldly concerns, their intent without inclination. Their will flows like water; their dwelling is like an empty city. Accumulating and guarding non-action, they can attain long life.

The *Precepts of the Many Perfected* say: Impatience and violence are the greatest thieves of the body and the scattered ladder of seeking the Dao. Those who employ them drive away the true; those who reform them invite the Dao. In all matters, one should be gentle and unhurried, exhausting the principle of utmost purity. Only then can one approach the Dao.

The spirit is what Heaven and Earth hasten toward. Nurturing the spirit and cultivating nature, practicing the qi of the life Dao to traverse difficulties—this is the profound understanding of the highest sages and perfected persons. Those who cultivate the Dao should practice this to sustain their person.

The *Scripture of the Lord Emperor of the Great One* says: If one can constantly practice the method of the Nine Dawns illuminating the Cavern Chamber and the Mud Pill Palace, restraining the hun and po souls and controlling the myriad evils, and purify their conduct, then the qi of the numinous immortals will descend into their bedchamber. This is what is called drawing the Three Lights and Nine Stars to illuminate the hundred spirits.

The *Arrayed Records of the Highest Clarity* say: Closing the womb and quieting the breath, internally preserving the hundred spirits, swallowing the radiance and swallowing the fluids, consuming food naturally—one’s body will surely enjoy longevity, and one may attain the immortality of the terrestrial realm.

The *Secret Essentials of the Perfected of the Great Highest* says: Qi is the vessel of spirit and brightness, the origin of purity and turbidity. Abiding in the mysterious, Heaven is clear; dwelling in humans, the body is preserved. Life and death, decline and fullness—these all depend on the art of nurturing and controlling.

The *Jade Scripture of the Great Cavern* says: Those who consume the qi of the mysterious root make their bodies clear and bright, their spirit and eight senses keen. Their body shines like the sun, their face glows with jade-like luster. Ingesting morning fluids and suspending grain, relying on golden liquor as the essential Dao and water jade as the wondrous practice—this is what is called exhaling and inhaling the Great Harmony of nature and governing the numinous qi of the Nine Essences.

The *Master Embracing Simplicity* says: The essentials of long life lie in the Dao of rejuvenation; extending years and eliminating illness are secondary. If one does not harm oneself, even if still young and strong, and knows the Yin Elixir of rejuvenation to supplement the brain, gathering the Seven Benefits in the Long Valley, without consuming medicinal herbs, one may still live one or two hundred years.

There are several ways to cause harm: straining to think beyond one’s capacity, exerting strength beyond one’s ability, deep worries and heavy resentments, sorrow and joy, relentless desires, constant anxieties, irregular sleep, excessive drunkenness and vomiting, eating to fullness and lying down immediately, running and panting, shouting and weeping, lack of sexual union—accumulating such harms to the utmost exhausts the body, violating the methods of nurturing nature.

Do not exhaust the ears with listening or the eyes with prolonged gazing. Do not sit until fatigued. Dress before feeling cold, remove clothing before feeling hot. Do not eat when extremely hungry, and do not eat to excess. Do not drink when extremely thirsty, and do not drink too much.

Do not overwork, nor sweat excessively, nor spit frequently. Do not gallop on horseback or race in carriages, nor strain the eyes with distant gazing. Avoid eating raw or cold foods. In winter, do not seek extreme warmth; in summer, do not seek extreme cold. Do not expose yourself to bitter cold, scorching heat, fierce winds, or dense fog. The five flavors should not be consumed in excess or imbalance.

Though such harms may not be immediately felt, over time they diminish one’s lifespan. Therefore, those skilled in nurturing life rise and rest in accordance with the seasons’ rhythms, maintain harmonious routines in daily activities, regulate the sinews and bones through proper postures, ward off illness and repel evil with breath control, balance the flow of *qi* through the stomach and meridians with tonifying and purging methods, and moderate exertion and rest with the principles of giving and taking. They restrain anger to preserve *yin*, suppress joy to nourish *yang*, and only then first consume herbs and plants to remedy deficiencies, later ingesting the Golden Elixir to secure boundless vitality. The principles of long life are fully encompassed herein.

If one indulges desires, follows whims, claims enlightenment and understanding of fate, dismisses heterodoxies while indulging passions, and neglects the pursuit of longevity, how can one be taught the words of nurturing life?

The *Dengzhen Yinjue* states: Master Fangzhu of the Azure Youth said, "Those who study the Dao suffer, and those who do not also suffer. Though both sufferings begin the same, their ends differ. For those who pursue the Dao, bitterness leads to joy; for those who do not, suffering remains endless. From birth to old age, from old age to illness, from illness to death—how great is this suffering! With sins accumulated in the heart and brain, the cycle of life and death never ceases, its bitterness beyond words. How can one fail to live out their natural years? This is the suffering of not pursuing the Dao.

Yet pursuing the Dao also entails hardship: maintaining purity, preserving truth, guarding the mysterious and contemplating the numinous, seeking teachers through toil, enduring hundreds of trials, and unwavering in resolve—this too is extreme suffering. During decades of such effort, the hardship may seem greater than the reward. But upon attaining the Dao, this suffering is instantly forgotten, like one who, after a hundred days of hunger, is sated in a single meal—how could they recall the former pangs of want? Without the Dao, this cannot be achieved."

The Right Radiant Perfected One said: "Those who entangle themselves in family affairs or are burdened by worldly duties cannot focus on the Dao. To hold the Dao yet not practice it is as if one had no Dao at all; to grasp a treasure yet not use it is as if one had no treasure."

The Primordial Lady of Purple Tenuity said: "Illness arises from excessive thoughts; evil begins with a scattered mind. Many thoughts lead to many affairs, and many affairs bring endless burdens. Adrift and unrestrained, entangled and unceasing, the mind is consumed by myriad worries, the body wearied by a hundred labors. When form and spirit are exhausted, how can illness not arise? Even behind high walls and heavy gates, one fears bandits; how much worse to leave the door unbarred and invite harm upon oneself? The intellect, when boundless, injures one’s nature; the heart, when reckless, dissipates truth. Forms appear before the eyes, sounds enter the ears—these open the mind to desires and attachments, fostering greed. The *hun* is the upright spirit, prizing clarity and sincerity; the *po* is the wayward ghost, prone to madness and rebellion. When thoughts of flying immortals arise, one must temper them with compassion and restraint. In all encounters, let this be the heart’s guiding principle, and the heart becomes the Dao."

The *Nine Splendors Scripture* states: "The eyes are the body’s mirror, the ears its windows. Excessive gazing dims the mirror; excessive listening shuts the windows. Polish the mirror and open the windows, and one can perceive all spirits and hear the faintest sounds. The face is the courtyard of the spirit, the hair the blossom of the brain. Grief withers the face; depletion of the brain whitens the hair. Thus, when essence and *qi* are lost within, the elixir of vitality is exhausted. Essence is the spirit of the body, clarity its treasure. Overwork scatters essence; excessive scheming consumes clarity. Thus, aging follows the decline of *qi*, and senility soon arrives."

The *Zhen’gao* states: "Wealth and rank are the axes and saws that break bones, the boats and carriages that carry sin. They suffice to invite transgressions and disgrace, serving as weapons that cut short life—these are not auspicious things. Thus, the sages of old, foreseeing the difficulties of guilt and misfortune, knew that wealth and rank could not be enjoyed. They retreated to deep forests and dwelled in famous mountains, seeking to distance themselves from such paths, to cultivate blessings, and preserve their primordial purity."

Master Pei said: "Regulating the Three Passes is the way to long life: the mouth is the Heavenly Pass, the hands the Human Pass, and the feet the Earthly Pass. When regulated, the five viscera are at peace, and peace brings freedom from illness. Moreover, one should visualize the Five Spirits within the body: the two hands, two feet, and head. Envision the head as azure, both hands as crimson, and both feet as white—thus one draws near to immort

The earth, by holding to the One, remains still and abides in its place; the mountains, by holding to the One, endure neither cold nor heat; the seas, by holding to the One, flow without return. When a person holds to the One, they are certain to attain true transcendence.

The *Scripture of Ascending the Mystery* states: "The Dao possesses a great method—attaining it brings immediate attainment. This is called the Way of the Three Ones. It commands generals, officers, and soldiers to sever the paths of evil."

The *Supreme Clarity Jade Emperor* says: "The Three Perfected are the emperors of one’s body, ruling over the hundred spirits within. They initiate transformations, partings, and unions, merging with the true and penetrating the numinous. Subtle indeed, beyond words—transmitted only to immortals."

The *Scripture of the Plain and Numinous* states: "The Three Ones are the numinous origin of the body, the life-root of the hundred spirits, the mountain-source of fluids, and the jade chamber of the ethereal soul. Thus, the stomach’s reservoir is square to receive things, while the palace of the brain is round and numinous to adapt."

The *True Supreme* says: "The reason the perfected value the One as true is simply this: the One alone. What the One contracts is the primordial qi of creation. The transformations of the One merge heaven and earth in darkness. Therefore, the Upper One is the celestial emperor of the body, the Middle One is the cinnabar sovereign of the Crimson Palace, and the Lower One is the primordial lord of the Yellow Court. These Three Ones truly govern the twenty-four qi within the body to bestow life, establishing the One within. Above, they correspond to the twenty-four true qi of the Grand Tenuity. When the true qi circulates in harmony, the myriad things take form. The dark spirits intermingle, and the Purple Chamber fades into obscurity. The Upper One is the ultimate of the true emperor, the Middle One is the lord of the true sovereign, and the Lower One is the wonder of the true king. The Celestial Sovereign attains the ultimate and thus ascends to the imperial ultimate; the Terrestrial Sovereign attains the lord and thus ascends to the Orthodox One; the Human Sovereign attains the wonder and thus ascends to the host of wonders. The Three Sovereigns embody the true and hold to the One—this is their true ultimate, for they attain the One alone."

The *Records of Immortals Gathered* states: "All movements, gazes, breaths, eating, speech, likes, dislikes, and judgments—each person has their allotted years, months, days, and hours, determined by their corresponding fate. This is the constant principle of things. The body has the peril of decay, the spirit has its destined time of dispersal, and life has its inevitable end. When the spirit abides, there is a person; when the spirit departs, there is but a corpse. This arises from desires disturbing the heart, unable to forget the pleasures of form and taste. Those who cultivate the Dao dwell in ease without encumbrance, harmonious and ever-permeable. Good and evil each follow the principle of retribution, without the slightest deviation. The foundation of long life lies solely in goodness as its base. Born between heaven and earth, each fulfills their nature. Those with clear qi are wise and sagely; those with turbid qi are cruel and foolish; those with firm qi are lofty, stern, and resolute; those with yielding qi are kind, benevolent, and sincere. The enlightened subdue their nature to extend life; the benighted indulge their desires and harm their nature. Nature is the source of life, and life is the root of existence. Strive to cultivate it, nurturing life to nourish nature and guarding the spirit to preserve life. Human life arises from the spirit—when the spirit is settled, there is life; when the spirit is severed, there is death. Thus, accumulating qi forms essence, and accumulating essence forms spirit. Therefore, the immortal seeks within, and when the inner is recondite, the Dao draws near. The true one cultivates quiescence, and through stillness, unites with the true. The spirit must accumulate resonance to become numinous and penetrating. By constantly holding to the One, transcendence draws near, and one shares the same lodging with heaven and earth in the Great Void. Further, by penetrating the numinous body, the absence becomes the Great Void, and one lodges together in the vast silence. By penetrating the silent, hearing and sight become unhearing and unseen, merging with the Dao. The Dao is the utmost truth of numinous penetration; arts are the mysterious techniques of transformation. The Dao is formless, relying on arts to aid others. Humans possess numinosity, and through cultivation, they contract the Dao. The essentials of the Dao lie in profound simplicity and ease of practice. The secrets of arts reside solely in elixirs and qi. Superior practitioners who ingest them ascend as immortals of the celestial bureaus; middling practitioners who ingest them dwell on Kunlun; inferior practitioners who ingest them attain long life among humans."

Thus, the Primordial Sovereign of the Great One expounded the essential practices of the returning elixir and golden fluid to the world.

It further states: "The Lord of Wood and the Queen Mother of Metal are the ancestral origins of the two qi, the fundamental roots of yin and yang, the sovereigns of the immortal perfected, and the primal beginnings of creation. Condensing qi to form the true, they unite with the Dao in substance. Moreover, qi pervades heaven and earth, animating the movements of all things, both animate and inanimate. As humans, we are among things; as things, we manifest the great. The latent and dispersed are boundless. Nature arises from heaven, while life is completed by humans. What establishes it is heaven; what enacts it is the Dao."

The Mysterious Elder of the Dao said: "Attain utmost emptiness and hold fast to stillness. The myriad things will naturally revert—reversion means returning to the Dao and abiding forever. The essentials of longevity are: heaven preserves its mystery, earth guards its things, and humans nurture their qi."

It further states: "When the King of Shang heard that Peng Zu possessed the Dao, he appointed him as a grand minister. Peng Zu often claimed illness and lived in seclusion, not participating in government affairs. He ingested mica powder and drank water infused with deer antler."

He maintained a youthful appearance and a deeply tranquil nature, never boasting of his mastery of the Dao. When the king visited to seek his counsel, Peng Zu offered no instruction. The king then had a resplendent chamber with purple pavilions built in the palace gardens for Peng Zu to reside in. When asked about the Way of extending life and increasing longevity, Peng Zu replied: "Those who wish to ascend to heaven and serve as immortal officials must ingest the Golden Elixir of the Primordial Sovereign and Grand Unity. This is the greatest of all methods. Next is to cherish essence and nurture spirit, consuming herbal medicines—this can grant long life. Following that is the regulation of yin and yang, the circulation of qi, and guiding the body through bending and stretching to ensure the free flow of qi through all joints and mechanisms without obstruction. This can prevent illness from taking hold. Contemplating the divine and focusing on the true, sitting in stillness to refine the fluids—all these can extend one’s years. As for the essentials of replenishing the brain, these are exceedingly difficult to practice. They involve the dangers of treading upon thorns and walking on blades, which are not fitting for a king to undertake. What I have heard is shallow and limited; my knowledge of the Dao extends only this far. It is not sufficient to propagate widely. Yet if one lives in the world and nurtures oneself properly, one may reach over a hundred years. Those who fall short do so because they harm themselves. Overindulgence in drink, extreme joy, great anger, excessive warmth, extreme cold, overexertion, and exhaustion—all these cause harm. Supreme pleasure, deep sorrow, overwhelming fear, terror, agitation, restlessness, extravagance, and excess—all these cause harm. Extreme hunger, raging thirst, excessive thought, and overmuch worry—all these cause harm. Prolonged sitting, standing, exposure, or walking—all these cause harm. When cold and warmth are moderated, hunger and satiety are balanced, and one is free from thought and action, abiding only in clarity and stillness—only then can one speak of cultivating the body. Having already attained longevity, if one continues to nurture oneself properly, one may enjoy extended life, provided one avoids harm. To remain warm in winter and cool in summer, never losing harmony with the four seasons—this is how one adapts to the body. To behold beauty and graceful forms without succumbing to desire—this is how one unites with the spirit. To possess carriages and robes with dignity, knowing contentment and seeking no more—this is how one unifies the will. To enjoy the eight tones and five colors without becoming ensnared—this is how one guides the heart. All these things are meant to nurture humanity, yet people, unable to moderate and balance them, instead turn them into afflictions. Thus the sages and worthies left warnings, fearing that those of lesser talent would become lost in excess, forgetting the proper use of things and straying from their purpose. Therefore, those who cultivate the Dao are all instructed to abstain from such things, making restraint easier. It is like fire and water—used improperly, they become harmful. People do not realize that their meridians are damaged, their blood and qi depleted, their inner principles hollow and weak, their marrow and brain unsolidified. Their bodies are already ailing, and so they are vulnerable to external influences, falling ill due to wind, cold, alcohol, or desire. If one’s foundation were full and strong, how could illness or evil take hold? Excessive longing, envy, and desire harm a person. Grief, resentment, sorrow, excessive joy, unresolved anger, obsessive love, constant worry, imbalance of cold and warmth, and lack of union between yin and yang—all these cause harm. The union of man and woman is like the mutual generation of heaven and earth. It is through this that one guides and nurtures the spirit and qi, ensuring harmony is not lost. Heaven and earth separate by day and unite by night; in a year, they join three hundred and sixty times. Thus the four seasons are balanced, and the myriad things are born, their generation and completion without end. This is how heaven does not lose its movement, earth does not lose its harmony, and things do not lose their vitality, enduring forever. Yet people, unable to emulate heaven and earth and maintain constancy, reduce their clothing and abstain from food, bringing upon themselves illness and death—how foolish this is! Avoiding such extremes and practicing moderation, regulation, and proper circulation, one may absorb the harmonious qi of the universe. When one attains this Way, evil cannot enter—this is the foundation of nurturing life. There are over seventeen hundred other methods, such as absorbing the radiance of the sun, contemplating the spirit, guiding the organs, practicing daoyin, swallowing saliva, and consuming elixirs. Additionally, there are practices for the first month of each season: examining oneself, repenting for transgressions, and regulating the times of rising and resting. These can guide beginners toward the gate of goodness, gradually correcting their hearts and slowly dispelling their faults. Yet they do not immediately enable one to attain the Dao. If one’s blood and vessels are withered, one’s spirit and qi decayed, how can mere contemplation of the divine and focus on the true preserve them? It is doubtful whether any benefit can be gained. This is because ordinary people seek the Dao by pursuing its branches rather than its root.

Another passage states: "If one does not nurture the spirit within and exhausts the body without, one’s primordial essence will gradually be plundered, and one’s spirit and qi will become depleted. Even if one diligently studies and recites scriptures and formulas day and night, it will be of no avail. The myriad scriptures, numbering over thirteen thousand, merely point to the gateway for beginners."

The King of Shang received all these essential teachings and practiced Peng Zu’s methods, thereby extending his life. Yet he could not restrain his excesses of desire.

The *Register of Assembled Immortals* states: There was a woman of the common folk named Fan, a wine-seller in the market of Chen. Her wine was excellent, and a transcendent passed by her home to drink. In exchange, he gave her five volumes of plain silk books. When she opened and read them, she found they contained methods for nurturing life and attaining longevity. She secretly copied the essential formulas and practiced them. After three years, her complexion became youthful. Several years later, the transcendent who had given her the wine returned. Smiling, he said to her, "You have stolen the Dao without a teacher—you have wings but do not fly." Lady Fan then followed the transcendent away, and her whereabouts became unknown.

It further states: The Woman of Grand Yang, Shi Yi, obtained the Way of exhalation and inhalation and served Jue Dongzi, Li Xiu. Li Xiu wrote forty scrolls, titled *The Source of the Dao*. He practiced the principle that softness overcomes hardness and weakness subdues strength. It is like treading on thin ice or walking on the edge of a cliff, driving a galloping chariot with rotten reins—deviate by a hair’s breadth, and you lose your strategy. Yet if one practices diligently, one can attain long life.

It also states: The Woman of Grand Yin, Lu Jin, had not yet completed her study of the Dao. While selling wine along the Way, she secretly sought her teacher. When a guest arrived, she asked him how many years he had lived in the land. He replied, "Three in the south, five in the north, nine in the west, and the middle in the northwest." She returned and reported, "This guest is a great worthy, a transcendent who has attained the Dao. When I first asked, he knew one and understood five." She then inquired about the Way of long life and obtained the essentials of supplementation and guiding, as well as the method for steaming the elixir.

It further states: The Lady of Grand Mystery, Zhuan He, often said: "In this world of men, a single misstep cannot be regained, and death once met cannot be revived. The span of life is brief—without cultivating the Dao, it cannot be prolonged." Thereupon, she purified her heart and sought the Dao, obtaining its arts.

**Daoist Canon, Scroll Ten**
**Daoist Canon, Scroll Eleven**
**On Ingesting Medicinal Substances, Part One**

The *Divine Farmer’s Classic* states: "Superior medicines bring bodily peace and extend life." It further says: "Ingesting the Five Mushrooms, cinnabar, malachite, mica, *taiyi* [primordial essence], and *yuyuliang* [limonite], each taken singly, grants long life. Middle-grade medicines nourish nature, while lower-grade medicines dispel illness. These are the ultimate words of the highest sages and the true records of esoteric arts."

The foremost

Here the translation follows:

---

She favored sitting alone in quiet places, refining her thoughts with subtle focus. Daily at sunrise, she would face east, rinse her mouth, and ingest solar *qi*—practicing thus each dawn.

*The Declarations of the Perfected* states: During the late Han, Zhang Zhengli of Mount Heng received the Rainbow Radiance Elixir formula from the Lord of Western City. Distressed by the scarcity of cinnabar, he departed for Guangzhou as a Daoist adept and ascended as an Upper Immortal from the Whistling Chamber.

It further says: Zhang Xuanbin, a native of Dingxiang, was nominated as a *maocai* during the reign of Emperor Wu of Wei. Returning to his hometown, he studied under Ji the Elder of Xihe, receiving the method of ingesting wood-based medicines. Later, he encountered the Perfected Man Fan Ziming on Mount Shaoshi, who transmitted to him the arts of concealment, transformation, and luminous concealment. Formerly of Mount Tianzhu, he now serves as the Master of Regulations in the Inner Hua Yang.

It further says: In the mountains of Mount Qian in Lujiang, Daoist practitioners Zheng Jingshi and Zhang Chonghua both received oral instructions from the Immortal Meng Deran during the early Jin, entering the mountains to practice the method of guarding the Five Viscera while absorbing solar essence, along with consuming sesame and the Mysterious Elixir.

It further says: Ping Zhongjie, a native of Hedong, fled the chaos of Liu Cong’s rebellion by crossing the Yangtze into Mount Kuocang. His body possessed true *qi*, and through ingesting medicines, he ascended as an immortal.

It further says: Zhao Guangxin, a native of Yangcheng, crossed the Yangtze during the late Wei to enter Mount Xiaobai in Ke, where he received Li’s method of ingesting *qi* and the Way of Guarding the Mysterious Center from Lord Zuo. After many years, he sometimes sold medicines in the capital, refining cinnabar into the Ninefold Radiance Elixir before ascending as an immortal.

It further says: Yu Wengsheng, a native of Kuaiji, received the method of consuming solar essence from the Immortal Jie Jun. During the Wu dynasty, he retreated to Mount Langwu, practicing the arts of cloud *qi* and bodily transformation. Through prolonged refinement, he ascended as an immortal.

It further says: Zhu Ruzi entered Mount Chishui during the late Wu, consuming chrysanthemum blossoms and wood. Later, he met the Master of Western Return, who granted him the essential teachings for transcending the world, and he ascended as an immortal.

It further says: The Jade Maiden of Bright Star resided on Mount Hua, consuming Jade Nectar. Atop the mountain stood a stone tortoise spanning several *mu*, its height exceeding three *ren*. Beside it lay a staircase ascending to the tortoise’s back, where a shrine to the Jade Maiden stood. Before it were five stones, known as the Jade Maiden’s Hair-Washing Basin. The water within was jade-green and limpid, neither swelling with rain nor diminishing in drought. A jade horse stood within.

It further says: In the mountains of Mount Hua, Daoist practitioners Yin Shouzi, Zhang Shisheng, and Li Fanghui—all contemporaries of Emperor Wu of Jin—received the method of steaming elixirs and ingesting wood from the Immortal Guan Chengzi. They also transmitted the method of consuming rosy clouds to Su Men and Zhou Shouling.

It further says: Fan Youchong, a native of Liaoxi, constantly practiced the Three *Qi* Method, where blue, white, and red *qi* each resembled threads. After a decade of practice, he attained immortality. This is the Supreme Primordial Inner Radiance Method of High Origin Lord, performed daily at dawn, with visible benefits. The method is simple, its effects verified.

It further says: Jiang Bozhen, on Mount Daheng, consumed *shinao* (stone brain). *Shinao* resembles small, speckled stones, soft in texture. On the eastern side of Mount Great Mao, a similar substance exists, round and small like *zengqing* (azurite), yet resembling stalactites in color. Fan Yangzi once consumed this as well.

*The Inner Transmission of Master Pei* states: The Buddhist-faced Daoist Zhi Ziyuan received the arts of longevity from Master Pei. It further says: While the pursuit of medicinal substances and meditative visualization both lead to the Dao, their origins differ. Ingesting medicines preserves the body, and when the body is sound, the spirit is at peace. Meditative visualization stabilizes the spirit, and when the spirit is attuned, the body is preserved. These two principles complement one another.

*The Biographies of Daoist Scholars* states: Xu Mai, styled Shu Xuan, originally named Ying and later renamed Yuanyou, shared a transcendent friendship with Wang Xizhi and his sons. Xizhi also renounced worldly honors to cultivate longevity, often visiting Yuanyou and staying for days without returning. Their poetic exchanges frequently discussed the ingestion of medicines.

It further says: Huang Guanzi, the Left Minister of the Upper Clarity, studied the Dao, consumed the Golden Elixir, and attained the Way through reciting the *Great Cavern Scripture*. Bai Yusheng, the Left Minister of the Eastern Bureau, possessed a method for boiling stones. Zhang Shuyin, the Stone Immortal Overseer of Literary Virtue, received the Azure Essence formula. Li Baozu, the Right Duke of Grand Clarity from Mount Min, received the Azure Essence refinement method.

Ge Hong’s *Biographies of Divine Transcendents* states: Liu Jing received the Cloud Pellet formula from Zhang Jun of Handan. It further says: Feng Junda, a native of Longxi, entered Mount Wushu to ingest medicines. At over a hundred years of age, he often rode a green ox. It further says: Wei Shuqing, a native of Zhongshan, consumed mica. It further says: Kong Yuan, a native of Xuchang, regularly consumed pine resin and *fuling* (poria). It further says: Jiao Xian, styled Xiaoran, a native of Hedong, often ate white stones, sharing them with others after cooking them like taro. It further says: Ling Shouguang, a native of Fufeng, obtained the Pill of Unending Elixir at over seventy years of age. After consuming it, he lived for over two hundred years without aging. It further says: Fan Miao, the Upper Immortal of the Central Office, styled Dushi and formerly named Bing, attained the Way through consuming the Rainbow Radiance Elixir and authored *The Biography of Lady Wei*. It further says: The Perfected Man of Pure Emptiness, Wang Bao, styled Zideng, was a seventh-generation descendant of Wang Ling, the Marquis of Anguo during the Former Han. The Lord of the Dao of Immortals bestowed upon him two *dou* of Cloud Azure Sunrise Elixir and Morning-Flown Elixir Fat. After consuming them, his vision extended far, and he could vanish while seated or standing, commanding a host of spirits.

**Daoist Canon, Scroll Eleven Concluded**
**Daoist Canon, Scroll Twelve**

**On the Consumption of Elixirs and Nourishment**

The *True Records* states: On the night of the fifteenth day of the seventh month, the Perfected Man of Pure Emptiness spoke to Xu Yufu, saying: "The fat of the Five Lords’ Stone suits your constitution—you should hasten to consume it. It will preserve your youthful countenance, and the Wood Powder will dispel illness. These are what you ought to take." Next, consume [missing text] along with grains, and do not deviate from this. It further says: Those who master the *Great Cavern* become Immortal Ministers; those who consume the Golden Elixir become Grand Masters; those who consume the various mushrooms become Imperial Censors. If one obtains and consumes the Hidden Mushroom of the Supreme Ultimate, one becomes the Left Immortal Duke.

It further says: When one’s nature nears the Dao, true efficacy naturally arises. The Perfected Man of Purple Yang said: "Let Xu Yufu bathe frequently to cleanse the qi of water-borne illness and dissolve the accumulated blemishes of past hardships. This is the path to attaining perfection." In the study of the Dao of nourishing life, one must not weep excessively, for tears and spittle cause great harm. Thus, perfected ones and Daoist adepts constantly practice exhalation, inhalation, and the swallowing of essences to harmonize the six fluids.

It further says: Long ago, Emperor Cheng of Han was hunting in the Zhongnan Mountains when he saw a person without clothing, their body covered in hair, leaping and flying beyond reach. After encircling and capturing them, he asked who they were and learned they were a palace attendant from Qin. They recounted how, during the reign of Qin King Ziying, they had attended a court audience for the Dao. When the palace was burned, they fled in terror into the mountains, starving and on the verge of death. An old man instructed them to eat pine needles and pine nuts. The hunters later took them back and fed them grains, but they vomited for days before recovering. Over a year later, they died. Had they not been captured by humans, they would have become immortals.

It further says: Long Shu, styled Bogao, was a native of Jingzhao. During the Later Han, he studied the method of Embryonic Qi with the immortal Dao Lin and also received the [missing text] formula. He concealed himself in a drunken stupor and vanished into seclusion.

It further says: The Daoist Dai Meng of Mount Wudang, originally surnamed Yan and named Ji, styled Zhongwei, lived during the reign of Emperor Ming of Han. From youth, he cultivated the Dao and virtue, refusing office. He entered Mount Hua, consuming mushrooms, Solomon’s seal, mica, and cinnabar, and received the Way of longevity from the Perfected Man of Pure Numinosity, Lord Wang. The Perfected Man Pei further bestowed upon him the *Scripture of Jade Pendants and Golden Earrings*, along with the *Stone Essence and Golden Light Talisman*.

It further says: Consuming herbal medicines without practicing qi-circulation and guiding-and-pulling exercises is of no benefit—one will never attain the Dao. If one’s will is sincere and resonates with the numinous, success is inevitable, and one need not rely on the benefits of herbs. Yet if one only knows qi-circulation without mastering the method of the Divine Elixir, one will not become an immortal. If one obtains the Golden Liquid Divine Elixir, no other techniques are necessary. If one masters the *True Scripture of the Great Cavern*, one need not attain the Way of the Golden Elixir to become an immortal. Every person is born with a destiny recorded in the celestial registers, and if their will is steadfast, the Dao will make it so. Thus, some achieve immortality without study, for the Dao comes to them of its own accord. Beyond this, all require unwavering resolve.

It further says: The Jade Consort of the Eastern Sea, younger sister of the Azure Lad, descended to teach Zhang Weizi the method of consuming mist.

It further says: When one inhales the qi of cypress, the three impurities of the intestines and stomach are purged. The *Scripture of the Three and Five in Harmonious Flow* states: The Perfected Man of Broad Peace, bearing a halo of radiant light and holding a flowered banner, stood before the Supreme Emperor and inquired about the methods of refinement.

It further says: Within the Terrace of the Five Peaks on Great Mount Huo in Luojiang, there grows a five-colored Hidden Mushroom. On Mount Huayang, there are five kinds of Night-Glowing Mushrooms. On Mount Liangchang, there is a Firefly Mushroom, its form resembling grass, its body on the ground like a firefly, as large as a bean, with purple blossoms. When viewed at night, it emits light. Those who consume it gain clarity of mind and can read and calculate by night. Consuming forty-seven of them grants longevity.

It further says: Within Mount Bao, there is a White Mushroom and a Hidden Spring of purple hue. On Mount Huayang’s Leiping Peak, there is the Field Lord’s Spring, its flowing jade sands ideal for washing clothes.

It further says: Those who consume the Ninefold Numinous Essences of the Sun and Moon obtain the method of the Supreme Ultimate’s Dark Perfection.

It further says: Lang Zong, styled Zhongsui, was a native of Anqiu in Beihai. In his youth, he pursued an official career, and during the Later Han, he served as Magistrate of Wu. He diligently studied the protective arts of the Dao and divined the movements of wind and qi. One day, a sudden whirlwind arose in his courtyard. He divined that a great fire would burn the Longxia Gate in Luoyang. He sent someone to verify this, and it proved true. When the imperial court heard of this, they summoned him as an Academician.

Lang Zong felt ashamed to be summoned for his divination skills, so one night he removed his official seal and sash, shouldered his books, and fled into seclusion. He dwelt beneath Mount Hua, consumed sesame seeds, attained the Dao, and now resides within the mountain’s grotto.

It further says: Fu Lihe was the grandson of Emperor Huan of Han through his daughter, named Fu Jian’an. He regularly ingested the qi of the Five Stars, attained the Dao, and became the Master of the Hall of Embracing Reality.

*The Master Who Embraces Simplicity* states: My grandfather, the Grand Herald, once served as Magistrate of Lin’kang. He remarked that in this county there was a family whose members all enjoyed long lives. Later, when they moved away, their descendants increasingly suffered early deaths. Others who took residence in their former home again lived long lives for generations. Suspecting the well water was unusually red, they dug around the well and unearthed several *hu* of cinnabar buried by ancients—how much more so for those who consume cinnabar!

It further says: Zhao Qu of Shangdang had suffered from leprosy for years, and despite numerous treatments, he did not recover. Nearing death, his family loaded him onto a cart and abandoned him in a mountain valley. Zhao lamented his misfortune, weeping day and night, his tears flowing for months. A transcendent passed by the cave’s entrance, saw him, and took pity. After inquiring about his plight, Zhao, recognizing him as an extraordinary being, kowtowed and pleaded for mercy. The transcendent then gave him a pouch of medicine and instructed him on its consumption. After taking it, Zhao’s illness was cured, his complexion became radiant, and his skin smooth as jade. The transcendent visited him again. Zhao expressed his gratitude and begged for the formula. The transcendent replied, “It is merely pine resin. This mountain has an abundance—refine it, and you may attain longevity.” Zhao returned home, where his family was astonished. When asked how he recovered, he lived to one hundred seventy, his teeth and hair robust, remaining among people for over a hundred years before entering Mount Baodu.

It further says: As for longevity and the choice between staying or departing, each follows their own inclination. After consuming the Reverted Elixir or Golden Liquid, if one wishes to remain in the world, they need only take half. If seeking transcendence, they must consume it entirely. In ancient times, Master Anqi, Lord Longmei, Lord Xiuyang, and Yin Changsheng all took half a dose of the Golden Elixir. They remained in the world for nearly a thousand years before departing.

It further says: According to the middle chapter of *The Jade Key Classic*, establishing merit is paramount, followed by eliminating transgressions. For Dao practitioners, rescuing those in peril is the highest merit. Those who seek transcendence must base their practice on loyalty, filial piety, harmony, benevolence, and trust. Without cultivating virtue and focusing solely on techniques, one will never attain longevity. Major evil deeds forfeit one’s allotted lifespan, while minor transgressions reduce one’s years. Even if one consumes transcendent medicines, without sufficient accumulated goodness, it will be of no benefit.

I have perused texts on nurturing life, and none fail to regard the Reverted Elixir and Golden Liquid as the essentials—indeed, the pinnacle of the Dao of transcendence. In the past, Zuo Ci, styled Yuanfang, meditated intently for a long time in Mount Tianzhu, where a divine being bestowed upon him the *Scripture of the Golden Elixir of Transcendence*. Amid the great chaos at the end of the Han, he had no time to refine it and fled to the lands east of the Yangtze, intending to seek a renowned mountain to cultivate this Dao and follow his ancestral transcendent master. He received from Yuanfang the *Three Scrolls of the Supreme Clarity Elixir Scripture*, the *One Scroll of the Nine Cauldrons Elixir Scripture*, and the *One Scroll of the Golden Liquid Scripture*. My teacher, Master Zheng, was a disciple of the transcendent master. He also received these from my ancestor, but being poor and unable to afford the ingredients, I personally served him. After years of sweeping and attending to him, he established an altar on Mount Maji and transmitted the oral instructions not recorded in the texts. These scriptures were previously unknown in the Jiangdong region; they originated with Zuo Ci. Ci transmitted them to my ancestral transcendent master, who passed them to Master Zheng, who then bestowed them upon me. Thus, no other Daoists possess this knowledge.

This method relies on external substances to strengthen oneself. There is also the *Divine Elixir of Supreme Clarity*, whose method derives from the Primordial Lord. The Primordial Lord was the teacher of Laozi. The *Heavenly Scripture of Supreme Clarity* comprises ten chapters. The upper seven cannot be taught; the lower three, though transmitted in the world, are unworthy of dissemination and should be buried in the Three Springs. The lower three chapters are precisely the *Elixir Scripture*. It states: The superior person who attains the Dao ascends as an official of heaven; the middling person dwells on Kunlun; the inferior person attains longevity in the world.

Toward the end of the Later Han, Yin Jun of Xinye refined this *Divine Elixir of Supreme Clarity*. Gifted with literary talent, he composed poems, eulogies, and prefaces for the elixir scriptures, recounting his early studies under his teacher and what he had learned. The Radiant Elixir differs in method from the Ninefold Cyclically Transformed Elixir, and there is also the method of the Min Mountains Elixir. The Daoist Zhang He meditated intently in a stone chamber on Mount Min and obtained this formula. Each elixir method is distinct. The Golden Liquid is what the Great One consumes to attain transcendence.

It further says: Longevity is determined by the great medicine, not by sacrifices and invocations. During the Qin and Han dynasties, grand supplications were made, offerings presented to the Great One, the Five Emperors, Chenbao, the Eight Spirits, and the like, expending billions without benefit. How much more deluded are those of little virtue who vainly pray for extended years with the three sacrificial animals!

It further says: When compounding the great medicine of the Golden Elixir and refining the essence of the eight minerals, one must especially avoid the gaze of the vulgar, or the transcendent substance will not form. Some say: The superior person attains the Dao amidst military camps, the middling person in bustling cities, and the inferior person in mountain forests. This refers to those who have already refined the transcendent medicine but do not yet wish to ascend lightly. Even amidst armies and blades, they remain unharmed; in cities, misfortunes cannot befall them. The inferior person, not yet having reached this stage, must enter the mountains.

In ancient times, Daoists who refined transcendent medicines invariably entered renowned mountains. According to the *Scripture on Entering Mountains*, one may meditate and refine elixirs in the following: Mounts Taihua, Heng, Song, Shaoshi, Taibai, Zhongnan, Nüfan, Difei, Wangwu, Baodu, Anqiu, Hengqian, Qingcheng, Emei, Leishou Terrace, Luofu, Yangjia, Huangjin, the Greater and Lesser Tiantai, Gaizhu, Kuocang, and Siwang—all abodes of true spirits.

Where these mountains rise, lingzhi mushrooms grow in abundance, serving not only to compound elixirs but also to avert great wars and floods. Should a practitioner of the Dao ascend them, the mountain spirits will surely aid in bestowing fortune, and their elixirs will assuredly succeed. Those who do not climb these mountains may still compound elixirs upon the great isles of the sea.

It is further said: My master, Master Zheng, was over eighty years of age when his temples first showed streaks of white. Yet after several years, his hair turned black once more. His complexion grew radiant and full, and he could draw a mighty crossbow. He walked hundreds of *li* in a day, drank two *dou* of wine without becoming drunk, and when climbing mountains, his body felt light and agile—young men could not keep pace. His diet differed not from that of ordinary people, nor was it ever seen that he abstained from grain. I asked Huang Zhang, a disciple who followed the master, who recounted: Master Zheng was once returning from Yuzhang to the shores of Pu when he encountered a great storm and fell among bandits. He distributed his provisions to the others, taking none for himself, and went fifty days without hunger. Yet no one saw him perform any extraordinary acts—it was unclear by what means he achieved this. By lamplight, he could write in finer script than a youth.

Master Zheng was naturally adept in music and rhythm. On quiet nights, he would play the zither, while several attendants sat beside him. Though his mouth answered their questions without pause, his playing remained resonant, and his ears could still discern the subtlest variations in the strings of those beside him—correcting their errors in length and pitch, leaving not the slightest flaw unnoticed.

In my later years as Master Zheng’s disciple, I requested to see his esoteric writings. He told me: “The essential Dao fits upon a foot of silk—sufficient to transcend the world.” He also said: “What you know is vast but not yet refined, and your mind lingers on externals. Your learning lacks single-minded focus; you are not yet ready to delve deeply or journey far.” He promised that in time, he would show me the finest texts. Over the years, the short scrolls and silk manuscripts I had seen accumulated, and he had compiled nearly two hundred volumes of scriptures—though they could not all be grasped at once.

He further said: “Each new scroll contains fine matters, but you must discern the refined from the coarse and choose what to practice. Once the Golden Elixir is achieved, all these texts will become unnecessary.” At times, he would instruct me in the proper sequence, beginning with the fundamentals to encourage learners, leaving no step unattended. Master Zheng was reluctant to allow others to copy his books in full; one had to grasp their essence. Even when lent for long periods, no one dared to steal so much as a single character.

Master Zheng had originally been a great Confucian scholar. In his later years, he turned to the Dao, yet he continued to teach the *Book of Rites* and the *Book of Documents*, never abandoning his scholarly bearing. His gaze was lofty and forthright, his demeanor upright and dignified; those who met him could not help but feel reverence. Whenever I sought his counsel, he would receive me with a gentle countenance, and I dared not speak lightly.

Among his fifty-odd disciples, only I was entrusted with the *Scripture of the Golden Elixir*, the *Inner Writings of the Three Sovereigns*, and the *Five Phases Record in the Pillow*. The others were not permitted even a glimpse of the opening lines of these texts.

The *Records of the Assembly of Immortals* states: The lush fruit is the bright pearl of spring’s awakening; the giant sesame is the hidden spirit of profound autumn; the cinnabar jujube is the cloud fungus of flourishing yang; the poria is the crimson embryo of the numinous. The Five Flowers hold mist within, the Three Qi refine and harmonize essence, and the Six Qi nourish the po-soul and guard the spirit.

It further says: The Jade Maiden of the Great Mystery was a person of Emperor Shaohao’s time. She dwelt on Mount Changsong in Shu, cultivating the Dao of long life. There, a mountain dweller taught her the *Hidden Writings of the Eight Heavens* and instructed her to practice and wear them, saying: “The essence of cultivating the Dao lies in taking non-action as its foundation. The writings of the Eight Heavens are true non-action, and the Dao will naturally be achieved.” Yet she also refined and ingested the fluid of curved jade and dawn’s light, the elixirs of the Eight Jewels and Nine Flowers—secrets of the Great Ultimate—enabling her to enter the imperial court and witness the myriad transformations. She was granted the *Nine-Flower Formula* and refined the elixir by the river. By the riverbank lies the Golden Sand Spring, her legacy.

It also states: During the reign of Gao Xin, the immortal Zhan Shanggong often recounted that in ancient times, he had eaten white plums in Huayang, their flavor surpassing all others. Though he had not thought of them for long, three thousand years had already passed in an instant.

It further says: Li Tuo dwelt beneath Dragon Bridge Peak on Mount Jintang in Shu, cultivating the Dao. The people of Shu saw him across generations, estimating his comings and goings to span over eight hundred years—hence he was called Li Eight Hundred. Initially, he had come to Guanghan during the reign of King Mu of Zhou, residing on Mount Xuan and compounding the Nine-Flower Elixir to completion. He then traveled to the Five Marchmounts and the Twelve Grottoes, spending over two hundred years by the sea, where the Purple Yang Lord transmitted to him the Dao of Water Jade. Later, he returned to Dragon Bridge Peak, forged a golden tripod, and refined the Nine Elixirs, achieving perfection. As he had studied the Dao thrice upon this mountain, the world named it Three Studies Mountain, also calling it Mount Bingxian.

It further says: The Wen clan of Nanyang recounted that during the great chaos at the end of the Han, their ancestor fled into Mount Hu. Starving and near death, a man taught him to eat wood, and thus he never hungered again.

For a decade he returned to his hometown, his complexion growing ever more youthful. His body light as if about to take flight, he treaded perilous paths without weariness, walking amidst ice and snow yet utterly unaware of the cold.

The wood was also called *shanji* or *shanjing*.

It further says: Xue Nüzhēn, of unknown origin, lived during the upheavals of the Jin dynasty. As people fled to forests and marshes to avoid the world, she took refuge on Mount Heng. Beyond the Terrace of Seeking the Real, wherever she went, yellow birds, white apes, and white leopards followed her—yet none knew what Dao she cultivated.

It further says: Yùjiāng was a woman of hair, known as the Mao Maiden. Dwelling on Mount Hua, she claimed to be of Qin descent. She first learned to eat pine needles, never suffering hunger or cold. She dwelt in the cliffs, her movements swift as flight. The place is now called Mao Maiden Peak.

It further says: Juānzǐ, a man of Qi, consumed wood and composed the *Scripture of the Three Powers*. Prince Liu An of Huainan obtained his writings but could not fathom their meaning. He also authored three scrolls on the *Book of the Qin*, which were highly systematic.

It further says: Zhāng Wēizǐ was the daughter of Zhang Qing, Superintendent of Works during the reign of Emperor Zhao of Han. Fond of the Dao, she often ingested misty qi. She claimed that mist was the essence of mountains, marshes, water, and fire, the overflowing qi of metal and stone. Prolonged ingestion allowed one to disperse form and enter emptiness, merging body with cloudy qi. Wēizǐ said she received this method from Chúnwénqī, the Jade Consort of Eastern Florescence of the Eastern Sea and sister of the Azure Lad. She also taught this mist-ingestion method to her disciples.

The *Nine Perfected and Radiant Consorts* states: The sun is the fruit of rosy clouds; rosy clouds are the essence of the sun. People have heard of methods to ingest the sun’s fruit, yet few know of the essence of rosy clouds. The *Scripture of Rosy Cloud Ingestion* is most arcane, while the Dao of attaining rosy clouds is most simple. This refers to the method of embodying jadelike radiance, where rosy clouds reflect the Upper Clarity.

*Daoist Canon, Section Twelve* concludes.
*Daoist Canon, Section Thirteen* begins.

**On Ingesting Elixirs**

The *Secret Instructions for Ascending to Perfection* states: The Supreme Ultimate Perfected One once transmitted a divine formula to Master Changli. The master, surnamed Xue and styled Changli, lived during the reign of King Wu of Zhou. He passed it to the Overseer of All Perfected Ones of the Western Regions, who was the chief minister of the Golden Portal Sagely Lord. According to [missing text], the *Grain Elixir Formula* was received from the Perfected One of Western Liang, at a time in the northern valley of Dayuan. Now, the ninefold transmutation transmitted by Changli occurred during the early Zhou, marking the reception of the [missing text] grain elixir. Three to four hundred years later, this cinnabar was refined. This is recorded in the preface to the *Sword Scripture of the Controller of Destinies*. The Overseer of All Perfected Ones transmitted it to the Supreme Primordial Perfected One, who was the Controller of Destinies of the Eastern Ministry, Lord Mao the Elder. He received it in the third year of the Tianhan era of Emperor Wu of Han, at the age of forty-eight. Later, he also bestowed it upon his two younger brothers, each receiving a dose of the completed elixir. Though the Controller of Destinies transmitted it to his two brothers, this is not recorded here, as it was by the command of Lord Wangming, not through the proper lineage of transmission. After these two lords, only the Rectifier of Registers and Attendant Yang conveyed it to Director Xu and others, continuing to the present. Thus, during the Han and Jin dynasties, Daoist practitioners who ingested the golden liquid and ascended as immortals across the Six Directions never spoke of the ninefold transmutation. Since this Perfected One’s formula was first transmitted, none have dared to violate the covenant against reckless dissemination. The later generations, bound by the pacts of the Golden Dragon and Jade Fish, have only circulated written copies. Those who break the covenant and betray trust will be examined by the Three Ancestors in the Water Bureau, deemed guilty of recklessly transmitting to the unworthy.

Transmission requires a solemn covenant, using gold and jade rings in place of the oath sworn with cut hair and blood. To refine the ninefold transmutation, one must first craft a divine crucible, using clay crucibles from Yingyang, Changsha, or Yuzhang—these are earthenware crucibles. In ancient times, the Yellow Emperor fired nine tripods at Mount Ke, and the *Central Scripture of Great Clarity* also contains a nine-tripod elixir method. Elixir crucibles have long been called "tripods." They are fired with chaff and should be placed in a secluded spot within a famous mountain, near water, constructing a turtle-shaped hut. The hut should be four *zhang* long and one *zhang* wide, with three doors opening to the south, east, and west. One must first purify oneself for a hundred days, then daub the divine crucible. Once the crucible is complete, the medicine is pounded. The fire is lit at dawn on the ninth day of the ninth month. When compounding various elixirs, the quality of the year is irrelevant; only the auspicious or inauspicious timing within the day or month matters. For the *Langgan* elixir, the fire is lit in the fourth, seventh, or twelfth month; for the *Quchen* elixir, in the fifth month; and for the nine elixirs of Great Clarity, though no fixed month is prescribed, the sixth, first, fifth, seventh, and ninth months are considered best. From the start of the purification, one must sever all worldly affairs until the elixir is complete. Only four or five like-minded and sincere companions may assist in compounding the elixir, all of whom must undergo purification together.

On the day the purification begins, five *hu* of dark wine are poured into the flowing water at the chosen site. If the location lacks flowing water, a well must be dug, and the wine poured into it to stabilize the earth’s *qi*. All participants in the purification must drink and eat from this water. The elixir method further requires placing ten *jin* of fine dragon bone in a green stone vessel, submerged in east-flowing water, called "Azure Dragon Liquid."
